    - **ADR-0032 (Blocker pattern):** registry grows by entry #10 (fix-only).

  - **History pattern: lifecycle capture (unchanged from prior assignment).** Project state transitions are captured per ADR-0013 pattern 2: `active → closed`, `active → cancelled`, `closed → active`, `cancelled → active` each produce a lifecycle-capture record carrying command, actor, timestamp, and payload (`rfp_file` for `close_project`; `rfp_reason` and the new-RFP-id for `reopen_project` from `closed`; no extra payload for the other two). The new-RFP-id on reopen-from-`closed` is captured so the audit trail directly links the project's reopen event to the new RFP Document that derives from it.

  - **Delete policy: soft delete (unchanged).** Project carries lifecycle capture; history references preclude hard delete. The `cancel_project` path is not deletion — it's a terminal transition; the project record persists.

  - **Authorization: any coordinator (MVP).** All three commands (`close_project`, `cancel_project`, `reopen_project`) are authorized to any coordinator. Per-role refinement deferred to Step 6c alongside the concrete role catalog (ADR-0012 + ADR-0036 carry-forward).

  - **Naming.** "RFP" is reused for both the new top-level `document_type` (SCA → us) and CPR's internal payment-request bucket (contractor → us). The acronym overlap is accepted: the two live at different schema levels (document_type vs CPR-internal bucket), and current office vocabulary tolerates the ambiguity without operational confusion. Disambiguation deferred until scale or onboarding pressure forces it.

  - **Carry-forwards.**
    - **Per-role authorization predicates** for `close_project`, `cancel_project`, `reopen_project`: Step 6c.
    - **Post-MVP:** SCA-side RFP-rejection notification (would automate the trigger for `reopen_project` rather than requiring coordinator action); long-tail "what if SCA never responds to a submission" (currently the `saved` RFP just sits indefinitely; a derived stale-RFP signal could surface later but is not a closure blocker for the original submitter).

---

## ADR-0038 — Sample Batch state-machine removal and project-state-driven immutability rule

- **Date:** 2026-05-13
- **Decision:** Sample Batch's `received → billed` state machine is dropped: the entity becomes stateless, joining EmployeeRole, UserRole, DepFiling, and Note as "no state machine." Lifecycle capture (per ADR-0013) is retained, recording `create_sample_batch` and `relink_sample_batch_wa_code` as discrete events without a state field. The deletion is motivated by a clarified reading of `billed`'s original semantics: it was conceived as a closure-snapshot membership marker ("this batch was in a submitted payment package"), not as a billing-system finalization state. Closure-snapshot membership is derived from `Project.state == closed` plus the dismissed-flag pattern at closure moment, not per-entity sticky state. The MVP billing flow is a draft-invoice estimator with no state transitions, so no entity-level state is required. To carry the immutability burden that `billed` was implicitly meant to provide, this ADR formalizes a project-state-driven immutability rule: commands on entities attached to a project in `closed` state are rejected at command guard, except regular Note creation and `reopen_project`. The `cancelled` terminal does not trigger this rule — cancelled work was never billed, and entities on cancelled projects remain available for cleanup or reassignment to active projects. This rule is declared as design pattern #13 (project-state-driven immutability). ADR-0033's `Status` stays `accepted`; this is an amendment, not a supersession.
- **Status:** accepted
- **Context:** ADR-0033 specified a two-state machine for Sample Batch (`received → billed`), with the `received → billed` transition described as "triggered by billing-system finalization (specific command and authorization defined at billing-design time)." Step 6b-residual's original scope (session 9) was to specify that billing-finalization command. Session 9 deliberation reframed the item: there is no separate billing-finalization event in the MVP billing flow. The MVP flow is a draft-invoice estimator that aggregates rates, sample quantities, and WA flat fees on demand, with no state transitions on any entity. `billed` had been conceived in ADR-0033 as marking closure-snapshot membership (which batches were included in a given submitted payment package). Closure-snapshot membership is not sticky per-entity: RFP rejection or withdrawal returns all submitted documents and the next submission is a blank slate (ADR-0037). The structurally correct expression of "this batch was in the submitted package" is `Project.state == closed` at the moment of submission, combined with which dismissable blockers had been dismissed at that point — both derivable from project state and Note history, neither requiring per-entity state. With `billed` gone, Sample Batch loses the implicit immutability that the terminal state was providing (in practice not enforced anywhere, since the transition was never specified). That immutability burden needs to be carried explicitly. Project state already carries the operational signal — work on a `closed` project should not mutate (billed work, snapshot stable) — so the rule is formalized at the Project-state level and applied to every entity whose project membership puts it in a closed-state project. Cancelled projects are exempt from the rule because cancelled work was never billed: entities on cancelled projects remain available for legitimate relink-to-active-projects flows and cleanup.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Retain `billed` as a state, redefined as "this batch was included in the most recent submitted package."* Rejected — non-sticky semantics (reopen-from-`closed` would have to revert `billed → received`, and the revert would be triggered by a project-level event rather than the batch's own lifecycle). Per-entity state driven by another entity's state machine is the wrong factoring. Project state IS the carrier; deriving from it is cleaner than mirroring it.
  - *Retain `billed` as a state, redefined as "billing-system finalization (post-MVP)."* Rejected — adds a state that no MVP command writes and no MVP read consumes. Per Step 6b's discipline (don't speculate state for non-MVP flows), the state is added when the billing-finalization command lands, not before.
  - *Add a per-entity `immutable: bool` flag set by closure cascades.* Rejected — duplicates Project state. The flag and the project's state can drift; the check at every command guard would still need to validate project state to recover. A single source of truth (Project.state) with derived immutability is simpler.
  - *Apply immutability per-entity-type (declare on each entity's ADR which terminal-project states freeze it).* Rejected — every entity attached to a project shares the same operational answer (work on closed projects is frozen). Per-entity declaration would be ceremonial repetition with drift risk.
  - *Apply immutability uniformly across both terminals (`closed` and `cancelled`).* Rejected — cancelled work was never billed and the closure-snapshot intent doesn't apply. Coordinators may legitimately reassign work from cancelled projects to active ones (work incorrectly recorded against a cancelled project; scope amendment on another project rendering this project's work redundant). Enumerating an exception list for cancelled would be brittle; declaring the rule fires only on `closed` is cleaner.
  - *Block ALL commands (including regular Note creation and reopen) on closed projects.* Rejected — `reopen_project` is the structural escape hatch (ADR-0037) and would be blocked, breaking ADR-0037's reopen-from-`closed` cycle. Regular Note creation is commentary/audit, not state mutation; blocking it forecloses the legitimate "discovered later that..." post-hoc audit case. The exception list is load-bearing.
  - *Declare project-state-driven immutability as a one-off ADR-0037 consequence, not a design pattern.* Rejected — the rule's reach is general (every project-scoped entity in the roster) and the mechanism (terminal-state-of-parent gates child commands, with differentiated semantics across terminals) is reusable for any future entity-parent relationship with terminal-state semantics. Pattern menu entry makes the mechanism discoverable for future entity design.
  - *Keep ADR-0033 unamended and add a separate ADR for the immutability rule.* Rejected — the immutability rule is the structural replacement for `billed`'s implicit immutability promise. Bundling keeps the cause-and-replacement together in one document; separating would make the dependency between `billed`'s removal and the rule's introduction harder to trace.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Sample Batch state-machine removed.**
    - No `state` field on Sample Batch. The entity carries its intrinsic attributes (composition, sample type, TAT, location(s), wa_code reference, employee reference, collection time) and is referenced by Documents (COC, Lab Report) and Notes.
    - Lifecycle capture (ADR-0013 pattern 2; per-entity assignment from ADR-0014/ADR-0033) is retained. Captured events: `create_sample_batch` (full attribute payload, including derived COC and Lab Report Document ids) and `relink_sample_batch_wa_code` (old wa_code, new wa_code, actor, timestamp). No other Sample Batch commands produce lifecycle-capture records.
    - Sample Batch moves in the cumulative state-machine grouping from "With state machines" to "Without state machines."
  - **Project-state-driven immutability rule (design pattern #13).**
    - **Rule statement.** A command is rejected at command guard if it targets an entity whose project membership puts it in a project with `state == closed`, unless the command is in the exception list below.
    - **Exceptions (commands permitted on closed-project entities).**
      - **Regular Note creation on the entity.** Rationale: Notes are commentary, not state. Per ADR-0018 they have no history themselves and don't trigger state transitions; post-hoc commentary preserves the closure snapshot rather than mutating it. Blocker and resolution Notes are not in this exception — those are tied to dismissal flows, which are blocked on closed projects (no new dismissable conditions can fire post-closure since the closure gate already resolved them).
      - **`reopen_project` on the project itself.** Rationale: this command IS the structural escape hatch from `closed`.
    - **Cancelled projects do not trigger this rule.** Operations on entities in cancelled projects proceed per each command's own guards. Rationale: cancelled work was never billed, so the closure-snapshot intent doesn't apply. Coordinators may legitimately relink work to active projects, dismiss now-moot blockers as cleanup, edit attributes, or write Notes. `cancel_project` and `close_project` still reject re-firing per their own guards.
    - **Project membership.** Every project-scoped entity carries an answer to "what project am I in?" — computable from its references (direct or transitive). The rule treats this as a predicate, not a storage commitment; physical-shape decisions (denormalized `project_id` vs. traversal vs. materialized view) are Step 8's concern. The entity-roster split:
      - **Project-scoped (subject to the rule):** Project, WA, WA Code, RFA, DepFiling, Time Entry, Sample Batch, Deliverable, Document (via owning entity), Note (when attached to any project-scoped entity).
      - **Not project-scoped (not subject to the rule):** Employee, User, EmployeeRole, UserRole, School, Contractor.
    - **Cross-scope references don't propagate.** When a project-scoped entity references a non-project-scoped entity (e.g., Time Entry → EmployeeRole, Sample Batch → Employee, WA → School), the rule freezes the project-scoped side only. The non-project-scoped target remains mutable for its own purposes.
    - **Failure mode.** A rejected command surfaces a structured rejection ("project P is in state `closed`; this command is not permitted on entities of a closed project"). Resolution path is `reopen_project` followed by retry.
    - **Pattern menu entry (#13).** *Project-state-driven immutability.* When a parent entity has multiple terminal states, those states can carry differentiated downstream semantics: some freeze child entities (immutability), others do not. Project's `closed` is the freezing terminal (billed-work snapshot); `cancelled` is the non-freezing terminal (abandoned work available for cleanup or reassignment). Exception list typically includes commentary-only paths (regular Note creation) and the parent-reopen escape hatch. Implementation: derive the parent's state at guard time; reject non-exempt commands when the parent is in a freezing terminal.
  - **Amendments to other ADRs.**
    - **ADR-0033 (Sample Batch).** State machine section amended: drop `received` and `billed` states; drop the `received → billed` transition; drop the "triggered by billing-system finalization" carry-forward. Lifecycle-capture covered events restated as `create_sample_batch` and `relink_sample_batch_wa_code`. ADR-0033's history pattern (lifecycle capture), delete policy (soft delete), Lab Report `document_type` shape, derivation-source roster entry, relink command shape, chain-dismissal rule, and smart-inference hint are all unchanged. Status stays `accepted`.
    - **ADR-0037 (Project lifecycle).** No structural amendment. This ADR references ADR-0037's `closed` and `cancelled` terminals and its `reopen_project` command; ADR-0037's lifecycle mechanics are unchanged.
    - **ADR-0032 (Blocker pattern).** No structural amendment. Blocker and resolution Notes are not in this ADR's exception list (consistent with no-new-dismissals-on-closed); regular Note creation is exempted separately.
    - **Per-entity history-pattern and delete-policy assignments unchanged.** Sample Batch retains lifecycle capture and soft delete.
  - **Cumulative-table updates in `handoff.md` (applied at session wrap-up).**
    - Entity roster row for Sample Batch: drop "States: `received` / `billed` (ADR-0033)" from the Notes column.
    - State-machine grouping: Sample Batch moves from "With state machines" to "Without state machines" (joining EmployeeRole, UserRole, DepFiling, School, Note, User, Employee, Contractor).
    - Design-patterns list: append pattern #13 (Project-state-driven immutability) with one-line description.
    - Vocabulary: no new terms required.
  - **Carry-forwards.**
    - **Closure-snapshot construction (post-MVP, billing-design step).** When the MVP draft-invoice estimator is replaced by a real billing-system finalization, the closure-snapshot semantic ("which batches were in the submitted package") becomes a derived query over `Project.state == closed` plus dismissed-blocker history at the closure moment. No new state field required.
    - **Project-scoped flat-storage (Step 8 implementation).** The expected implementation pattern is to denormalize the project reference onto every project-scoped entity (`project_id` column or equivalent), making both the immutability-guard check and flat read-side queries ("all batches in project P," "all NOB PLM samples across all projects") trivial. The domain model commits only to the predicate; the storage choice lands in Step 8.
    - **Audit-log filtering on terminal-state projects (UX, not domain).** Whether read-side UI hides or visually-distinguishes entities on closed projects is a UI concern. The immutability rule applies only to writes.

---

## ADR-0039 — `change_employee_role_rate` compound command, primitive-guard relaxation, and Time-Entry-out-of-role-range blocker

- **Date:** 2026-05-13
- **Decision:** Defines `change_employee_role_rate(employee, role_type, new_rate, effective_date, new_end_date=NULL)` as a compound command. Target state: `(employee, role_type)` has a row covering `[effective_date, new_end_date or NULL]` at `new_rate`. Algorithm dispatches by existing structure to one of four branches: create (no covering row, no adjacent same-rate), merge-adjacent (no covering row, adjacent same-rate at `effective_date - 1`), close+create+auto-reparent (covering row, different rate, `R.start_date < effective_date`), or edit-in-place (covering row, same rate OR `R.start_date == effective_date`). Auto-reparent atomically re-points Time Entries on the existing row whose dates fall within the new row's coverage. Amends ADR-0035: `close_employee_role` and `edit_employee_role` no-orphan-future-Time-Entries guards removed; Time Entry boundary invariant enforced on Time Entry write-time only. Amends ADR-0032 registry: adds dismissable blocker "Time Entry references EmployeeRole with `time_entry.date` outside `[start_date, end_date]`"; dismissal chain-nulls `wa_code` on Sample Batches collected during the Time Entry's coverage (second concrete instance of ADR-0033 pattern #12). History: each underlying EmployeeRole and Time Entry write emits its native-pattern event; compound-marker event on EmployeeRole tags the invocation. Resolves ADR-0035 carry-forward.
- **Status:** accepted
- **Context:** ADR-0035 established EmployeeRole's temporal shape and rate-resolution mechanics, including a strict no-orphan-future-Time-Entries guard on `close_employee_role` (and by extension, `edit_employee_role` when shortening). The compound `change_employee_role_rate` was named as a carry-forward, with the close+create primitive sequence sketched but the compound's spec deferred to workflow consolidation. Step 6b-residual session 10 deliberation surfaced that the strict reject model breaks reasonable operational paths: (a) rate changes effective in the past, where existing Time Entries reference the role on dates the new rate should apply — the close step rejects because shortening the row would orphan those entries, but the right behavior is to atomically re-point them to the new row; (b) license-expiration corrections where the coordinator discovers retroactively that work was performed after the role's actual end — the right behavior is to permit the shortening, leave the affected Time Entries pointing at a now-out-of-range role, and surface the resulting state as a dismissable blocker so the coordinator can resolve (re-point, edit date, extend role, delete entry, or dismiss as unbillable). Both paths require relaxing ADR-0035's primitive guards and introducing a registry entry for the resulting state. The compound's auto-reparent step handles (a) automatically when the new row covers the affected entries; otherwise the relaxed primitives + blocker mechanism handles (b). The chain-dismissal pattern (ADR-0033 pattern #12) provides the propagation mechanism for Sample Batches collected during a dismissed Time Entry's coverage.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Keep ADR-0035's strict no-orphan-future-Time-Entries guard.* Rejected — rejects two real operational paths (retroactive rate change with intervening Time Entries; license-expiration discovery after work performed). The relaxation cost is one registry entry and a chain linkage; the friction cost of strict reject is multi-step workarounds.
  - *Auto-reparent in the compound but keep primitives strict.* Rejected — handles rate change but not license-expiration. Splits the operational model along an internal/external command boundary with no domain meaning.
  - *Classify the new blocker as fix-only.* Rejected — work was performed; the dismiss-as-unbillable acceptance path is real. Fix-only would foreclose it.
  - *Introduce a separate Sample-Batch-collected-under-unbillable-Time-Entry blocker.* Rejected — redundant with the existing sample-batch-orphan (wa_code=null) blocker once the chain nulls wa_code. The "orphan by collector" vs "orphan by wa_code" distinction is recoverable from chain-dismissal Notes via derivable queries.
  - *Time Entry rate snapshot at write time (ADR-0035 carry-forward).* Rejected for MVP — different model layer (rate copied onto Time Entry, decoupled from EmployeeRole row). Solves retroactive-correction at the snapshot layer; requires schema change. Stays as post-MVP option if rate-correction workflows become a frequent pattern.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Compound command.** Signature: `change_employee_role_rate(employee, role_type, new_rate, effective_date, new_end_date=NULL)`. Target state: `(employee, role_type)` has a single row covering `[effective_date, new_end_date or NULL]` at `new_rate`. No contiguous same-rate row pairs produced.
  - **Algorithm.** Resolve R = the row covering `effective_date` for `(employee, role_type)`, if any. Dispatch:
    1. No R, no same-rate row ending at `effective_date - 1` → `create_employee_role(employee, role_type, new_rate, effective_date, new_end_date)`.
    2. No R, same-rate row ends at `effective_date - 1` → `edit_employee_role` on that adjacent row to set `end_date = new_end_date` (merge).
    3. R covers, `R.rate != new_rate`, `R.start_date < effective_date` → atomic: (a) edit R, `end_date = effective_date - 1`; (b) create new row `(new_rate, effective_date, new_end_date)`; (c) re-point Time Entries where `employee_role_id == R.id AND date >= effective_date` to the new row.
    4. R covers, with `R.rate == new_rate` OR `R.start_date == effective_date` → `edit_employee_role(R, rate=new_rate, end_date=new_end_date)`.
  - **Guards.** No compound-specific guards. Each underlying write inherits its existing guards (disjoint-ranges-per-`(employee, role_type)`; Time Entry boundary invariant on Time Entry write-time only per the ADR-0035 amendment below). **Interaction with ADR-0038:** branch 3's auto-reparent writes to Time Entries; if any targeted Time Entry belongs to a closed project, the write is blocked by ADR-0038's immutability rule and the compound rejects atomically. Coordinator resolves by picking a later `effective_date` or reopening the affected project first.
  - **Amendment to ADR-0035.**
    - `close_employee_role` and `edit_employee_role` no longer reject when shortening orphans existing Time Entries.
    - Time Entry boundary invariant (`time_entry.date ∈ [employee_role.start_date, employee_role.end_date ?? +∞]`) scoped to Time Entry write-time only. EmployeeRole writes do not enforce it; resulting orphan states surface via the blocker below.
  - **Amendment to ADR-0032 registry.** New entry: **Time-Entry-out-of-role-range** (dismissable). Predicate: `time_entry.date < employee_role.start_date OR (employee_role.end_date IS NOT NULL AND time_entry.date > employee_role.end_date)`. Held against the Time Entry. Closure-gate impact: standard dismissable. **Interaction with ADR-0038:** EmployeeRole writes are not project-scoped, so this blocker may fire on Time Entries belonging to closed projects (e.g., when a license correction post-closure shortens the role). Such instances stay derived — dismissal is a command, blocked by ADR-0038's immutability rule on closed projects — and become actionable only on `reopen_project`.
  - **Chain-dismissal linkage (new instance of ADR-0033 pattern #12).** Dismissal of Time-Entry-out-of-role-range atomically: (a) writes the dismissal resolution Note on the Time Entry; (b) for each Sample Batch where `batch.employee == time_entry.employee` and `batch.collection_time ∈ time_entry.on_site_range`, sets `batch.wa_code = NULL`; (c) materializes the sample-batch-orphan blocker on each affected batch; (d) writes paired auto-dismissal resolution Notes referencing the upstream Time Entry dismissal.
  - **History capture (two-tier).**
    - Each underlying EmployeeRole write emits its native lifecycle-capture event.
    - Each Time Entry re-point emits a Time Entry audit-log event with `(old_employee_role_id, new_employee_role_id, actor, timestamp, compound_marker_id)`.
    - The compound emits a logical marker event on EmployeeRole's lifecycle-capture stream with full input params, branch fired, and affected row/Time-Entry ids. Underlying events reference the marker via `compound_marker_id`.
  - **Auto-reparent is compound-scoped.** Direct `close_employee_role` and `edit_employee_role` invocations do not auto-reparent. Coordinator re-points manually via `edit_time_entry` (or accepts the resulting blocker state).

---

## ADR-0040 — Role catalog (superadmin/admin/coordinator/auditor), linear hierarchy with conservative grant authority, Note polymorphism extension to history records, and `tracker` → `coordinator` rename

- **Date:** 2026-05-13
- **Decision:** Concrete role catalog under ADR-0036's UserRole substrate is four roles: `superadmin`, `admin`, `coordinator`, `auditor`. The roles form a linear hierarchy — each higher role's permission set is a superset of the next lower's — but this is an **emergent semantic property** of the permission table, not a structural rule. Permissions are authored as explicit `(role, command) → permitted?` rows so the hierarchy can be "frozen" when a non-chain role is introduced later. Conservative grant authority: `superadmin` grants any role; `admin` grants `coordinator` and `auditor` only (cannot mint admins or superadmins); `coordinator` and `auditor` grant nothing. Superadmin's MVP-distinct operational surface is precisely "can grant `admin` or `superadmin`" — the role catalog itself is hardcoded (no runtime role-CRUD), so no other escape-hatch operations differentiate the two in MVP. The deferred `reason`-field shape on grant/revoke audit events (ADR-0036 carry-forward) is resolved by extending Note's polymorphism (amends ADR-0018): the audit-log event carries no reason field; the command surface accepts an optional `reason_text` parameter which, if non-empty, materializes an immutable Note (new subtype `audit_reason`) attached to the resulting history row. Note's polymorphic target is broadened in capability (Note can now reference history records in addition to entities) but in MVP usage is exercised only by `grant_user_role` and `revoke_user_role`; the broader pattern is available for future event-anchored commentary without re-amendment. Term `tracker` is renamed to `coordinator` throughout planning files and prior ADR text; the existing vocabulary entry "Coordinator — office staff who manage work" is dropped (it was a placeholder for "non-app-users," and `coordinator` as a role consumes that slot by defining those people as app users).
- **Status:** accepted
- **Context:** ADR-0036 established UserRole as the app-access substrate and carry-forwarded the concrete role catalog and `reason`-field shape to Step 6c. Step 6c-i picks them up. The user's framing: implementation is laid out like a WordPress site — split between a user-facing site (the project-tracking dashboard) and an admin dashboard. The split is driven less by specific authority partitioning and more by the operational reality that many coordinators are not technically able; the project-tracking dashboard is the most intuitive, foolproof surface, while the admin dashboard is granted to users trusted to administrate the system more generally. The auditor role accommodates users who shouldn't have any editing capability — read-only views with simple filters. Superadmin is the user-developer's escape hatch. Linear hierarchy was chosen for MVP simplicity but explicitly designed to be freeze-able so a future non-chain role (e.g., a "rate-only admin" with admin's rate-setting authority but not user-grant authority) appends a column without refactoring existing rows. The `tracker` → `coordinator` rename addresses vocabulary debt: the app is itself called sca-**tracker** (and ADR-0007 etc. use "tracking" semantics), so `tracker` as the user-role name was a collision; `coordinator` is the role token, "project manager" remains the job title.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Two-role catalog (admin/coordinator only).* Rejected — leaves no room for a read-only role and conflates the user-developer's privileged operations with the standard admin role.
  - *Permissive grant authority (admin grants admin).* Rejected — small firm, MVP usage is bounded; conservative preserves a clean trust boundary at the admin/superadmin line. Loosening to permissive later is a one-row amendment; tightening permissive → conservative later requires revoking unintended admins. Asymmetric reversibility favors starting tight.
  - *Structural hierarchy with inheritance derived in code (admin = coordinator + extras).* Rejected — convenient but loses the "freeze" property. A non-chain role added later would require refactoring the inheritance chain. Explicit per-`(role, command)` rows preserve the freedom to break out of the hierarchy.
  - *Reason field as free-text on event payload.* Rejected — creates a second narrative-anchor channel alongside Note, breaks symmetry with other commands that don't carry `reason?` payloads, and contradicts precedent set by ADR-0032/0033 (blocker dismissal Note) and ADR-0037 (reopen-from-`cancelled` relies on Note).
  - *Reason as regular Note on the User entity (Note-as-narrative principle preserved without extending polymorphism).* Rejected — weak structural link from Note to specific grant event. Coordinators reviewing the audit log would have only temporal-proximity heuristic to tie a Note to a specific event among many.
  - *Reason as enum, or enum + free-text.* Rejected — MVP has no signal yet about which reason categories actually matter for queries. Premature enumeration risks over-specifying (wrong categories) or under-specifying (escape-hatch "other" defeats the enum). Free-text now; promote to enum convention later if a query pattern emerges.
  - *Keep `tracker` as the role name.* Rejected — collision with the app's name and "tracking" semantics in ADR-0007. The vocabulary debt was real; the rename lands at Step 6c rather than compounding through implementation.
  - *Keep the existing "Coordinator" vocabulary entry (office staff, not an app user).* Rejected — the entry was a placeholder for "people in the org but not in the app yet." Defining `coordinator` as the role for those people consumes the placeholder.
  - *Mutable `audit_reason` Notes (reuse `regular` subtype).* Rejected — audit-adjacent narrative wants immutability. If a coordinator can later edit the stated reason for a revoke, audit forensics is weak. New immutable subtype is the cleaner separation, following precedent of `blocker` and `resolution` being immutable per ADR-0032.

- **Consequences:**

  - **Role catalog.**
    | Role | Description |
    |---|---|
    | `superadmin` | System-level; user-developer's role. Operationally distinct from `admin` only by grant authority (can grant `admin` or `superadmin`). No other privileged operations in MVP — role catalog is hardcoded, no runtime role-CRUD. |
    | `admin` | Admin-dashboard access. Manages static rosters (Employee, EmployeeRole, School, Contractor, User, UserRole grants below own level) and creates Project shells (`create_project`). Cannot mint admins or superadmins. |
    | `coordinator` | Project-tracking-dashboard access. Manages project lifecycle: Time Entries, Sample Batches, Documents, Deliverables, RFAs, DepFilings, Notes (including blocker dismissals), Project lifecycle commands (`close_project`, `cancel_project`, `reopen_project`). Replaces former `tracker` term. |
    | `auditor` | Read-only views with simple filters. No command authority, no editing. Intended for users not trusted with mutation (external accountants, oversight). |

  - **Linear hierarchy is emergent.** Permission table is authored as explicit `(role, command) → permitted?` rows. The hierarchy property — `auditor ⊆ coordinator ⊆ admin ⊆ superadmin` for permitted commands — is maintained by how rows are filled, not by structural inheritance. **Propagation default:** any permission added to a lower role in the chain also propagates to all higher roles unless explicitly signaled otherwise. The `auditor` row is read-only by definition; adding a write command to `auditor` is itself a chain-break signal and should be questioned before being applied.

  - **Grant authority (conservative).**
    | Granting role | Can grant |
    |---|---|
    | `superadmin` | any role |
    | `admin` | `coordinator`, `auditor` |
    | `coordinator` | nothing |
    | `auditor` | nothing |

    Revoke authority mirrors grant: a role that can grant role X can revoke role X. The `grant_user_role` / `revoke_user_role` authorization predicates read the actor's roles against the target role per the table above.

  - **Multi-role grants.** ADR-0036's UserRole composite-key shape permits a user to hold multiple roles. A user's effective permission set is the **union** of all granted roles. In the linear-hierarchy MVP, granting the highest role suffices (lower-role sets are subsets); granting both `admin` and `coordinator` to the same user is redundant but harmless. The union semantics continue to work unchanged when a non-chain role is introduced.

  - **`reason` carry-forward resolved (ADR-0036).** Command signatures:
    - `grant_user_role(user, role_type, reason_text?: string)` — creates UserRole row; appends `grant_user_role` event to User's audit log; if `reason_text` non-empty, materializes an `audit_reason` Note attached to that history row.
    - `revoke_user_role(user, role_type, reason_text?: string)` — hard-deletes UserRole row; appends `revoke_user_role` event; same Note materialization conditional on `reason_text`.

    `reason_text` is a command parameter only — it is **not** stored on the audit-log event payload itself. The Note carries the actual text. Audit-log UI surfacing reasons inline is a join over Note where `target_type = 'history_record' AND target_id = event.id AND subtype = 'audit_reason'` — at most one such Note per history row by construction.

  - **Note polymorphism amendment (amends ADR-0018).** Note's polymorphic target is extended from "any entity" to "any entity *or any history record*." The `audit_reason` subtype is added to the existing `regular | blocker | resolution` subtype set:
    | Subtype | Mutability | Authoring | Attachment target |
    |---|---|---|---|
    | `regular` | Creator-editable per ADR-0018 | User | Entity |
    | `blocker` | Immutable per ADR-0032 | System or user | Entity |
    | `resolution` | Immutable per ADR-0032 | System or user | Entity (`references` field links to dismissal Note) |
    | `audit_reason` | Immutable | User (command actor) | History record |

    `audit_reason` is immutable to preserve audit forensics: once written, the reason for a grant or revoke cannot be later rewritten. `authorship_class = 'user'`; `created_by` mirrors the audit event's actor (same person by construction). Note's existing not-deletable rule (per ADR-0018) carries through.

  - **Polymorphic-target scope.** Note → history record is broadly available across the system in capability. MVP only exercises it for `grant_user_role` and `revoke_user_role` history rows. Other commands that want event-anchored reasons (e.g., a future `dismiss_wa_code(reason_text?)`) can adopt the same `audit_reason`-attached-to-history-row pattern without re-amending ADR-0018.

  - **Cascade and deletion.** Notes are not deletable per ADR-0018. History records are not deletable (they are history). The `audit_reason` attachment is stable for the lifetime of the history record.

  - **`tracker` → `coordinator` rename — planning-file cascade (applied this session).** Mechanical vocabulary substitution. Sites touched:
    - `handoff.md` vocabulary (the former "Tracker" entry renamed to "Coordinator"; the former placeholder "Coordinator — office staff who manage work" entry consumed into the new role definition).
    - Every ADR with "any tracker" / "tracker authorization" / "tracker-side" language across ADR-0027 through ADR-0037, plus prose mentions in earlier ADRs. No semantic change to prior authorization decisions — all prior "any tracker" predicates collapse to "any coordinator-or-higher" under the new linear hierarchy.
    - `post-mvp.md`, `steps.md` (surgical fixes — `sca-tracker` product name preserved by exclusion).
    - One non-role usage retained: "in a tracking tool" (was "in a tracker tool" at ADR-0037 alternatives) — rephrased to use the verb form rather than rename to "coordinator tool," which would have lost meaning.

  - **Dashboard split is informational, not authorization-structural.** The admin / coordinator / auditor dashboards are a UX shape that falls out of each role's command surface; they are not gated structurally beyond the role's commands. A user holding multiple roles sees all corresponding dashboards.

  - **Project creation placement.** `create_project` is admin-side. Project lifecycle commands (`close_project`, `cancel_project`, `reopen_project`) are coordinator-side. Project is the one entity in the 16-entity roster whose commands genuinely split across dashboards; recorded here so Step 6c-ii's per-command predicate table treats Project as the one entity with role-split commands.

  - **Amendments to other ADRs.**
    - **ADR-0018 (Note polymorphism):** target broadened from "any entity" to "any entity or any history record"; new immutable subtype `audit_reason` added to the `regular | blocker | resolution` set.
    - **ADR-0036 (UserRole carry-forwards):** `reason`-field shape resolved (no field on the event payload; UI surfaces optional `reason_text` parameter that materializes an `audit_reason` Note on the history row when non-empty). Concrete role catalog and grant authority resolved.
    - **ADR-0012 (authorization predicates):** concrete role substrate established; per-command predicate enumeration still carry-forwarded to Step 6c-ii.

  - **Carry-forwards.**
    - **Per-command predicate enumeration:** Step 6c-ii. The role catalog established here is the substrate; per-`(role, command)` cells are filled there.
    - **Cross-project commands** (Time Entry cross-project overlap dismissal, cross-project Sample Batch reassignment if it lands): predicates may need to read both projects' coordinator rosters. Surface in Step 6c-ii.
    - **Post-MVP role expansions** (rate-only admin; per-project coordinator scoping; external SCA-contact role): all break the linear-chain assumption and would trigger the table "freeze." `post-mvp.md` candidates.
    - **Audit-log UI surfacing `audit_reason` Notes inline:** implementation detail, deferred to frontend work.
    - **Security-immediate revoke runtime semantics** (carry-forward from ADR-0036): deferred to auth implementation step; the domain shape supports immediate revoke.

---

## ADR-0041 — Entity-pair relationships: WAAuthorization + ContractorEngagement associative entities, Time Entry restructure, Document single-scope, derivation-chain clarifications

- **Date:** 2026-05-13
- **Decision:** Consolidated declaration of entity-pair relationships across the 16-entity roster, filling structural gaps left implicit by prior ADRs. Eight gap resolutions land in this ADR:
  1. **Time Entry → School:** M:1 mandatory direct typed reference (`site_id`).
  2. **Sample Batch → School:** M:1 mandatory direct typed reference (`site_id`); descriptive plain-text `sampling_locations` field separated from the structural site reference.
  3. **WA ↔ WA Code:** M:N via new associative entity `WAAuthorization(wa_id, wa_code_id)`. Composite-key-only in MVP; gains budget and any other per-(WA, code) state when budget tracking lands.
  4. **RFA → WA:** M:1 mandatory direct typed reference (`amends_wa_id`), set at draft creation, immutable for RFA lifetime. Project derives via WA → Project (one hop).
  5. **User ↔ Employee:** 0..1 ↔ 0..1 via `User.employee_id?` (nullable FK on User side, UNIQUE-constrained). Set at User creation; null for non-Employee Users (superadmin, external auditor).
  6. **Time Entry → Employee restructure:** Time Entry no longer references EmployeeRole via FK; self-describes `employee_id`, `role_type`, `project_id`, `site_id`, `wa_code_id?`, `date`, `on_site_range`, `off_site_sub_intervals`. EmployeeRole becomes a *derived/validated* link looked up at closure-gate evaluation, blocker surfacing, and rate resolution. Amends ADR-0035 (drops Time Entry → EmployeeRole FK, drops the boundary invariant at FK-level), amends ADR-0039 (blocker predicate generalizes; auto-reparent compound branch dissolves entirely under the new schema).
  7. **WA ↔ Contractor M:M** via new associative entity `ContractorEngagement(wa_id, contractor_id, started_at, ended_at?)` carrying stint markers. Multiple rows per (wa_id, contractor_id) when a contractor closes their CPR filing and is re-added. CPR derives per `ContractorEngagement` row. Project ↔ Contractor: derived (no explicit storage) through `ContractorEngagement → WA → Project`.
  8. **Document ↔ Deliverable redesigned:** Documents are **single-scope** (not M:M as the handoff entity row had aspirationally listed). Document carries `(scope_type, scope_id)` discriminator+FK; `scope_type ∈ {project, deliverable, wa_code}`. Deliverable's bundle is a *query* over scoped Documents: derived required docs (system-generated from the Deliverable) + user-added Documents scoped to the Deliverable + user-added Documents scoped to WA Codes that map to this Deliverable. The three-scope distinction is load-bearing because of cascade semantics on WA Code dismissal. Amends ADR-0015 (clarifies derivation chain: WA Code → Deliverable → required Documents; the "WA Code" entry on Document's derivation set is more accurately "Deliverable").

  Entity roster bumps from 16 → 18 (WAAuthorization, ContractorEngagement added). All other gaps consume into existing entities' schemas.

- **Status:** accepted (relationship table amended by ADR-0044 — `WA → Project` becomes derived via the WABundle; new rows `WA → WABundle`, `WABundle → Project`, `WABundle → Contract`)
- **Context:** Step 6c-i required consolidation of entity-pair relationships, since many pair-links were declared in their owning ADRs (Time Entry → EmployeeRole in ADR-0035; Sample Batch → WA Code in ADR-0033; etc.) but several relationships in the 16-entity roster were either implicit, ambiguous, or contradictory between handoff cumulative tables and ADR text.

  The session surfaced 8 gaps. Several resolutions stayed mechanical (Gap 4 site_id; Gap 5 site_id + descriptive split; Gap 2 User.employee_id?). Three required substantive deliberation:

  - **Gap 6 (Time Entry restructure)** emerged from user pushback on the gap-3 framing. The mandatory `Time Entry → EmployeeRole` FK (ADR-0035) blocked two real operational paths: entering a Time Entry before its EmployeeRole row is set up (forces sticky-note workflow), and identifying an orphaned Time Entry's Employee after EmployeeRole termination shortens coverage. Reframe: Time Entry self-describes who/role/project/site; EmployeeRole becomes derived/validated. Cascading amendments to ADR-0035 + ADR-0039.

  - **Gap 7 (Contractor)** revealed a domain misunderstanding on the agent's part: WAs are SCA-issued documents, not records we create. The "multi-contractor edge case" is in fact how the SCA portal models WAs (multiple contractors common; same contractor can leave and return on the same WA). Promotion to associative entity `ContractorEngagement` driven by stint semantics + CPR-per-stint derivation rule from the user's edge case.

  - **Gap 8 (Document ↔ Deliverable)** shifted significantly: user clarification reframed the handoff's "bundles Documents (M:M)" as imprecise. Documents are single-scope; same conceptual doc needed for two Deliverables = two distinct Document records. M:M dissolves; structural shape becomes scope discriminator + FK. The bundle is a query.

  The Document derivation-chain clarification (Gap 8 sub-point) refines ADR-0015: Documents derived from "WA Codes" are actually derived from Deliverables (which derive from WA Codes). The WA Code is upstream of both Deliverable and required Documents; required Documents derive *from the Deliverable*.

  Step 6c-ii (per-command authorization predicates) inherits this ADR's relationship + entity surface as substrate.

- **Alternatives considered:** (per gap, brief)

  - *Gap 4 — derive Time Entry's School from WA Code's school.* Rejected — WA Codes are sometimes school-scoped (sample-collection codes per ADR-0020), often not. Derived path unreliable.
  - *Gap 5 — multi-school Sample Batches (M:N).* Rejected — Sample Batch → WA Code M:1 mandatory (ADR-0033) + sample-collection codes are one-per-(sample_type, school) (ADR-0020) structurally pin to one school via the WA Code chain. Multi-school COCs would require restructuring beyond MVP scope.
  - *Gap 5 — derive site from WA Code rather than direct ref.* Rejected — smart-inference misfiling detection (ADR-0033) requires the recorded collection site to be independent of the wa_code's school, and dismiss-cascade nulling of wa_code would lose location info on direct-derive.
  - *Gap 7 (WA Code ↔ WA) — embedded `authorized_codes` array on WA.* Rejected — budget tracking will force promotion to associative entity per ADR-0004; declaring the right shape now avoids migration. ADR-0004's promotion criterion holds even pre-budget given the deferred carry-forward.
  - *Gap 8 (RFA → Project direct).* Rejected — introduces RFA into the mis-attribution cascade unnecessarily. RFA → WA M:1 (with project derived) keeps cascade footprint at WA + WA Codes only.
  - *Gap 8 (RFA → target WA Codes only; project + WA both derived).* Rejected on a subtle point — RFA can target *new* codes (codes that don't exist until the RFA approves), so target-code-derived WA fails for those. RFA → WA direct is unambiguous.
  - *Gap 2 (Employee.user_id? — FK on Employee side).* Rejected — Employee is HR-driven; user_id would always be null at creation, set later. User.employee_id? aligns the FK with the side that knows the link at row-creation time.
  - *Gap 3/6 (keep Time Entry → EmployeeRole FK).* Rejected per user pushback — blocks real workflow (Time Entry entered before EmployeeRole row) and obscures orphan-recovery identity when EmployeeRole terminations shorten coverage. Trade-off: rate resolution becomes a `(employee, role_type, date)` lookup instead of a one-FK-hop. Negligible perf cost; significant workflow gain.
  - *Gap 7 (Project ↔ Contractor explicit M:M, no stint structure).* Rejected — user's CPR-per-stint edge case requires stint distinguishability. Simple project-level M:M can't distinguish "same contractor served twice" from "same contractor served once." `ContractorEngagement` associative entity captures this.
  - *Gap 7 (WA → Contractor M:1, model multi-contractor case as separate WAs).* Rejected on user correction — WAs are SCA-issued documents; "making a new WA" is structurally invalid. M:M is how the portal models WAs.
  - *Gap 8 (Document ↔ Deliverable M:M with join table + bundling commands).* Rejected — user clarification reframed Documents as single-scope; M:M dissolves. The bundle is a query over scoped Documents.
  - *Gap 8 (explicit bundling via add/remove commands without derivation).* Rejected — required-doc derivation from Deliverable is a real first-class behavior; explicit-only forces coordinators to manually populate every Deliverable from scratch. Derived + explicit-attach overlay is the cleaner shape.
  - *Gap 8 (collapse WA Code scope into Deliverable scope).* Rejected — WA Code scope earns its keep through cascade semantics on `dismiss_wa_code`: Documents tied to a specific code's work should reflect that dependency when the code is dismissed.

- **Consequences:**

  - **Consolidated relationship table** (declared in this ADR or in prior ADRs):

    | From → To | Cardinality | Kind | Source ADR |
    |---|---|---|---|
    | WA → WA (self) | nullable self-ref `supersedes` | typed ref | ADR-0017 |
    | WA → Project | M:1 | typed ref | ADR-0020 (implied) |
    | WA → Contractor | M:N via `ContractorEngagement` | associative entity | **ADR-0041** |
    | WA Code → Project | M:1 | typed ref | ADR-0020 |
    | WA Code → WA | M:N via `WAAuthorization` | associative entity | **ADR-0041** |
    | Time Entry → Employee | M:1 mandatory direct | typed ref | **ADR-0041** (amends ADR-0035) |
    | Time Entry → Project | M:1 mandatory direct | typed ref | **ADR-0041** |
    | Time Entry → School | M:1 mandatory direct (`site_id`) | typed ref | **ADR-0041** |
    | Time Entry → WA Code | M:1 mandatory at create, nullable via dismiss cascade | typed ref | ADR-0020, ADR-0027 |
    | Time Entry → Daily Log (Document) | M:1 nullable (`daily_log`) | typed ref | ADR-0026 |
    | Time Entry ↔ EmployeeRole | derived (lookup by `(employee, role_type, date)`) | derived | **ADR-0041** (amends ADR-0035) |
    | Sample Batch → WA Code | M:1 nullable via dismiss cascade | typed ref | ADR-0033 |
    | Sample Batch → Employee | M:1 direct (collector) | typed ref | ADR-0033 |
    | Sample Batch → School | M:1 mandatory direct (`site_id`) | typed ref | **ADR-0041** |
    | Sample Batch → Project | derived (via WA Code) | derived | (no change) |
    | Sample Batch → Document (COC, Lab Report) | 1:1 derivation each | derivation | ADR-0033 |
    | WA Code → Deliverable | M:1 (codes share Deliverables) | derivation | ADR-0022 |
    | WA Code → Document (via Deliverable) | indirect (clarified) | derivation chain | **ADR-0041** (amends ADR-0015) |
    | Deliverable → Document (required) | 1:N derivation | derivation | **ADR-0041** (clarifies ADR-0015) |
    | DepFiling → Project | M:1 | typed ref | ADR-0023 |
    | DepFiling → Document | 1:N derivation (editable `required_doc_types`) | derivation | ADR-0023 |
    | Project → RFP Document | 1:N derivation (1 non-terminal + unbounded terminal) | derivation | ADR-0037 |
    | Project ↔ Contractor | derived (via `ContractorEngagement` → WA → Project) | derived | **ADR-0041** |
    | EmployeeRole → Employee | M:1 (composite key) | typed ref | ADR-0035 |
    | UserRole → User | M:1 (composite key) | typed ref | ADR-0036 |
    | User → Employee | 0..1 (`employee_id?`, UNIQUE) | typed ref | **ADR-0041** |
    | RFA → WA | M:1 mandatory direct (`amends_wa_id`) | typed ref | **ADR-0041** |
    | RFA → WA Code | M:N (targets) | targets | ADR-0031 |
    | RFA → Project | derived (via WA) | derived | **ADR-0041** |
    | Document → scope | M:1 (`scope_type ∈ {project, deliverable, wa_code}`, `scope_id`) | typed ref + discriminator | **ADR-0041** (reshapes ADR-0014, ADR-0015) |
    | Note → entity OR history record | polymorphic typed ref | per subtype | ADR-0018, ADR-0032, ADR-0040 |
    | Note → Note | nullable `references` | typed ref | ADR-0032 |
    | `WAAuthorization` → WA, → WA Code | composite key | associative entity | **ADR-0041** |
    | `ContractorEngagement` → WA, → Contractor | composite + stint markers | associative entity | **ADR-0041** |

  - **New entity: WAAuthorization.** Associative entity for WA ↔ WA Code M:N. Composite key `(wa_id, wa_code_id)`. No additional fields in MVP. Hard delete. No history (rows are immutable per WA's supersession-immutability; lifecycle is captured on WA's comprehensive history). Cascade-deletes when WA is hard-deleted via `cancel_project` cascade. Gains budget and any other per-(WA, code) state when budget tracking lands (deferred per existing `WA ↔ WA Code budget tracking` carry-forward).

  - **New entity: ContractorEngagement.** Associative entity for WA ↔ Contractor M:N with stint markers. Schema: `(wa_id, contractor_id, started_at, ended_at?)`. Multiple rows per `(wa_id, contractor_id)` permitted when a contractor closes their CPR filing and is re-added to the same WA. CPR Document derives per `ContractorEngagement` row. Lifecycle capture: `engagement_started` (created at contractor addition to WA), `engagement_ended` (when CPR filing closes). Soft delete (referenced by derived CPR Documents).

  - **Time Entry restructure (amends ADR-0035, ADR-0039).** Time Entry schema:
    - `employee_id` — direct M:1 typed ref to Employee.
    - `role_type` — enum (not FK).
    - `project_id` — direct M:1 typed ref to Project.
    - `site_id` — direct M:1 typed ref to School.
    - `wa_code_id` — direct M:1 typed ref to WA Code (mandatory at create, nullable via dismiss cascade per ADR-0027).
    - `date`, `on_site_range`, `off_site_sub_intervals` (per ADR-0034).
    - **No `employee_role_id` FK.**

    EmployeeRole link is derived: lookup row from `(employee_id, role_type)` covering `date`. Used at:
    - Closure-gate evaluation (per ADR-0032 registry).
    - Blocker surfacing (the ADR-0039 blocker predicate reframed, see below).
    - Rate resolution at billing/use time.

    **Amends ADR-0035.** Drops `Time Entry → EmployeeRole` M:1 mandatory FK. Drops the time_entry-write-time boundary invariant *at FK-validation level* — the invariant is replaced by the reframed blocker (see ADR-0039 amendment below). `close_employee_role` and `edit_employee_role` no-orphan-future-Time-Entries guards remain dropped (ADR-0039 had already removed them).

    **Amends ADR-0039.** The "Time-Entry-out-of-role-range" blocker predicate generalizes: **"no EmployeeRole row covers `(time_entry.employee_id, time_entry.role_type, time_entry.date)`."** This now covers two cases under one entry: (a) no EmployeeRole row exists at all for this `(employee, role_type)` (the "entered before role set up" case), and (b) row exists but doesn't cover the date (the termination-orphan case). Same dismissable classification; chain-dismissal logic unchanged.

    **Auto-reparent dissolves.** `change_employee_role_rate`'s branch 3 (close+create+auto-reparent) no longer needs to re-point Time Entry FKs — there are no FKs to re-point. Branch 3 reduces to "close existing row + create new row." The Time Entries previously covered by the old row remain self-describing; rate resolution at billing time picks up the new row automatically via `(employee, role_type, date)` lookup. Significant simplification.

  - **Document single-scope (reshapes ADR-0014, ADR-0015).** Document schema gains `(scope_type, scope_id)`:
    - `scope_type` enum: `project | deliverable | wa_code`.
    - `scope_id`: FK to the appropriate entity.

    **Bundle of a Deliverable** = (Documents where `scope_type = deliverable AND scope_id = D.id`) ∪ (Documents where `scope_type = wa_code AND scope_id ∈ {codes mapping to D}`). Plus derived required Documents (system-generated, also scoped to the Deliverable per derivation). Query, not stored M:M.

    **Single-scope semantic:** if "lab calibration cert" is needed for Deliverables D1 and D2, two distinct Document records exist (D1's cert, D2's cert). They may hold the same file content but are distinct entities.

    **Three-scope distinction earns its keep via cascade:**
    - `scope_type = wa_code` Document, cascade on `dismiss_wa_code`: Document orphans (specific cascade behavior — null `scope_id`, surface a derived blocker, or cascade-delete — left as Step 6b-residual-2 design item).
    - `scope_type = deliverable` Document: unaffected by individual code dismissal; affected only by Deliverable-level events (wasted flag, etc.).
    - `scope_type = project` Document: unaffected by either; tied only to Project state.

    **Re-scoping command:** `edit_document_scope(doc, new_scope_type, new_scope_id)` permitted to coordinator-or-higher. Rare case but in scope; updates the FK pair atomically.

    **Bundle snapshot at submission:** `submit_deliverable` freezes the bundle (the query result) at submission time. Bundle becomes editable again on `under_review → outstanding` (rejection); frozen on `approved` (terminal).

    **Amends ADR-0015.** The Document derivation-set's "WA Codes" entry is more accurately "Deliverables (which derive from WA Codes)." The derivation chain is `WA Code → Deliverable → required Documents`. Document's derivation sources are: Deliverables (transitively WA Codes), DepFilings (direct), Sample Batches (direct, COC + Lab Report), Project (direct, RFP per ADR-0037).

  - **RFA → WA direct ref.** RFA schema gains `amends_wa_id` (M:1 mandatory typed ref to WA). Set at auto-draft creation = the current non-superseded WA on the project at that moment. Immutable for the RFA's lifetime. Project derives via WA → Project (one hop). Pre-condition for auto-draft creation: the WA must be issued (per the user's RFA-only-after-WA-issued lifecycle rule). The WA-issuance-reconciliation flow populates the auto-draft with discrepancies between issued codes and expected codes.

  - **User ↔ Employee.** User schema gains `employee_id?` (nullable M:1 typed ref to Employee, UNIQUE-constrained). Set at User creation: filled when the User represents an Employee (common case — coordinator onboarding); null for superadmin / external auditor cases.

  - **Project ↔ Contractor derived.** No `project_id` on Contractor and no `contractor_id` on Project. "Which contractors have been on this Project" derives via `ContractorEngagement → WA → Project`. CPR derivation per `ContractorEngagement` row.

  - **Roster bumps from 16 → 18 entities.** Added: `WAAuthorization`, `ContractorEngagement`. Handoff entity roster cumulative table refreshes at wrap-up.

  - **Mis-attribution cascade carry-forward.** The "WA mis-attributed to wrong Project" use case (raised in deliberation) needs a future compound command `reassign_wa_project(wa, new_project)` that atomically: flips `WA.project_id`; cascades to WA Codes' `project_id`; cascades to Time Entries' `project_id` (per the new direct ref); validates no other WA on the old project references the moved codes. Plus an ADR-0030 amendment for `project_id` mutability on current WAs (supersession-immutability invariant doesn't currently address this). Out of Step 6c-i scope; placed in step roadmap as Step 6b-residual-2 or post-MVP.

  - **Amendments to other ADRs.**
    - **ADR-0014 (Document/RequiredDocument unification):** Document gains `(scope_type, scope_id)` pair. Slot-spanning lifecycle unchanged; scope is orthogonal to lifecycle.
    - **ADR-0015 (Document derivation set):** "WA Codes" derivation source clarified as "Deliverables (transitively WA Codes)." Required Documents derive from Deliverable; the Deliverable derives from WA Code.
    - **ADR-0020 (WA Code project-scoped):** WA Code's relationship to WA is via `WAAuthorization` associative entity, not implicit.
    - **ADR-0031 (RFA):** RFA gains `amends_wa_id` M:1 mandatory direct ref. Auto-draft creation pre-condition pinned: WA must be issued.
    - **ADR-0033 (Sample Batch):** Sample Batch schema clarified — `site_id` direct M:1 mandatory to School (was loosely listed as "location(s)" in prior ADR text); `sampling_locations` plain text field separate.
    - **ADR-0035 (EmployeeRole):** Time Entry → EmployeeRole FK dropped. Time Entry self-describes employee + role_type. Rate resolution remains "lookup EmployeeRole by `(employee, role_type, date)`."
    - **ADR-0039 (`change_employee_role_rate` compound):** Blocker predicate generalized to "no EmployeeRole covers `(employee, role_type, date)`." Auto-reparent dissolves under the new Time Entry shape.

  - **Carry-forwards.**
    - **Mis-attribution `reassign_wa_project` compound + ADR-0030 amendment for current-WA `project_id` mutability:** Step 6b-residual-2 / post-MVP.
    - **`WAAuthorization` budget fields:** added when budget tracking design lands (existing handoff carry-forward).
    - **Document cascade on `dismiss_wa_code` for WA-Code-scoped Documents:** specific cascade behavior (null scope_id, orphan blocker, or cascade-delete) to be designed in Step 6b-residual-2 or earlier if it blocks Step 6c-ii.
    - **Per-command authorization predicates:** Step 6c-ii. Uses this ADR's relationship + entity surface as substrate.
    - **`ContractorEngagement` lifecycle commands** (`start_contractor_engagement`, `end_contractor_engagement` or equivalents) and CPR derivation rule: Step 6b-residual-2 if not already implicit; possibly already covered by ADR-0024's CPR cycling-family doc_type lifecycle.

---

## ADR-0042 — Write-off model, blocker-resolution binary reframe, and nuclear-option guard

- **Date:** 2026-05-14
- **Decision:** Replaces ADR-0032's "is there a real-world acceptance path?" dismissable/fix-only blocker binary with a **default-resolution** model. Every registry blocker has a structural-fix path (the conflicting data can always be corrected); *some* additionally have a **default-resolution** — a coordinator-initiated command that resolves the blocker by **writing off** the conflicting entities. A **write-off** is an entity that exists but does not count toward billing or blocker/conflict derivation; it is recorded by a new immutable Note subtype `write_off`, attached to the written-off entity and carrying a `reason`. "Written off" is a *derived status* — the entity has a `write_off` Note not superseded by a later `revoke_write_off` — not a per-entity field. Blocker-derivation predicates are computed over not-written-off entities, so a default-resolution dissolves its blocker *structurally*; ADR-0032's closure gate consequently simplifies to "no registry blocker holds" (the "OR has a dismissal Note" escape clause is dropped). The dismissable/fix-only binary is reframed as a derived property — `has-default-resolution` vs. `fix-only` — that governs *which resolution commands are available*, not gate logic. Default-resolutions are guarded as the nuclear option: never autonomously system-initiated (the ADR-0032 pattern-#12 chain-dismissal is the sole declared-consequence exception, inheriting the primary's justification), and requiring a mandatory coordinator justification stamped on the `reason` of every `write_off` Note the command produces. Cascade write-offs from non-blocker commands (e.g. `dismiss_wa_code`) are not separately guarded — they inherit their reason from the initiating command, which is why the model admits non-blocker reasons. Write-off is a liftable status: an explicit `revoke_write_off` command writes an immutable superseding Note. `resolution_kind` becomes `structural_fix | default_resolution | dismissal` (`dismissal` retained only for free-form user-flagged blockers). Vocabulary: `non_billable` (ADR-0027) is retired; `wasted` (ADR-0029) is reframed as a derived reporting label over a written-off Deliverable; `invalid` (ADR-0033 Lab Report state) stays fully distinct. Declares design pattern #14 (write-off / default-resolution). This is the **model half** of Step 6b-residual-2 (session 14a); the per-blocker registry reclassification and per-blocker default-resolution command definitions are session 14b's output.
- **Status:** accepted
- **Context:** ADR-0032 classified each registry blocker `dismissable` ("a real-world acceptance path exists") or `fix-only` ("structurally must be resolved"). Step 6c-ii session 13, working cluster 7 (cross-project commands), surfaced that "fix-only" is partly dishonest: a mechanical acceptance path always exists — mutate the conflicting data until the derived condition dissolves — and ADR-0028 calling cross-project overlap "fix-only" merely pushed that mutation off-system into unaudited manual edits. Bringing it on-system as a defined, audited command is the fix. Step 6b-residual-2 was sized (session 14) as not fitting one window and split (Option A) into 14a (this ADR — the model) and 14b (the registry application). The `write-off` umbrella term was locked session 13; session 14 established that a write-off's reason is not always blocker-registry-derived (an `expected`-code abandonment via `dismiss_wa_code` produces one with reason "code abandoned pre-issuance"), so the model must admit non-blocker reasons. A deliberation correction this session: `split_entry` is a *pure partition* command — it tiles a Time Entry's range into contiguous sub-entries and reassigns batches by collection time — it is **not** itself a write-off; the cross-project-overlap default-resolution is `split_entry` *then* a separate write-off of the overlapping sliver.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Keep a two-bucket taxonomy inside the closure gate — just rename the buckets and swap the classification test.* Rejected — a smaller delta from ADR-0032, but it keeps the gate's "OR has a dismissal Note" clause, which is dishonest in a new way: it treats default-resolution as an override *annotation* when it is actually a *structural change* (the written-off entities leave the predicate domain). The honest model puts the acceptance into the predicate domain, not the gate.
  - *Write-off as a per-entity persisted `written_off` + `write_off_reason` field.* Rejected — per-entity field proliferation across Time Entry, Sample Batch, Deliverable (the exact pattern ADR-0032 rejected for `acknowledged`), redundant with the immutable audit record that must exist anyway, and drift-prone.
  - *Write-off as a pure derived flag (generalize `non_billable`).* Rejected — a derived flag is computed from a structural condition, but a cross-project-overlap sliver (post-`split_entry`) is a structurally valid Time Entry; nothing about it computes to "written off." Moreover the overlap *persists* after the split — the sliver still overlaps the other project's entry — so writing it off is what *resolves* the blocker, meaning write-off must be an *input* the predicate honors, not an *output* derived from the conflict being gone.
  - *Fold write-off into the existing `resolution` Note subtype.* Rejected — a `resolution` Note is blocker-bound (`blocker_ref`); a write-off is produced both by blocker default-resolutions *and* by non-blocker commands (`dismiss_wa_code`), and its reason should name the originating cause, not a proximate blocker. The two are distinct records for distinct jobs: a blocker default-resolution produces both together (N `write_off` Notes on the entities + one `resolution` Note on the blocker); a cascade command produces `write_off` Notes alone.
  - *Auto-lift the write-off when the structural cause is corrected (relink, range edit).* Rejected — putting work back *into* the billable package is a money-affecting decision, not a silent side effect of an edit. Lifting is an explicit `revoke_write_off` command.
  - *Higher authorization bar for default-resolutions (`> coordinator`).* Rejected for MVP — the auth model is coordinator-flat (locked clarification 1; one coordinator per project), so an approval step needs a second actor. The guard is about *deliberateness* (mandatory justification, never auto-invoked), not *who*. Post-MVP at most.
  - *Retire `wasted` entirely, as `non_billable` is retired.* Rejected — `non_billable` was a bland restatement of "written off" for a Time Entry / Sample Batch, with no added meaning; `wasted` carries a real audit distinction ("work was done, then invalidated," vs. an overlap sliver where the work was real but merely double-booked) worth keeping as a label.
  - *Fold `invalid` (Lab Report) into write-off.* Rejected — `invalid` is a genuine lifecycle *state* with an *outbound* transition (`invalid → saved`), and a blocker *condition* (#3); it means "not done yet," not "excluded from the package." Different structural level from a state-orthogonal exclusion marker.
- **Consequences:**
  - **`write_off` Note subtype.** Note's `subtype` enum (`regular | blocker | resolution` per ADR-0032; `audit_reason` added by ADR-0040) gains `write_off`. Fields: a polymorphic entity target (the written-off entity, via ADR-0018's reference); `reason` (mandatory free text for default-resolution-initiated write-offs; derived/inherited for cascade write-offs); an optional `references` link to the originating blocker/resolution Note (null for non-blocker causes). Immutable, like `blocker` / `resolution` / `audit_reason`.
  - **Write-off semantics.** A written-off entity is retained (audit-preserved) but does not count toward billing aggregation or toward blocker/conflict derivation. It is a marker *orthogonal to* state machines (like ADR-0029's `wasted`, not like ADR-0033's `invalid` state), applied uniformly across billing/conflict-counted entities (Time Entry, Sample Batch, Deliverable). "Written off" is the derived status defined above. Subsumes ADR-0027's `non_billable` derived flag, which is retired.
  - **Default-resolution model.** Every registry blocker has a structural-fix path. A blocker *additionally* has a **default-resolution** iff a coherent one exists. **Coherence test:** the blocker's condition can be dissolved by writing off a well-defined set of entities — i.e. by *excluding* something, as opposed to *creating or correcting* something. The test fails when the condition is the absence of something closure definitionally requires (registry entry #10, non-terminal RFP not `saved` — there is no entity to write off; the RFP must come to exist). A default-resolution is a compound: it may first mutate structure (e.g. `split_entry`) and then writes off the conflicting entities, producing one `write_off` Note per entity plus one `resolution` Note on the blocker.
  - **Binary reframe.** ADR-0032's per-registry-entry `dismissable | fix-only` classification is replaced by the property `has-default-resolution | fix-only`, and the classification *test* changes from "is there a real-world acceptance path?" to "does a coherent default-resolution exist?". The property governs **which resolution commands the coordinator has available** — has-default-resolution → structural-fix *or* the default-resolution command; fix-only → structural-fix only — and is *no longer part of closure-gate logic*. The per-blocker reclassification pass over all 11 registry entries is session 14b.
  - **Closure-gate simplification.** Because blocker-derivation predicates are computed over not-written-off entities, a default-resolved blocker *stops holding* structurally (its conflicting entities leave the predicate domain). ADR-0032's gate — "(i) no fix-only blocker holds AND (ii) every dismissable blocker no longer holds derivationally OR has a dismissal resolution Note" — collapses to: **no registry blocker holds**, predicates evaluated over not-written-off entities. Clause (ii)'s Note-annotation escape is removed.
  - **Nuclear-option guard.** Default-resolution commands are guarded two ways. (a) **Never autonomously system-initiated** — a default-resolution is always either directly coordinator-initiated, or a *declared chain-consequence* of a coordinator-initiated resolution (the ADR-0032 pattern-#12 chain-dismissal), which inherits the primary act's justification rather than prompting for its own. (b) **Mandatory justification** — the coordinator supplies one justification per invocation; it is stamped onto the `reason` of every `write_off` Note that invocation produces (e.g. all slivers of one overlap resolution share one justification). The `resolution` Note records `resolution_kind: 'default_resolution'` and links; it gains no new free-text field.
  - **Cascade write-offs.** Write-offs produced as a *cascade* of a non-default-resolution command — e.g. `dismiss_wa_code` nulling `wa_code` on referencing Time Entries / Sample Batches — are **not** separately guarded: they inherit their `reason` from the initiating command (consistent with the session-12 clarification that cascade effects inherit from the initiating user-facing command). This is the structural reason the write-off model must admit non-blocker, non-prompted reasons.
  - **`revoke_write_off`.** Write-off is a liftable *current status*, not equated with the bare existence of the `write_off` Note. Lifting is explicit — a `revoke_write_off` command writes an immutable superseding Note (Notes are not deletable; this matches the RFP reopen-cycle shape, not an in-place undo). Re-including the entity re-exposes it to blocker-derivation predicates. The command's full shape (parameters, guards) is carried forward — no natural home step yet.
  - **`resolution_kind` value set.** Becomes `structural_fix | default_resolution | dismissal`. `default_resolution` replaces the registry-blocker use of the former `dismissal` value. `dismissal` is retained *only* for free-form **user-flagged** blockers (no registry entry, no default-resolution — the coordinator simply decided to stop tracking it), which the binary reframe does not touch since they were never in the registry.
  - **Design pattern #14 — write-off / default-resolution.** *An entity that exists but should not count (toward billing, conflicts) is excluded by an immutable `write_off` record carrying a reason, rather than deleted or mutated. Derived predicates — billing aggregation, blocker conditions — are computed over not-written-off entities, so excluding an entity dissolves the conditions it participated in. The exclusion is produced either by a guarded, coordinator-initiated **default-resolution** command (the nuclear option for resolving a blocker: mandatory justification, never auto-invoked) or as a reason-inheriting cascade of another command. It is reversible only by an explicit superseding command.* Distinct from pattern #9 (delete-or-dismiss): write-off always retains the entity. Pattern #10 (derived `wasted` flag) is now an instance of this pattern rather than a standalone mechanism.
  - **Amendments to other ADRs.**
    - **ADR-0027 (WA Code / dismiss cascade).** The `non_billable` derived flag is **retired**. Its job splits cleanly: the orphan condition (`wa_code == null`) remains blocker #1 / #2 — the *problem* — while exclusion from billing is the write-off status — one *resolution* of that problem. ADR-0027's dismiss-cascade text that derived `non_billable` is superseded by the write-off model; the WA Code state machine and the cascade's reference-nulling behaviour are otherwise unchanged.
    - **ADR-0029 (Deliverable / wasted flag).** `wasted` is reframed: no longer an independently-derived boolean ("WA Code dismissed AND work done"), but a **derived reporting label** for a written-off Deliverable. The work-done-vs-not split is unchanged — no work done → hard-delete per pattern #9; work done → written off, labelled `wasted`. The wasted Deliverable's write-off is a *cascade* write-off (from WA-Code dismissal/removal), so it carries an inherited reason. Re-derivation mechanics and the `dismissed → dismissed OR removed` trigger extension interact with Step 6c-iii (which already lists ADR-0029) and are settled there.
    - **ADR-0032 (Blocker pattern).** The dismissable/fix-only binary and its classification test are reframed; the closure gate is simplified; the Note `subtype` enum gains `write_off`; `resolution_kind` gains `default_resolution`. The per-registry-entry reclassification is session 14b's output. ADR-0032's lazy materialization, chain-dismissal (#12), and paired-blocker mechanics are otherwise unchanged.
    - **ADR-0028 / ADR-0033 / ADR-0039 — touchpoints for 14b and downstream.** ADR-0028 (cross-project overlap) gains a default-resolution — `split_entry` then write off the overlapping sliver — defined in 14b. ADR-0033 and ADR-0039 chain-dismissal instances now also emit `write_off` Notes for the secondary entities — folded into 14b or the relevant downstream amendment.
  - **Out of scope (session 14b and beyond).** The one-by-one classification of all 11 registry blockers (`has-default-resolution` vs. `fix-only`); per-blocker default-resolution command definitions (cross-project overlap is the worked example); the `revoke_write_off` command shape.
  - **Carry-forwards.**
    - **`revoke_write_off` command shape** — parameters and guards undefined; no home step yet (candidate: alongside `split_entry`, Step 6d or a residual).
    - **`split_entry` half-open interval semantics** — surfaced this session: Time Entry ranges are `[start, end)`; a boundary instant (and a sample collected at it) belongs to the entry *starting* at the boundary; gross duration is plain `end − start` (the exclusive end is a limit, not "one unit prior"). Refines ADR-0034; belongs with `split_entry`'s deferred command-shape work.

---

## ADR-0043 — Contract entity, Project → Contract relationship, and contract-attachment model

- **Date:** 2026-05-14
- **Decision:** Introduces the **Contract** entity (19th in the roster) and wires Project to it. A Contract is the contractual basis a project is opened against; it defines, per contract, the default flat fee for each WA code type, and it is the scoping anchor for employee billing rates. **Attachment model — the two schedules land on opposite sides of the fork.** Employee role rates stay **FK-side**: EmployeeRole keeps its own per-row `rate` and (in Step 6c-iv-b) gains a `contract_id`; Contract carries no role-rate table. Code default flat fees go **inline**: Contract carries a `code_flat_fee_schedule` — a value collection of `{code_type, fee}` pairs, **non-temporal** (fixed for the contract's whole life). The asymmetry is intentional — title rates are not consistent across employees or contracts, so they cannot collapse into a contract-level table; code flat fees are genuinely per-`(code_type, contract)` with no per-instance variation, so they can. **Contract schema:** `id` (system UUID per ADR-0005); `contract_number` (mandatory, uniqueness-constrained natural key); `start_date` + nullable `end_date`; `code_flat_fee_schedule`; optional `name` (when null, the display label derives as `C` + the last 5 characters of `contract_number` — a derived label, not a stored default). No counterparty field (SCA is the sole MVP client; additional clients are indefinitely deferred). No contract total/ceiling (post-MVP, with budget tracking). **Lifecycle:** no state machine — status (`pending` / `active` / `expired`) is derived from `(start_date, end_date?)` + clock, the reasoning ADR-0035 used to reject an explicit state machine on EmployeeRole; early termination is an edit to `end_date`, not a transition. **History pattern:** audit log. **Delete policy:** soft delete. **Project → Contract:** M:1, mandatory, direct typed ref (`Project.contract_id`); set at `create_project`, which gains a mandatory `contract` parameter (admin-side per ADR-0040); no in-term validation at creation; **immutable in MVP** — no mutation command. Entity roster 18 → 19. Amends ADR-0037 (`create_project` signature). This is the **model half** of Step 6c-iv (session 6c-iv-a); the EmployeeRole and WA Code retrofit is Step 6c-iv-b.
- **Status:** accepted (amended by ADR-0044 — `Project.contract_id` removed and the Contract re-homed onto the WABundle; "immutable in MVP" retired, contract now mutable via `issue_wa` / `edit_wabundle`; the `reassign_project_contract` carry-forward dissolved. The Contract entity definition itself is unchanged)
- **Context:** New requirement given 2026-05-14: every project is opened against a specific contract, and contracts define both the employee rate schedule and the WA code default flat fees — so both become contract-scoped. Previously deferrable because new contracts are rare, but one was just signed, making it immediately relevant. Step 6c-iv was sized as a Case 2 entry, tripped the fit checklist (Signal 1 — three independently-deliberable decisions: the attachment-model fork, the EmployeeRole invariant restructure, the WA Code flat-fee scoping; Signal 5 — cross-concern reach across entity identification, rate resolution, and WA Code config), and was split Option A (model / application) into 6c-iv-a and 6c-iv-b along the model/application dependency seam — 6c-iv-b's EmployeeRole and WA Code work cannot be deliberated concretely until the attachment model is fixed. This ADR is 6c-iv-a's output. The load-bearing decision was the attachment model; the deliberation established that it does not land uniformly — employee rates and code flat fees go to opposite sides of the fork — which is the ADR's central finding.
- **Alternatives considered:**
