The **contract-resolution path** (ADR-0045) shortens from `code → project → WABundle → contract` to `code → WABundle → contract` — one hop fewer, structurally identical at runtime since the path always resolves through the same bundle. Amends ADR-0020 (scoping rationale reframes from operational shell to contractual-identity entity).

  **(2) Single-table WACode with explicit `level` discriminator.** WA Codes come in two flavors — **project-level** (apply across the whole project, e.g., supervision) and **building-level** (apply at a specific school within the project, e.g., asbestos sampling at school X). Sample-collection codes are one species of building-level code, not their own class. Both flavors share the entire WA Code substrate — state machine (ADR-0027), references from TE / SB and WACA, write-off cascade behavior, lifecycle history. Modelled as a **single table** with an **explicit `level: enum('project' | 'building')` discriminator** (required, non-default) and a **nullable `school_id`** (M:1 → School). Two structural invariants: `WACode.level = 'building' ⟺ WACode.school_id IS NOT NULL` (enforced as DB CHECK), and `WACode.school_id IS NOT NULL ⇒ WACode.school_id ∈ WACode.wabundle.sites` (the bundle-sites invariant — see (3)). `WACode.level` is denormalized at creation from the code type's `default_level` (see (5)) and fixed thereafter; changing a code's level requires changing its code type, which is not a supported operation.

  **(3) WABundle gains `sites` (M:N → School) with a building-level WA Code containment invariant.** A WABundle declares its in-scope schools via an M:N associative entity **WABundleSite** with composite key `(wabundle_id, school_id)` (no additional fields, no history, hard-delete on row). The invariant: **every building-level WA Code on a bundle has its `school_id ∈ bundle.sites`.** Sites are declared intentionally — *not* auto-grown from code creation, so the invariant has real bite. `create_project` (ADR-0044 compound) gains a `sites: [School]` parameter alongside `contract`. `edit_wabundle` (`role >= admin`, ADR-0044) handles post-creation site mutations: adding a site is unconditional; removing a site is guarded — fails if any WA Code under the bundle references that school. Amends ADR-0044 (WABundle schema gains `sites` access via WABundleSite; `create_project` signature gains `sites`; `edit_wabundle` gains site management).

  **(4) TE / SB drop direct `project_id`; project derives through `wa_code`.** Time Entry and Sample Batch shed their direct `project_id` (ADR-0041) — Project becomes a derived/validated read via `TE / SB → wa_code → WACode → WABundle → Project`. The historical fact on TE / SB is `(employee, date, site)`; the project association is a coordinator's downstream organizational fact, not an empirical-truth datum. `site_id` (TE / SB direct, ADR-0041) remains intact. **Cascade keeps the FK** (principle stated here; mechanics in Step 6c-iii-b-ii's ADR): the `dismiss_wa_code` / removal cascade (ADR-0027 / ADR-0042 / ADR-0046) no longer nulls `wa_code` on referencing TE / SB — it keeps the reference (now pointing at a `dismissed` / `removed` code) and emits a `write_off` Note. With WABundle always present from `create_project` and missing-derived auto-generation already in expected form (ADR-0022), `wa_code = null` becomes a state the system can no longer produce. Blocker registry consequence: entries **#1 (TE `wa_code = null`)** and **#2 (SB `wa_code = null`)** become unfireable predicates and are removed in 6c-iii-b-ii's ADR (the registry's source of truth for that pass). Amends ADR-0041 (relationship table — TE / SB drop direct `project_id`; new derived rows TE / SB → Project via wa_code chain); amends ADR-0027 / ADR-0042 / ADR-0046 cascade behavior (principle: keep FK, don't null; full reframe in 6c-iii-b-ii's ADR).

  **(5) `WACodeConf` is code-side static config.** The WA Code-type catalog (the set of `code_type_id` identifiers, their display names, and their `default_level`) is **code-side static configuration** — a deployed Python module / dataclass list, not a DB entity. Minimum-viable entry: `{ code_type_id, name, default_level: 'project' | 'building' }`. Other attributes (abbreviation, description, category) may be added in-file as needed. Default flat fee per code type stays on `Contract.code_flat_fee_schedule[code_type_id]` (ADR-0045), keyed by `code_type_id`; the schedule reference and the code-type catalog are coupled only through the shared identifier. Adding a code type requires a code deployment — an acceptable cost given the catalog's empirical churn rate (rare, every 6+ months or longer). Migration to a DB entity remains a future option if churn rises; the `code_type_id` keys are stable across the migration.

  **(6) `WAAuthorization` → `WACodeAssignment` rename (shorthand WACA).** Naming-only refactor of the associative entity introduced by ADR-0041 (composite key `(wa_id, wa_code_id)`, no additional fields in MVP, gains budget when budget tracking lands). The rename improves M:N-link clarity (the row records that the WA *assigns* authority for a code) and reads naturally into the post-MVP budget direction (the budget is *assigned to a code on a WA*). Amends ADR-0041 (entity name + relationship-table row label); amends ADR-0020 (vocabulary). All cross-references to `WAAuthorization` in prior ADRs are read as `WACodeAssignment` going forward.

  **(7) `reassign_wa_project(wa, new_project)` compound — work follows automatically; school-subset guard.** Compound command for the misattribution-correction use case. The `move_work` flag from the original brief **dissolves** — under the project-derivation-through-wa_code model, TE / SB referencing the WA's codes automatically derive their new project once the WA is in the new bundle; there is no separate "move the work" step to flag. Guard: `moving_wa.codes.school_id ⊆ target_project.wabundle.sites` (the school-subset check — restricts the operation to projects that already cover the moving WA's school context). Predicate: `role >= coordinator` (inherits ADR-0047's Cluster 3 named-WA-domain class rule; no explicit row needed). Interface is settled here; the deeper mechanics (version_seq integration into the target chain, source-bundle gap handling, the special case of moving the only WA out of a bundle, audit-trail shape on both sides) are an implementation-phase concern — the ADR fixes the interface + guard + work-follows principle, not the version-chain bookkeeping.

  **(8) Item 5 — TE / SB keep direct `site_id`** (ADR-0041, settled session 12) is confirmed in the relationship-table refresh. The empirical-truth principle pushes `(employee, date, site)` onto the TE / SB row; `project_id` was the outlier and is now retired (see (4)).

  Plus a clarifying confirmation: **v0 in-place issuance (Fork B).** ADR-0044 spec'd per-version `issued_date` / `initialization_date` "null while `pending`, set at issuance" — implicit in-place language. Made explicit here: the v0 `pending → issued` transition under ADR-0030's `issue_wa` is in-place — v0's state flips to `issued`, dates populate, expected codes reconcile (ADR-0022). No new row is created at initial issuance; subsequent amendment-issued WAs (RFA-approval, third-WA-origin in 6c-iii-b-ii) are v1+ with their own rows. Audit captured by WA's comprehensive-capture history pattern. No structural change to ADR-0030's state machine.

  Entity roster: 20 → 21 (WABundleSite added as an associative entity, following the WACodeAssignment / ContractorEngagement precedent in ADR-0041 of counting associatives as roster entries). WA Code adds `level` + `school_id?`. Cumulative tables in `handoff.md` refreshed accordingly.
- **Status:** accepted
- **Context:** Step 6c-iii-b was sized 2026-05-15 (`_workflow.md` Case 2 — signals 1, 3, 5 fired) and split along the item-cluster seam into 6c-iii-b-i (items 1–5 of the original brief — restructure surface) + 6c-iii-b-ii (item 6 — WA Code removal model). This ADR is 6c-iii-b-i's output. Deliberation in chat unwound the original brief in two unexpected places: item 5 ("confirm TE / SB keep direct `project_id`") turned into a substantive reframe (project becomes derived through wa_code, the historical fact on TE / SB is `(employee, date, site)`, and the cascade reframes to keep-FK rather than null); and the original "items 1–5 are mechanical" framing for item 1 turned out to require a coupled fork on WA Code's single-vs-two-table modeling (project-level vs. building-level codes) plus a WABundle.sites declaration to give the cross-project reassignment school-guard a structural target. The original `move_work` flag on `reassign_wa_project` dissolved as a consequence of project-derivation. The remaining items (rename, WACodeConf placement, v0 in-place issuance clarification) landed at expected weight.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Keep direct `project_id` on TE / SB (the calibration-round position before the user pushed back).* Rejected — `project_id` at TE / SB creation is a coordinator-intent snapshot, not a historical fact; it can be wrong at scheduling time, can change after reassignment, and is not the live truth. Project's authoritative source is the contractual binding via `wa_code → bundle`. Carrying both a direct `project_id` and a derivable one introduces drift risk for no information gain.
  - *Denormalize `last_known_project_id` on TE / SB as a sticky pointer for the `wa_code = null` interim.* Rejected — `wa_code = null` does not survive contact with the post-WABundle world (WABundle is always present, expected codes auto-generate, cascade keeps FK). The interim doesn't exist; denormalization solves a problem the model no longer has.
  - *Two-table modeling for WA Codes (ProjectLevelCode vs. BuildingLevelCode).* Rejected — the two flavors share the entire WA Code substrate (state machine, references from TE / SB / WACA, lifecycle, cascade); splitting forces polymorphic FKs from TE / SB or duplicated reference plumbing, duplicate lifecycle code, UNION queries for "all codes on this bundle," and partitions invariants that are most readable when stated once. The single-entity, two-flavor reading is the right model; the explicit `level` discriminator makes the dispatch readable and the constraints DB-enforceable.
  - *Nullable `school_id` alone as the project-vs-building discriminator (no `level` column).* Rejected — implicit "absence of column value tells you what kind of row this is" is a known structural smell; readers and queries have to know null-as-discriminator folklore. An explicit `level` column + coupled CHECK constraint costs one column and dissolves the smell.
  - *School-on-code-type (school as an attribute of the WA code type rather than the WA code instance).* Rejected — nothing in the WA code configuration is site-related; the type is about *what kind of work* (asbestos sampling, supervision), not *where*. The school is row-level on instances.
  - *Auto-grow WABundle.sites from WA Code creation (allow adding a code at a new school and have the bundle's sites set silently expand to include it).* Rejected — would make the school-subset guard on `reassign_wa_project` vacuous (a move would auto-grow the target's sites). Intentional curation gives the guard real bite. Friction case (a new school becomes operationally relevant) is handled by `edit_wabundle`.
  - *WACodeConf as a DB entity with admin CRUD.* Rejected as premature — empirical churn rate is "rare" (session-12 user signal), schema/history/audit/seeding cost is real, the admin-command surface does not justify itself, and migration to a DB entity later is cheap (stable `code_type_id` keys). Re-addressable if churn rises.
  - *`reassign_wa_project` keeps the `move_work` flag.* Rejected — under project-derivation through wa_code, work follows the WA automatically (TE / SB inherit the new project via their wa_code reference). There is no coherent case for "move the WA but leave the work behind" — that operation, if ever needed, is `relink_te_wa_code` / `relink_sample_batch_wa_code` on individual records, a different command class. The flag added a degree of freedom with no real branch behind it.
  - *Set v0 aside as a pending placeholder and create a new v1 at first issuance (Fork A).* Rejected — leaves v0 stuck in `pending` forever as audit junk and breaks the version-seq semantic where v0 = initial / v1+ = amendments. ADR-0044's per-version date-fields-populated-at-issuance language already implies in-place (Fork B); confirming it explicitly here closes any ambiguity.
- **Consequences:**
  - **WA Code schema.** `WACode { id, wabundle_id (M:1 → WABundle, required), code_type (string identifier, keyed against WACodeConf), level (enum('project','building'), required), school_id (nullable, M:1 → School), state (ADR-0027 lifecycle), ... }`. Field `project_id` removed (was ADR-0020). CHECK constraint: `(level = 'building') ⟺ (school_id IS NOT NULL)`. Conditional FK invariant (`school_id IS NOT NULL ⇒ school_id ∈ wabundle.sites`) enforced at the application layer with a CHECK / trigger where the SQL engine supports it.
  - **WABundle schema.** Gains an M:N relationship to School via the **WABundleSite** associative entity (`wabundle_id`, `school_id`, composite key, no other fields, no history pattern, hard-delete). WABundle's audit log covers add / remove site operations through `create_project` and `edit_wabundle`. The 1:1 with Project, the `contract_id`, and the three SCA-supplied natural keys (ADR-0044) are unchanged.
  - **`create_project` signature** (amends ADR-0044). Gains `sites: [School]` parameter. The compound creates Project + WABundle + the `sites` set + v0 `pending` WA atomically. The `sites` set may be empty at creation (admin doesn't yet know the in-scope schools); building-level WA Codes can only be added once at least the relevant school is in the set, by `edit_wabundle`.
  - **`edit_wabundle` extension** (amends ADR-0044). Gains site management: `add_site(school)` (unconditional) and `remove_site(school)` (guarded — fails if any WA Code under the bundle references `school`). Predicate stays `role >= admin` (ADR-0047 explicit row). The signature change does not change the predicate.
  - **TE / SB schema.** Drop direct `project_id` column. Drop direct project relationship from the ADR-0041 table. Add derived row: `Time Entry → Project` via `wa_code → WACode → WABundle → Project`; same for `Sample Batch → Project`. Site (`site_id` direct on both, M:1 → School) is unchanged.
  - **Cascade-keep-FK principle.** `dismiss_wa_code` (ADR-0027) and the removal cascade (ADR-0042 / ADR-0046) no longer null `wa_code` on referencing TE / SB — they keep the FK and emit a `write_off` Note on each referencing record. The dismissed / removed code stays referenceable in a terminal state, preserving the project-derivation chain. Full mechanics — what the cascade does instead of nulling, the `write_off` Note's shape on referencing records, the closure-blocker shape for cascade-written-off TE / SB — written up in Step 6c-iii-b-ii's ADR. The amendments to ADR-0027, ADR-0042, ADR-0046 land in full there; this ADR fixes the principle as a consequence of project-derivation.
  - **Blocker registry — #1 and #2 become unfireable.** With `wa_code = null` no longer a producible state, blockers **#1 (TE `wa_code = null`)** and **#2 (SB `wa_code = null`)** are predicates over an empty state set. They are removed from the 12-entry registry by 6c-iii-b-ii's ADR (the registry's source of truth for that pass). ADR-0046's `default_resolve` Hybrid command's `blocker ∈ {#1, #2}` rows in its dispatch are similarly retired there. ADR-0047's predicate-table rows for those default-resolutions stay covered by the generic `default_resolve` row (no removal needed in ADR-0047 — the command is generic).
  - **Contract-resolution path shortens** (amends ADR-0045). The WA Code → Contract derivation reads `code → WABundle → contract` (one hop fewer than ADR-0045's `code → project → WABundle → contract`); the Time Entry → Contract derivation similarly shortens — Time Entry no longer holds a direct `project_id`, so the path is `TE → wa_code → WABundle → contract`. The EmployeeRole rate-resolution lookup keyed on `(employee, role_type, contract, date)` is unaffected — the contract is still resolved the same way, just via the bundle directly. ADR-0045's "always resolves" property (anchored by WABundle's required `contract_id` and create_project's bundle creation) is preserved.
  - **v0 in-place issuance** (clarifies ADR-0030 / ADR-0044). `issue_wa` operates in-place on v0: v0's state flips `pending → issued`, `issued_date` and `initialization_date` populate, expected codes reconcile (ADR-0022). No new WA row is created at initial issuance. Amendment-issued WAs (RFA-approval per ADR-0031; third WA origin per 6c-iii-b-ii) are v1+ with their own rows. WA's comprehensive-capture history pattern records the state flip; the row's identity is preserved.
  - **`WAAuthorization` → `WACodeAssignment` rename** (amends ADR-0041). The associative entity composite key `(wa_id, wa_code_id)` and field set are unchanged in MVP. Future budget tracking (post-MVP) adds the budget field on this entity. Shorthand: **WACA**. All prior ADR references to `WAAuthorization` are read as `WACodeAssignment` going forward.
  - **`WACodeConf` shape.** Code-side static config (Python module / dataclass list). Minimum entry: `code_type_id` (machine identifier), `name` (display label), `default_level` ('project' | 'building'). Adding a code type requires a code deployment. The schema-side concept (DB table) is rejected for MVP. ADR-0045's `Contract.code_flat_fee_schedule[code_type_id]` keys against `code_type_id`; the catalog and the schedule are loosely coupled through the shared identifier. WA Code `level` is denormalized from `default_level` at creation and fixed; consistency (`WACode.level == WACodeConf[WACode.code_type].default_level`) enforced at create-time at the application layer.
  - **`reassign_wa_project(wa, new_project)` interface.** Compound command. Predicate: `role >= coordinator` (ADR-0047 Cluster 3 class rule; no explicit row needed). Guard: `moving_wa.codes.school_id ⊆ target_project.wabundle.sites` (building-level codes only — project-level codes have null school and are unconstrained). Effect: the WA's `wabundle_id` rebinds to the target bundle; work follows automatically via project-derivation through wa_code. Deeper mechanics (version_seq integration in the target chain, source-bundle bookkeeping after a move, the special case of moving the only WA out of a source bundle, audit-trail shape on both bundles) are implementation-phase concerns and are not pinned by this ADR.
  - **Amendments to other ADRs.**
    - **ADR-0020 (WA Code project-scoping).** WA Code reparented onto WABundle (`wabundle_id` replaces `project_id`). Scoping rationale reframed: WA Codes scope to the contractual-identity entity (WABundle), not the operational shell (Project). WA Code schema gains `level` (enum discriminator) and nullable `school_id`. WA Code → Contract derivation shortens to `code → WABundle → contract`.
    - **ADR-0027 (WA Code state machine and dismiss cascade).** Cascade step (2) — "nulls `wa_code` on referencing TE / SB" — retired; replaced by cascade-keep-FK behavior (full mechanics in Step 6c-iii-b-ii's ADR). State machine itself is untouched by this ADR (further amendments — `removed` terminal, `dismiss_wa_code` narrowing, delete-substitution drop — land in 6c-iii-b-ii's ADR).
    - **ADR-0030 (WA concrete state machine).** Explicit clarification: `pending → issued` (the initial `issue_wa` path) operates in-place on v0; no new WA row is created at initial issuance. The state machine, transitions, and supersession-immutability invariant are otherwise unchanged.
    - **ADR-0041 (entity-pair relationships).** Relationship table amended: drop direct `Time Entry → Project` and `Sample Batch → Project` rows; add derived rows via `wa_code → WACode → WABundle → Project` for each. WA Code → Project becomes derived (`WA Code → WABundle → Project`). New direct row: `WA Code → WABundle` (M:1 required) replacing `WA Code → Project`. New M:N row via WABundleSite: `WABundle → School`. Rename `WAAuthorization` → `WACodeAssignment` throughout the relationship table and vocabulary.
    - **ADR-0042 (write-off model) / ADR-0046 (cascade chains).** Cascade behavior reframed: the cascade from `dismiss_wa_code` / removal (and any future cascades that previously nulled the FK) instead keeps the FK and emits a `write_off` Note on the referencing record. Full re-statement of the cascade mechanics — what the cascade does instead of nulling, registry-level removal of blockers #1 and #2, downstream effect on ADR-0046's chain shape `te_batches_by_coverage` (the chain still operates per-TE; the cascade's per-record effect changes from null-FK to write-off-Note-with-FK) — lands in Step 6c-iii-b-ii's ADR. This ADR fixes the principle.
    - **ADR-0044 (WABundle entity).** WABundle gains the M:N → School relationship via WABundleSite (associative entity). `create_project` signature gains a `sites` parameter; the compound now creates Project + WABundle + sites + v0 pending WA atomically. `edit_wabundle` gains site management (add unconditionally; remove if no WA Code under the bundle references the school). v0 in-place issuance is the canonical reading of the per-version-date-fields language and is restated explicitly. The WABundle's other fields (`contract_id`, `project_id`, the three SCA-supplied natural keys) are unchanged.
    - **ADR-0045 (contract-scoping retrofit).** Contract-resolution path statement shortens to `entity → WABundle → contract` for any entity that holds a direct `wabundle_id` or chains to one (WA Code, WA). For Time Entry and Sample Batch, the path is `entity → wa_code → WACode → WABundle → contract`. The path remains "always resolves" (WABundle always exists; `contract_id` is required at bundle creation). Rate resolution and WA Code default flat fee derivations are unchanged in shape.
  - **Cumulative-tables update.** Entity roster row for WA Code reflects bundle-parent + `level` + `school_id?` fields. WABundle row reflects the `sites` (via WABundleSite) addition. WAAuthorization row renamed to WACodeAssignment. New roster row #21 for **WABundleSite** (associative entity, ADR-0041 conventions). Per-entity history-pattern + delete-policy assignments for WACodeAssignment (replacing WAAuthorization): unchanged (no history; hard delete). WABundleSite: no history; hard delete. Vocabulary entries for WACodeAssignment / WACA, WABundleSite, WACodeConf + `default_level`, building-level / project-level WA Codes, `reassign_wa_project`, and the cascade-keep-FK principle.
- **Carry-forwards.**
  - **Step 6c-iii-b-ii — WA Code removal model.** Inherits cascade-keep-FK as the principle; writes the full cascade mechanics, blocker registry trim (removes #1, #2), ADR-0027 / ADR-0029 / ADR-0030 / ADR-0031 / ADR-0033 amendments, `removed` terminal, `dismiss_wa_code` narrowing, RFA hybrid line items, third WA origin. ADR-0042 / ADR-0046's full cascade re-statement also lands there.
  - **`reassign_wa_project` mechanics — implementation phase.** Version_seq integration in the target bundle's chain, source-bundle bookkeeping after a move (especially "what if the moving WA was the source bundle's only WA"), audit-trail shape on both sides. Interface + guard fixed here; bookkeeping is implementation-phase work.
  - **WACodeConf evolution.** Migration to a DB entity remains an option if catalog churn rises beyond the "rare" empirical rate. The `code_type_id` keys are stable across the migration; no model-side changes needed if it lands.
  - **`level` mutation on a WA Code — not a supported operation in MVP.** Changing a code's level would require changing its code type, which is not a supported operation. If a use case emerges (e.g., a code type's `default_level` changes on the catalog side), the migration is a deployment concern, not an application command.
  - **Future non-school-keyed scoping dimensions on WA Codes.** If new scoping axes emerge (e.g., a contractor-keyed code class), the `level` enum extends with new values + per-value nullable FKs + per-value CHECK constraints; the single-table pattern absorbs them without restructuring.

---

## ADR-0049 — WA Code removal model: `dismiss_wa_code` narrowing, `removed` terminal, RFA hybrid line items, generalized `issue_wa` for SCA-direct amendments, shared cascade under keep-FK, blocker registry trim

- **Date:** 2026-05-15
- **Decision:** Lands item 6 of Step 6c-iii-b (this ADR is Step 6c-iii-b-ii's output). Six coupled decisions on WA Code's removal model, inheriting ADR-0048 §4's cascade-keep-FK principle.

  **(1) `dismiss_wa_code` narrowed.** Valid targets: `expected` and `pending_rfa` only — the `issued → dismissed` transition is dropped (replaced by `issued → removed` per (2)). The command always transitions; ADR-0027's delete-substitution branch (hard-delete when no references ever existed) is dropped — dismissal always records the lifecycle event, even for never-referenced codes. Optional `reason_text` parameter → `audit_reason` Note (ADR-0040) attached to the WA Code's lifecycle-capture record for the dismissal event. Predicate unchanged: `role >= coordinator` (ADR-0047 Cluster 3 explicit row).

  **(2) `removed` terminal state.** New WA Code state. Only entered via `issued → removed`. Two triggers: `approve_rfa` resolving a `remove` line item (per (3)), or `issue_wa`'s SCA-direct amendment branch diffing a code as dropped (per (4)). Distinct from `dismissed` ("never made it onto a WA") — `removed` means "was on an issued WA, taken off after the fact." Terminal: no outbound transitions. Pattern #9 (delete-or-dismiss) is no longer exercised by WA Code; the pattern itself stands for other entities (empty-draft RFA hard-delete, never-referenced `pending` WA hard-delete on project cancellation).

  **(3) RFA as a hybrid instrument.** RFA line items gain a type discriminator: `add | remove | budget`. Budget deferred behind budget tracking — placeholder only, ADR-0027's `budget_rfa_needed` state stays a deferred surface. **Additions stay system-derived** — a WA Code's `expected → pending_rfa` transition continues to atomically add an `add` line item to the bundle's open draft (creating one if none exists), per ADR-0031. **Removals are coordinator-authored** via new command **`add_rfa_line_item(bundle, code, type: add | remove)`** — find-or-create the bundle's draft, append the line item. The command is the only coordinator-facing path for `remove` line items; `type = add` is admitted by the discriminator for narrow recovery paths (e.g., a coordinator re-requesting a dismissed code) but is operationally rare — additions in normal flow are system-derived. Guards at line-item creation: `type = remove` ⇒ `code.state = issued` (non-`issued` removal request is rejected; `dismiss_wa_code` covers the conceptual operation for `expected` / `pending_rfa` codes); reject if any existing line item on the open draft already targets `code` (no add+remove or duplicate-remove on one cycle). The command does not transition any WA Code state — code transitions fire only at submit / approve / reject / withdraw boundaries. ADR-0031's empty-draft hard-delete still applies symmetrically: if the only line items were coordinator-authored removals and they're all rescinded before submission, the draft hard-deletes (revoke-line-item command shape is a carry-forward).

  **`approve_rfa` composition** becomes `(prior WA's codes ∪ add-target line items) \ remove-target line items` (was `prior ∪ line items`). **Polymorphic resolution** on line-item type:
    - *Add-targets* (unchanged from ADR-0031): code is `rfa_in_review` during review; `approve_rfa → issued`, `reject_rfa` / `withdraw_rfa → pending_rfa`.
    - *Remove-targets*: code stays `issued` through review (no intermediate state — the code remains operationally `issued`: work continues, billing aggregates, blockers fire normally); `approve_rfa → removed` (shared cascade fires per (5)); `reject_rfa` / `withdraw_rfa → no transition` (code stays `issued`).

    `submit_rfa` transitions only add-target codes `pending_rfa → rfa_in_review`; remove-target codes are not transitioned by submission. Auto-draft regeneration on rejection / withdrawal regenerates from remaining `pending_rfa` codes per ADR-0031; remove-target codes do not contribute (they remain `issued`).

  **(4) Third WA origin via generalized `issue_wa`.** `issue_wa(bundle, payload)` handles both initial issuance and SCA-direct corrected amendment — same compound, internal dispatch on `bundle.head_version_seq IS NULL`. The compound populates the bundle's four SCA-supplied facts (ADR-0044: `contract_id`, `wa_number`, `service_id`, `job_number`), sets the WA's `issued_date` and `initialization_date`, runs code reconciliation. Reconciliation branches:
    - *Initial path* (no head): v0 in-place issuance per ADR-0048's clarification — v0's `state` flips `pending → issued`, dates populate, expected-code reconciliation per ADR-0022 (expected codes present on the WA → `issued`; absent → `pending_rfa`; unexpected codes on the WA → created in `issued`). No new WA row.
    - *SCA-direct amendment path* (head exists): new WA row at `version_seq = head + 1`, `state = issued`. Diff against the head WA's `WACodeAssignment` set:
      - Codes on both: no-op (the new version reaffirms them at `issued`).
      - Codes added on the new WA: created in `issued` state, attached to the bundle. New building-level codes carry `school_id` from the payload (constrained to `bundle.sites` per ADR-0048's invariant; a payload referencing a school not in `bundle.sites` is rejected at the command guard — structural fix is `edit_wabundle` adding the school first). `level` is denormalized at creation from `WACodeConf[code_type].default_level`.
      - Codes on the bundle in `expected` or `pending_rfa` that the new WA payload affirms: transition to `issued` (SCA fulfilled the request directly via the amendment).
      - Codes dropped from the new WA (i.e., in the prior head WA's set but not in the new payload): transition `issued → removed`, shared cascade per (5).
      - The prior head WA transitions `issued → superseded` per ADR-0030 (invariant preserved).

    **Hard-gate on the SCA-direct branch:** rejects if any RFA on the bundle is in `in_review` state. The structural-fix path is `reject_rfa` / `withdraw_rfa` first, then re-fire `issue_wa`. `draft` RFAs do not gate — they're derived state (auto-regenerate from `pending_rfa` codes after the amendment lands). Rationale: SCA's real-world workflow rejects/asks-to-withdraw before issuing; auto-withdrawing in-review RFAs at command time would model a non-occurring path and would silently nuke a coordinator's pending request if they mistakenly fired `issue_wa` on a freshly-submitted RFA's bundle. `approve_rfa` stays the firm-initiated amendment path, unchanged in shape — both paths produce v_{n+1} rows; they differ only in origin (externally-arrived vs. system-derived from RFA approval).

  **(5) Shared removal cascade under cascade-keep-FK** (ADR-0048 §4 principle, full mechanics here). Single internal routine invoked from three triggers:
    - `dismiss_wa_code`: code transitions `expected → dismissed` or `pending_rfa → dismissed`.
    - `approve_rfa`: per remove-target line item, code transitions `issued → removed`.
    - `issue_wa` SCA-direct branch: per diffed-dropped code, code transitions `issued → removed`.

    Mechanics (uniform across triggers):
    1. WA Code transitions to its terminal state (`dismissed` or `removed`); lifecycle-capture record written per ADR-0013 / ADR-0027.
    2. For each Time Entry with `wa_code_id == target.id`: emit one immutable `write_off` Note per ADR-0042 (cascade write-off, not separately guarded; inherits reason from the initiating command). The `wa_code` FK is **kept** — the dismissed / removed code stays referenceable in its terminal state, preserving the project-derivation chain `TE → WA Code → WABundle → Project` per ADR-0048 §4.
    3. For each Sample Batch with `wa_code_id == target.id`: same shape as (2). The `wa_code` FK is kept; the cascade emits a `write_off` Note on the batch.
    4. For each Deliverable whose WA Code is now `dismissed` or `removed` AND which has prepared documents or a submission attempt on record: emit a `write_off` Note (Deliverable enters the `wasted` derived-reporting-label per ADR-0029's extended trigger). Deliverables in `outstanding` with no prepared documents and no submission history hard-delete per ADR-0029's existing branch (extended symmetrically to both terminals).
    5. Closure-blocker shape: no new registry entry. Written-off TE / SB leave the not-written-off domain (ADR-0042); blocker-derivation predicates are computed over not-written-off entities, so a written-off TE / SB does not fire any registry blocker. The cascade does not open a new closure surface; it dissolves participation in existing ones.

    Cascade `write_off` Note shape (free-text `reason` + structural `references` pointer, matching ADR-0042's existing schema — no new fields):
    - `dismiss_wa_code`: `reason = "WA Code dismissed: <code_id>"` + (if `reason_text` supplied) `; <reason_text>`. `references` = the WA Code's dismissal lifecycle record.
    - `approve_rfa` (per remove-target): `reason = "WA Code removed via RFA <rfa_id>"`. `references` = the RFA.
    - `issue_wa` SCA-direct (per diffed-dropped code): `reason = "WA Code removed via SCA-direct amendment WA v<seq>"`. `references` = the new head WA.

  **(6) Blocker registry trim — formal removal of #1 and #2.** Both predicates (`wa_code = null` on TE or SB) are unfireable under the cascade-keep-FK principle plus WABundle's always-present property + missing-derived auto-generation (ADR-0048 §4): `wa_code = null` is no longer a producible state. The registry drops from 12 to 10 entries (gap-preserving numbering retained for trace continuity with ADR-0032 / ADR-0046; renumbering deferred to implementation phase if it ever earns its keep). ADR-0046's `default_resolve` Hybrid command's dispatch rows for #1 and #2 are retired. ADR-0047's predicate-table coverage is unaffected (the generic `default_resolve` row covers all remaining `has-default-resolution` entries — no row-level changes needed). Post-trim composition: 9 `has-default-resolution` (#3, #4, #5, #6, #7, #8, #9, #11, #12) + 1 `fix-only` (#10).

- **Status:** accepted
- **Context:** ADR-0048 (Step 6c-iii-b-i) fixed the cascade-keep-FK principle as a consequence of project-derivation through `wa_code` and deferred the full cascade mechanics + state-machine surgery + RFA hybrid line items + third WA origin + registry trim to this ADR (Step 6c-iii-b-ii). The shape of all six items was deliberated in session 14 (productive tangent off Step 6b-residual-2 sizing); this session is the ADR write-up. Five sub-decisions surfaced during write-prep and were resolved at the STOP-AND-CONFIRM gate before the write:
  - **(D1) Command surface for the third WA origin** — settled as generalizing `issue_wa` (not a separate `record_sca_amendment_wa`). Decisive reason: both externally-arrived paths share the same surrounding compound (bundle-fact population, per-version date setting, reconciliation against the code set) and differ only in reconciliation algorithm; the WA domain is about faithfully recording what SCA issued, so a user-intent dispatch axis doesn't exist. The version-chain marker (`bundle.head_version_seq IS NULL`) is a first-class structural field — branching on it inside one command is honest. `approve_rfa` is structurally distinct (firm-initiated, no external payload) and stays separate.
  - **(D2) Interaction with in-flight RFAs** — settled as hard-gate on `in_review` (not auto-withdraw). Decisive reason: SCA's real-world workflow rejects/asks-to-withdraw before issuing; auto-withdraw would model a non-occurring path while creating a footgun for tech-illiterate coordinators (a confused `issue_wa` invocation would silently nuke a freshly-submitted RFA). `draft` RFAs don't gate — they're derived state and regenerate after.
  - **(D3) Command shape for coordinator-authored remove line items** — settled as RFA-mediated `add_rfa_line_item(bundle, code, type)` with find-or-create draft semantics (not a code-side `request_code_removal`). Decisive reason: the explicit RFA-side surface forces the UI to render the amendment-cycle context, surfacing exactly the state mutation (draft materialization, line item appended to in-flight thing) that a tech-illiterate coordinator needs to see. The find-or-create at the bundle level keeps the coordinator's mental model single-step (the RFA is a record of current gaps between recorded entities and contracted WA scope — new-vs-existing doesn't matter).
  - **(D4) Line-item conflicts** — settled as guard-side rejection of `remove` targeting non-`issued` codes and add+remove on the same code in one RFA cycle. Decisive reason: `dismiss_wa_code` covers the conceptual operation for non-`issued` codes; admitting `remove` line items there is redundant. Add+remove on one cycle is self-cancelling line items with no operational justification.
  - **(D5) Cascade `write_off` Note shape** — settled as free-text `reason` + `references` pointer (no new schema fields). Decisive reason: ADR-0042's existing fields already cover the human-readable surface + structural anchor; adding `origin_command` / `origin_id` fields would be schema churn for no audit gain.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Keep `issued → dismissed` (let `dismiss_wa_code` cover the full removal axis).* Rejected — collapses two operationally distinct events. Pre-issuance dismissal is the coordinator retracting an expectation; post-issuance removal is recording SCA's action (via RFA approval or SCA-direct amendment). Two states, two audit stories, two predicate domains.
  - *Hard-delete on `dismiss_wa_code` of never-referenced codes (preserve ADR-0027's delete-substitution).* Rejected — the cascade-keep-FK principle's value is uniform behaviour; the lifecycle-capture record on every dismissal is cheap. Branching on "did anything ever reference this code" complicates the command and creates an audit-trail discontinuity for the never-referenced case.
  - *Separate command for SCA-direct amendments (`record_sca_amendment_wa`).* Rejected (D1) — the shared scaffolding (bundle facts, per-version dates, reconciliation against the code set) outweighs the differing reconciliation algorithm. Wrong-context calls become body-level guards rather than command-level dispatch — straightforward to enforce.
  - *Auto-withdraw in-flight RFAs on SCA-direct amendment.* Rejected (D2) — models a non-occurring real-world path; creates a silent-data-loss footgun for confused coordinators.
  - *Code-side `request_code_removal(code)` command.* Rejected (D3) — hides RFA-draft materialization from a tech-illiterate coordinator; the UI cannot reliably surface "you're appending to an existing in-flight amendment cycle" if the command operates on the code rather than the RFA.
  - *Permit `remove` line items on non-`issued` codes.* Rejected (D4) — `dismiss_wa_code` already covers the conceptual operation for `expected` / `pending_rfa` codes.
  - *Machine-readable `origin_command` + `origin_id` fields on cascade `write_off` Notes.* Rejected (D5) — `reason` + `references` already cover.
  - *Coordinator-authored adds via `add_rfa_line_item(..., type: add)` as the primary path.* Rejected — additions are unambiguously derivable from code state; admitting coordinator-authored adds as a normal-flow path creates two routes to the same line item with drift risk. The discriminator admits `type = add` for narrow recovery paths only; ADR-0031's "additions are system-derived" stance is preserved on the add axis.
  - *Intermediate `removal_in_review` state on WA Code for codes targeted by a remove line item.* Rejected — the code is functionally still `issued` during review (work continues, billing aggregates, blockers fire normally); an intermediate state would force every read predicate to handle a third case for no operational benefit.
- **Consequences:**
  - **WA Code state machine (amends ADR-0027).** States: `expected`, `pending_rfa`, `rfa_in_review`, `issued`, `budget_rfa_needed` (deferred placeholder), `dismissed`, **`removed` (new)**. Transitions:
    - `expected → issued`: `issue_wa` reconciliation (initial path; expected code present on the WA).
    - `expected → pending_rfa`: `issue_wa` reconciliation (initial path; expected code absent from the WA).
    - `expected → issued`: `issue_wa` SCA-direct branch (post-issuance, when an amendment WA affirms a previously-expected code).
    - `expected → dismissed`: `dismiss_wa_code`.
    - `pending_rfa → rfa_in_review`: `submit_rfa` (per add-target line item).
    - `pending_rfa → issued`: `issue_wa` SCA-direct branch (when the new WA payload affirms a `pending_rfa` code).
    - `pending_rfa → dismissed`: `dismiss_wa_code`.
    - `rfa_in_review → issued`: `approve_rfa` (per add-target).
    - `rfa_in_review → pending_rfa`: `reject_rfa` / `withdraw_rfa` (per add-target).
    - `issued → removed`: `approve_rfa` (per remove-target) or `issued → removed` via `issue_wa` SCA-direct branch (per diffed-dropped code). Shared cascade fires per (5).
    - `issued → budget_rfa_needed` and back: deferred per ADR-0027.

    **Dropped from ADR-0027:** `issued → dismissed`. **Terminals:** `dismissed` and `removed` (no outbound transitions). The cascade step "(2) nulls `wa_code` on referencing TE / SB" is retired in full and replaced by the keep-FK + `write_off` Note mechanics in (5).
  - **`dismiss_wa_code` signature.** `dismiss_wa_code(wa_code, reason_text?)`. Predicate: `role >= coordinator` (ADR-0047 Cluster 3, unchanged). Optional `reason_text` lands as an `audit_reason` Note (ADR-0040) attached to the lifecycle-capture record. Pre-condition: `wa_code.state ∈ {expected, pending_rfa}` (`rfa_in_review` remains locked per ADR-0027; `issued` redirects the coordinator to the RFA-remove or SCA-direct paths).
  - **`add_rfa_line_item(bundle, code, type)` command.** New coordinator-facing command. Predicate: `role >= coordinator` (inherits ADR-0047 Cluster 3 class rule for the WA / WA Code / RFA cluster; no explicit row needed). Find-or-create semantics: if the bundle has no open `draft` RFA, create one and append the line item; if a `draft` exists, append. Guards: `type = remove` ⇒ `code.state = issued`; reject if any existing line item on the open draft already targets `code`. Does not transition any WA Code state — line-item creation is RFA-side; code transitions fire only at submit / approve / reject / withdraw boundaries.
  - **`approve_rfa` composition** (amends ADR-0031). Was: Amendment WA's code set = `(prior WA's codes) ∪ (RFA line items)`. Becomes: `(prior WA's codes ∪ add-target line items) \ remove-target line items`. Cascade per (5) fires per remove-target line item atomically with the `approve_rfa` compound's other effects (Amendment WA creation at `version_seq = head + 1`, WA Code state transitions, Deliverable cascade, prior-WA supersession, RFA → `approved`).
  - **`issue_wa` generalization** (amends ADR-0030, ADR-0044). Signature unchanged: `issue_wa(bundle, payload)`. Internal dispatch on `bundle.head_version_seq IS NULL` per (4). The compound now writes per the SCA-direct amendment branch when a head exists: new WA row at `version_seq = head + 1`, prior head transitions `issued → superseded`, diff cascade fires per (5) for any dropped codes. **Hard-gate on the SCA-direct branch:** rejects if `∃ rfa : rfa.bundle == bundle AND rfa.state == in_review`. `draft` RFAs do not gate. The `payload` carries per-code `school_id` for any building-level codes (constrained to `bundle.sites`); a payload referencing a school not in `bundle.sites` is rejected at the command guard.
  - **`wasted` re-derivation** (amends ADR-0029). Trigger extends from `WA Code is dismissed` to `WA Code is dismissed OR removed`. Hard-delete branch (no prepared documents + no submission history) extends symmetrically. The `wasted` derivation otherwise unchanged — `wasted` ⟺ Deliverable has a `write_off` Note (per ADR-0042's reframe). The cascade in (5).4 writes that Note.
  - **`relink_sample_batch_wa_code` guard** (amends ADR-0033). Permitted-state set extends from `{wa_code IS null, current code dismissed, batch trips #9}` (post-ADR-0048 + ADR-0046 Fork A) to `{current code dismissed OR removed, batch trips #9}` — the `wa_code IS null` branch is dropped (unfireable post-ADR-0048). The `removed` branch composes independently with Fork A.
  - **Blocker registry — 12 → 10 entries.** Formal removal of #1 (TE `wa_code = null`) and #2 (SB `wa_code = null`). Gap-preserving numbering. Post-trim canonical table:

    | # | Blocker | Classification | Target | Command shape | Compound names | Chain |
    |---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
    | 3 | Sample Batch Lab Report ∈ {`missing`, `invalid`} at closure | has-default-resolution | Sample Batch | generic | — | — |
    | 4 | Sample Batch COC `missing` at closure | has-default-resolution | Sample Batch | generic | — | — |
    | 5 | Time Entry no `daily_log` at closure | has-default-resolution | Time Entry | generic | — | `te_batches_by_coverage` |
    | 6 | DepFiling required-doc `missing` at closure | has-default-resolution | DepFiling | generic | — | — |
    | 7 | Open `draft`/`in_review` RFA at closure (add/remove RFA, MVP) | has-default-resolution | RFA | named-compound | [`resolve_open_rfa`] | — |
    | 8 | Cross-project time overlap on Employee | has-default-resolution | (paired Time Entries) | named-compound | [`resolve_overlap`, `resolve_overlap_paired`] | `te_batches_by_coverage` |
    | 9 | Sample collection time not in employee net on-site time | has-default-resolution | Sample Batch | generic | — | — |
    | 10 | Project's non-terminal RFP not in `saved` state at closure | **fix-only** | — | — | — | — |
    | 11 | Time Entry `(employee, role_type, contract, date)` not covered by EmployeeRole | has-default-resolution | Time Entry | generic | — | `te_batches_by_coverage` |
    | 12 | Time Entry dated before head WA's `initialization_date` | has-default-resolution | Time Entry | generic | — | `te_batches_by_coverage` |

    9 `has-default-resolution` + 1 `fix-only`. ADR-0046's `default_resolve` dispatch retires the #1 / #2 rows. ADR-0047's predicate coverage unchanged. Pattern #12 (chain-dismissal) unchanged in mechanism — `te_batches_by_coverage` operates on Time Entry targets via direct `write_off` Notes on chained batches; the per-record cascade effect from this ADR's shared cascade (5) is keep-FK + `write_off` Note (consistent with ADR-0048's principle).
  - **Amendments to other ADRs.**
    - **ADR-0027 (WA Code state machine + dismiss cascade).** State machine: `removed` terminal added; `issued → dismissed` dropped; `dismiss_wa_code` narrowed to `{expected, pending_rfa}` targets; optional `reason_text` parameter added. Cascade: step (2) "nulls `wa_code`" retired in full (per ADR-0048 §4 + this ADR's (5)); replaced by keep-FK + cascade `write_off` Note on each referencing TE / SB. Delete-substitution branch dropped — `dismiss_wa_code` always transitions and writes the lifecycle-capture record. Design pattern #9 (delete-or-dismiss gate) no longer exercised by WA Code; pattern itself stands for other entities.
    - **ADR-0029 (Deliverable `wasted` flag).** Trigger extends `dismissed → (dismissed OR removed)`. Hard-delete branch extends symmetrically. `wasted` derivation otherwise unchanged (per ADR-0042's reframe — `wasted` ⟺ `write_off` Note on the Deliverable).
    - **ADR-0030 (WA state machine + origins).** `issue_wa` generalized to handle SCA-direct corrected amendments. Internal branch on bundle head presence runs diff reconciliation against the prior head; produces v_{n+1} at `state = issued`; prior head transitions `issued → superseded`. State machine itself (`pending` / `issued` / `superseded`) unchanged. v0 in-place issuance (clarified by ADR-0048) unchanged.
    - **ADR-0031 (RFA hybrid line-item model).** Line items gain `type: add | remove | budget` discriminator (budget deferred). Coordinators author `remove` line items via `add_rfa_line_item(bundle, code, type)` (find-or-create draft); additions stay system-derived in normal flow. `approve_rfa` composition: `(prior ∪ adds) \ removes`. Polymorphic resolution per the Decision (3). `submit_rfa` transitions only add-target codes to `rfa_in_review`. Empty-draft hard-delete unchanged. Auto-draft regeneration unchanged in mechanism (regenerates from remaining `pending_rfa` codes; remove-targets don't contribute — they're already `issued`).
    - **ADR-0033 (Sample Batch / relink guard).** `relink_sample_batch_wa_code` permitted-state set: `{current code dismissed OR removed, batch trips #9}`. The `wa_code IS null` branch dropped. The `removed` branch composes independently with Fork A.
    - **ADR-0042 (write-off model) / ADR-0046 (registry).** Full cascade restatement under keep-FK: the cascade from `dismiss_wa_code` and from the shared removal cascade (3 triggers) keeps the `wa_code` FK on referencing TE / SB and emits `write_off` Notes with the shape in (5). Blocker registry trimmed to 10 entries (#1, #2 removed). ADR-0046's `default_resolve` dispatch retires the #1 / #2 rows. Remaining 9 `has-default-resolution` + 1 `fix-only` entries unchanged.
    - **ADR-0044 (WABundle, `issue_wa`).** `issue_wa` extension restated: in addition to the WABundle four-fact population at initial issuance, the SCA-direct branch operates on a bundle with an existing head, producing v_{n+1}. The hard-gate against `in_review` RFAs on the bundle is a new pre-condition on the SCA-direct branch only. WABundle schema, audit log, and `edit_wabundle` unchanged.
    - **ADR-0047 (predicate table).** No row-level changes. `dismiss_wa_code`'s `reason_text?` parameter is a signature change, not a predicate change (row stays `role >= coordinator`). `add_rfa_line_item` inherits Cluster 3 class rule (`role >= coordinator`); no explicit row needed. `issue_wa`'s SCA-direct branch inherits the existing `issue_wa` row.
  - **Cumulative-tables update (`handoff.md`).** WA Code state machine: `removed` terminal added; transitions table refreshed. Vocabulary: `removed` (WA Code terminal), `add_rfa_line_item`, RFA line-item `type` discriminator, generalized `issue_wa` with SCA-direct branch + hard-gate, the cascade `write_off` Note `reason` / `references` shape. Blocker registry: 12 → 10 entries (#1, #2 formally removed; gap-preserving numbering).
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **`revoke_write_off` command shape.** Predicate `role >= coordinator` (ADR-0047). Parameters and guards still undefined. No home step (candidate: alongside `split_entry`, Step 6d or a residual). Notable operational case post-keep-FK: revoking a write-off on a TE / SB whose `wa_code` is in a terminal state re-exposes the entity to billing while still pointing at a dismissed / removed code (which still resolves bundle → project structurally). UI mitigation is implementation-phase work.
  - **Revoke-line-item command shape** (rescinding a coordinator-authored `remove` line item before approval). Symmetric with empty-draft hard-delete: if rescinding the only line item on a coordinator-opened draft, the draft hard-deletes. Parameters and guards undefined; carry-forward.
  - **`split_entry` command shape** (load-bearing for ADR-0046's `resolve_overlap` compounds). Unchanged from ADR-0042 / ADR-0046 carry-forward — no home step.
  - **Budget-typed RFA line items.** Deferred behind budget tracking. When introduced, ADR-0027's `budget_rfa_needed` state activates; `approve_rfa` composition extends; #7 may need reclassification per ADR-0046's note.
  - **`reassign_wa_project` deeper mechanics.** Unchanged from ADR-0048 carry-forward — implementation-phase.
  - **Smart-command-inference state for codes created post-initial-issuance** (when a TE / SB references an `(sample_type, school)` that doesn't exist on the bundle's head WA). Post-ADR-0048 the code is auto-generated rather than left `wa_code = null`; the state in which it lands (`expected` vs. `pending_rfa`) is implementation-phase, but the SCA-direct branch's reconciliation handles either case (codes on the bundle in `expected` or `pending_rfa` that the new payload affirms → `issued`).

---

## ADR-0050 — MVP scope: 6 must-have features, ship the unique mechanics, defer speculative surface

- **Date:** 2026-05-15
- **Decision:** The MVP feature cut for `sca-tracker` lands at **6 must-have features** (under the ≤7 ceiling of Step 7's brief): (1) Project lifecycle; (2) WA + WA Codes + RFA cycle; (3) Time Entries + Sample Batches; (4) Documents + Deliverables + DepFilings; (5) Closure gate + blockers + write-off (including polymorphic Notes substrate); (6) Roster + role administration. The "not now" list folds in the full `post-mvp.md` catalog plus authorization/role surface deferrals, billing-adjacent deferrals, and model/config-evolution deferrals. One in-MVP carve-out is flagged as slip-eligible (`resolve_overlap_paired`). Seven command-shape carry-forwards stay in MVP but have their mechanics pinned in the implementation phase. The full cut, with per-item rationale, lives in `planning/mvp.md`.
- **Status:** accepted
- **Context:** Step 7 of the Conceptualization phase. Inputs were the rolled-up domain in `planning/domain-model.md` (21 entities, 14 design patterns, 10-entry blocker registry post-ADR-0049 trim, four-role authorization chain), the post-MVP holding pen `planning/post-mvp.md`, the full ADR log (ADR-0001 through ADR-0049), and the step brief in `planning/steps.md` § Step 7. The cut surface spans the whole domain because every entity contributes potential features — the question was not which entities ship but which features within each entity cluster ship.

  Three load-bearing forks framed the cut:

  - **(D1) Proof-of-concept purpose.** Three honest archetypes: (a) end-to-end vertical slice (cut depth for breadth — coordinator can run one project create → close, but unique mechanics thinned to demonstrate flow); (b) "hard parts" demonstrator (ship the unique mechanics — closure gate, blockers, write-off, RFA cycle — concede peripheral CRUD/UX may be rough); (c) usable internal tool (whatever set lets the agency actually start tracking real projects today). Settled **(b) + (c)**: the MVP audience is the user's own office, to be usable for new projects at introduction. (c) covers what the office tracks today; (b) covers the hard parts of (c). End-to-end paths must exist for every must-have (no half-wired features). Speculative surface — features no one at the office uses today — gets cut.
  - **(D2) RFA + amendment cycle in MVP?** Three sub-forks: (a) full cycle in (RFA entity + hybrid `add`/`remove` line items + `approve_rfa` / `reject_rfa` / `withdraw_rfa` + third WA origin + `removed` state + cascade-keep-FK across three triggers); (b) initial issuance only (no RFA entity; WA versioning collapsed; `removed` state gone); (c) RFA in, third WA origin out (drop SCA-direct branch only). Settled **(a)**: both RFA and SCA-direct issuance are common real cases at the office. (b) was off the table under D1's "tracked at the office today" test — the office tracks WAs over their amendment lifetime today. (c) was the only honest sub-question and was answered "keep in" — the SCA-direct branch is the same generalized `issue_wa` command with a different dispatch arm; incremental MVP cost is tiny once the design is paid.
  - **(D3) Closure gate + blocker registry + default-resolution in MVP?** Three sub-forks: (a) full stack in (10-entry registry + lazy materialization + `default_resolve` + named compounds `resolve_open_rfa` / `resolve_overlap` / `resolve_overlap_paired` + `revoke_write_off` + chain-dismissal `te_batches_by_coverage`); (b) closure gate + blockers in, default-resolution family out (only resolution path is structural fix; no write-off model); (c) all deferred (project closes whenever clicked). Settled **(a)**: ADR-0046 was the most-deliberated single piece of work in the phase, and the write-off model is what makes blockers honest — "fix-only" without a default-resolution path is a lie because the real-world acceptance path always exists (just off-system, unauditable). (b) ships a tool that forces the office to either lie ("mark something fixed when it isn't") or never close (manual override outside the system). (c) was off the table — would silently let projects close with `missing` Lab Reports and open RFAs. Carve-out flagged: `resolve_overlap_paired` may slip post-MVP if `split_entry`'s mechanics don't land in early implementation (single-row carve-out, not a fork).

  Three carve-outs were explicitly confirmed (rather than left implicit):

  - **(C1) Multi-contract in MVP.** `Contract` entity (ADR-0043) + per-`(employee, role_type, contract)` rate resolution (ADR-0045) + `Contract.code_flat_fee_schedule`. **Kept.** ADR-0043's driver was that the office just signed a second contract — immediately relevant, not speculative.
  - **(C2) All four roles in MVP.** `superadmin` / `admin` / `coordinator` / `auditor`. **All kept.** Auditor is read-only and cheap; admin is required for `edit_wabundle` (ADR-0044) + roster CRUD (ADR-0040). Per-project coordinator scoping stays explicitly post-MVP per existing chain-freeze framing (ADR-0047 locked clarification 1).
  - **(C3) DepFiling in MVP.** Self-contained regulatory filing surface (ADR-0023) — TRU + editable `required_doc_types` + 7 ACP/VAR doc types feeding into it. **Kept.** Parallel evidence track to Deliverables; the office files these with regulators today.

  The final cut was canvassed against the ≤7 ceiling and landed at 6 by folding Notes commentary into feature #5 (its load-bearing surfaces are the immutable Note subtypes for `write_off` / `blocker` / `resolution` / `audit_reason`, all already implied by features #5 and #6).
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Vertical-slice MVP (D1=a).* Rejected — under D1's settled "tracked at the office today" framing, this would ship a thin tracker that doesn't cover what the office does. The conceptualization phase invested ~30 ADRs in unique mechanics specifically because they reflect operational reality; cutting them defeats both the design effort and the office-usability goal.
  - *Initial-issuance-only WA (D2=b).* Rejected — the office handles RFA-driven amendments and SCA-direct corrected amendments as routine operations; first-WA-only would strand half the entity surface (RFA, third origin, `removed` state, hybrid line items) and force out-of-band handling for routine events.
  - *Closure gate without default-resolution (D3=b).* Rejected — without `default_resolve` + write-off, the closure gate forces the office to either lie ("structural fix" the issue without fixing it) or never close (override outside the system). Either defeats closure-readiness; default-resolution's incremental cost over (b) is one command family + one Note subtype + one cascade (already wired by ADR-0049).
  - *No closure gate (D3=c).* Rejected — silently allows close with `missing` Lab Reports, open RFAs, uncovered Time Entries. Closure-readiness is the unique trust mechanic distinguishing this tool from a generic tracker.
  - *7-feature cut breaking out polymorphic Notes as feature #7.* Considered and rejected — Notes' user-facing surface is thin (creator-editable commentary), and its load-bearing surfaces are subtype-based and already implied by features #5 (write-off, blocker, resolution) and #6 (audit_reason on grant/revoke). Breaking it out as #7 would over-count infrastructure as a feature.
  - *7-feature cut breaking out an "audit / history" feature.* Considered and rejected — history capture is substrate per `logic.md`'s pipeline; users don't "use" the history pipeline as a feature. Per-entity history-pattern selection is implicit in each feature's entity cluster.
  - *Drop Contract / multi-contract from MVP (lift C1).* Rejected — the office signed a second contract during conceptualization; rates and code default flat fees now resolve through `Contract`. Lifting C1 would force MVP to operate against an implicit single-contract assumption that's already false.
  - *Drop `auditor` and `admin` to coordinator-only (lift C2).* Rejected — `admin` is required for `edit_wabundle` (ADR-0044's post-issuance correction path) and roster CRUD (ADR-0040 Cluster 1); `auditor` is read-only and cheap. The chain is already designed; collapsing it adds work to a future implementation phase.
  - *Drop DepFiling from MVP (lift C3).* Rejected — DepFiling is the regulatory filing surface; the office files these with regulators today. It's a parallel track to Deliverables, not a duplicate, and the entity is shallow (TRU + project ref + editable `required_doc_types`).
- **Consequences:**
  - **`planning/mvp.md` written.** The full feature list, per-item expansion, the categorized "not now" list with rationale, the single `resolve_overlap_paired` carve-out, the command-shape carry-forwards (split_entry, revoke_write_off, revoke-line-item, reassign_wa_project deeper mechanics, ContractorEngagement signatures, ADR-0031 auto-draft regeneration suppression, smart-command-inference landing state), and the pointer block all land in `mvp.md`. `mvp.md` is now the canonical MVP-scope reference; `post-mvp.md` is consumed as a holding pen (retained for record).
  - **`post-mvp.md` superseded as the active holding pen.** All entries from `post-mvp.md` are folded verbatim into `mvp.md` § Not now. New post-MVP candidates that surface in implementation-phase work should append to `mvp.md` § Not now (or its successor) rather than re-opening `post-mvp.md`. `post-mvp.md` itself is retained for trace continuity; no future updates expected.
  - **Step 7 ✓ complete.** Next is **Step 8 — stack & architecture**. Inputs: `mvp.md`, `framework.md`, `logic.md`, `history-patterns.md`, `decisions.md`, `handoff.md`. Step 8 picks the stack and the architectural shape; resolves the history implementation shape (event store vs. append-only tables vs. temporal tables) informed by Step 5's pattern menu and the per-entity history-pattern assignments rolled up in `domain-model.md`.
  - **D1's "office-usability" framing carries forward as the MVP-scope decision rule.** Future MVP-scope deliberations (e.g., implementation-phase decisions on whether a feature ships in v1 or v1.1) inherit the test: "is this tracked at the office today?" Speculative surface gets cut even if it's modeled.
  - **Carve-out tracking.** `resolve_overlap_paired` requires `split_entry`'s mechanics to land in early implementation. If implementation surfaces that `split_entry` is heavier than estimated (split-point ergonomics, field-inheritance, batch reassignment at boundary — none designed yet), `resolve_overlap_paired` slips post-MVP and `mvp.md` § Carve-outs gets a follow-up note. `resolve_overlap` (single-side) ships either way.
  - **Command-shape carry-forwards.** The 7 items in `mvp.md` § Command-shape carry-forwards are *in MVP* (predicate-table rows in ADR-0047) but their full signatures and guards are pinned in the implementation phase. They are distinct from "not now" — implementation-phase work is responsible for landing them.
  - **No new entities, no new ADR amendments, no new design patterns.** Step 7 is a scope decision; the model is unchanged. The entity roster stays at 21; the design pattern catalog stays at 14; the blocker registry stays at 10.
  - **Conceptualization phase nearing close.** Remaining: Step 8 (stack & architecture) → Step 9 (data model sketch + roadmap + phase-transition ADR + pre-transition ADR consolidation pass for ADRs with 2+ amendments).
- **Amendments to other ADRs:** None. ADR-0050 is a scope decision; the model state at the close of ADR-0049 is unchanged.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **`resolve_overlap_paired` slip risk** — tracked in `mvp.md` § Carve-outs; revisit in implementation phase when `split_entry`'s mechanics surface.
  - **Command-shape carry-forwards** — 7 items tracked in `mvp.md` § Command-shape carry-forwards; mechanics pinned in implementation phase.
  - **Pre-transition ADR consolidation pass** — Step 9 responsibility; scan `decisions.md` for ADRs with 2+ amendments and consolidate before the phase-transition ADR lands.

---

## ADR-0051 — Runtime stack: Python/FastAPI backend + TypeScript/React frontend on PaaS-monolith deployment

- **Date:** 2026-05-15
- **Decision:** The runtime stack for `sca-tracker` lands at three coupled sub-decisions, bundled because the language choice rules in/out most framework and deployment options. **(D1) Language/runtime:** Python 3.12+ on CPython for the backend; TypeScript on Node for frontend tooling. **(D2) Web/app framework:** FastAPI on the backend with SQLAlchemy 2.0 + Alembic + Pydantic + Ruff + Pytest; React on the frontend with Vite + TanStack Router + TanStack Query + openapi-ts (FastAPI's OpenAPI schema generates typed TanStack Query hooks) + Storybook + ESLint + Prettier. Routes are transport; a thin `Command` base class + dispatcher (design carried to implementation phase) hosts the pipeline from `logic.md`. **(D3) Deployment shape:** Monolith container on a managed PaaS (vendor TBD at implementation kickoff); static SPA on the same platform's CDN; DB connection config-driven from env with **Neon free-tier Postgres as the dev default on both work machines** and **SQLite as offline fallback**; CI runs the integration test suite against Postgres (Neon ephemeral branch per PR or docker-compose Postgres in the runner); engine-specific features (Postgres JSONB ops, etc.) live behind a documented adapter boundary, not strewn through repository code.
- **Status:** accepted
- **Context:** Step 8a of the Conceptualization phase, the first half of Step 8 after the partition agreed 2026-05-15 (Step 8b will pick persistence engine + history-impl shape + draft `planning/architecture.md`). Inputs were `mvp.md` (the cut — defines what the stack must support), `framework.md` (entity/value/relationship/identity vocabulary), `logic.md` (the command pipeline: commands as named operations per ADR-0007, mandatory atomic state-mutation/history-capture per ADR-0008, declarative cross-cutting concerns — lifecycle per ADR-0009, well-formedness invariants per ADR-0010, authorization per ADR-0012), and `decisions.md` (esp. ADR-0001's stale-scaffolding stance — existing `backend/` and `frontend/` directories treated as stale and unconstrained for stack choices).

  Three sub-decisions framed the bundle:

  - **(D1) Language/runtime.** Candidates canvassed: (a) TypeScript on Node.js (strongest type-system fit for the declarative-pipeline story via discriminated unions + exhaustive matching + branded UUIDs; largest framework ecosystem; FE-BE type sharing in one language); (b) Python 3.12+ on CPython (mature web stack; Pydantic as the most honest declarative-validation substrate in any mainstream language; SQLAlchemy 2.0 + Alembic the most battle-tested ORM + migration combo in any language); (c) TypeScript on Bun/Deno (same type story as a, less mature deployment surface). Non-candidates ruled out at canvass head: Rust/Go (overweight for office-internal MVP), C#/JVM (toolchain overhead heavy for office-internal), Elixir/Phoenix (excellent fit for the command pipeline but ecosystem and operator-familiarity costs). Settled **(b)** after honest comparison of the agent's initial (a)-recommendation against the user's pre-existing (b)-proposal — the openapi-ts → TanStack Query pipeline cancels the FE-BE-type-sharing argument for (a); Pydantic does runtime validation more honestly than zod (schema *is* the validator, not a parallel layer); Alembic's migration maturity is non-trivial. The residual TS edge — discriminated-union exhaustiveness for command modeling — is mitigatable in Python with Pydantic discriminated unions + `match`/`case` + a base `Command` class hierarchy + `assert_never` helpers.
  - **(D2) Web/app framework.** Backend candidates: (a) FastAPI (async-by-default; dependency injection is a natural mount point for the pipeline's cross-cutting concerns; Pydantic models double as command-payload schemas); (b) Django (batteries-included; admin UI is essentially free for the roster/role-admin MVP feature; heavier and more opinionated); (c) plain Starlette/Flask (lighter than FastAPI, weaker validation story without bolting Pydantic on separately). Frontend candidates: (a) Vite + TanStack Router + TanStack Query + openapi-ts (type-safe routing, server-state caching matched to the command/state-change shape, no framework bloat); (b) Next.js (full-stack TS, RSC + middleware + caching machinery — overkill for an internal tool); (c) Remix (similar to Next.js, less opinionated). Settled FastAPI on the backend and Vite + TanStack on the frontend — Django's admin-UI win doesn't outweigh its heaviness for an MVP where the admin surface is small and well-bounded; Next.js's complexity is unjustified at this audience size.
  - **(D3) Deployment shape.** Three axes: monolith vs. service split (settled monolith — 21 entities + office-internal + small user base = zero service-split rationale), container vs. serverless (settled container — serverless cold-start latency hits UX daily for sporadic office use; pooling and background-job primitives add complexity that doesn't pay back at this scale), managed vs. self-hosted (settled managed PaaS — major-cloud-direct AWS/GCP overengineers ops; self-hosted VPS makes the user the sysadmin for backups/patching/TLS/monitoring; PaaS captures 90% of operational wins at ~10% of major-cloud ops cost). Dev DB tooling: user's initial preference was env-driven config with SQLite-as-no-config-default; revised after honest pushback on dev/prod parity (SQLite is effectively single-writer — concurrency-isolation bugs in the cross-entity-invariant story per ADR-0010 won't manifest in SQLite dev *at all*; engine-specific features diverge; migration parity is imperfect). Final shape: Neon free-tier Postgres as default on both dev machines (each machine on its own Neon branch — Neon's branching primitive makes this clean); SQLite preserved as offline-only fallback (Machine B is Docker-locked but has internet, so Neon is the working default there). CI tests against Postgres. Engine-specific code behind adapter boundary so the SQLite-fallback path stays buildable.

- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Bundle as three separate ADRs (0051 lang, 0052 framework, 0053 deployment).* Rejected — the three decisions are coupled (lang rules in/out framework and deployment); ADR-0009/0010/0012's three-way split was structurally justified by different declaration surfaces (state machine / entity / command), which this triple does not share. One bundled ADR avoids restating the coupling three times.
  - *TypeScript on Node end-to-end (the agent's initial recommendation).* Rejected after honest comparison — openapi-ts + Pydantic together cancel the two strongest TS arguments (FE-BE type sharing, declarative validation); SQLAlchemy 2.0 + Alembic's migration maturity meaningfully exceeds Drizzle/Prisma; the residual TS advantage (command-pipeline exhaustiveness at type-check time) is mitigatable in Python with discipline (Pydantic discriminated unions + `assert_never` + `Command` base class).
  - *Django backend.* Rejected — admin UI is a real win but admin surface for MVP is small and well-bounded (roster CRUD + role admin); Django's request/response handling, ORM, and template machinery is heavier than FastAPI's, with less natural fit for the command-pipeline shape.
  - *Next.js frontend.* Rejected — RSC + middleware + caching machinery is genuinely overkill for an internal tool; user's "bloat" concern is operationally correct at this audience size.
  - *Service-split backend.* Rejected — no scaling pressure, no team-cadence pressure, no isolation pressure at MVP scale. Service splits are a cost paid for benefits that don't exist here.
  - *Serverless (Lambda via Mangum, Cloud Run).* Rejected — cold-start latency (~1–3s on Cloud Run for Python; worse on Lambda for FastAPI) hits user experience every morning and after every long meeting gap; connection pooling against Postgres needs a pooler; background jobs need separate primitives. Cost savings don't justify the daily UX tax.
  - *Major-cloud-direct deployment (AWS ECS/Fargate or GCP Cloud Run with full IAM/VPC/IaC overhead).* Rejected — IAM, VPCs, security groups, load balancer config, IaC state files, and per-tweak console/CLI tax at MVP scale is weeks of plumbing the user wouldn't get any benefit from. Migration path from PaaS-container to major cloud is config, not architecture, so this isn't burning a bridge.
  - *Self-hosted on a VPS with Docker Compose.* Rejected — savings ($5–20/month vs. PaaS) don't justify becoming the sysadmin for backups, OS patching, TLS renewal, log rotation, and monitoring on an internal tool that needs to be reliable for the office.
  - *SQLite-as-dev-default with per-feature tracking of what's been Postgres-validated.* Rejected — tracking discipline is real overhead that decays under momentum pressure; concurrency-bug class won't surface in SQLite *ever*, so "tested on SQLite" gives false confidence on the ADR-0010 invariant story; two-machine handoff makes it worse (changes on the SQLite machine can't be Postgres-validated until physically back at the Docker machine). Neon free-tier resolves the underlying constraint (Machine B is Docker-locked, not offline) at $0/month.
  - *Pin a specific PaaS vendor now (Fly.io / Render / Railway).* Rejected — vendor pick decides on operational primitives (per-platform secrets shape, per-platform cron, region-control story) that don't yet have load-bearing context. Vendor research belongs at implementation-phase kickoff when the choice is actually exercised.

- **Consequences:**
  - **Backend stack pinned.** Python 3.12+ on CPython; FastAPI; SQLAlchemy 2.0 ORM with Alembic migrations; Pydantic for request/response/command-payload schemas and well-formedness invariants (ADR-0010); Ruff (lint + format); Pytest (unit + integration).
  - **Frontend stack pinned.** TypeScript; React; Vite (dev server + bundler); TanStack Router (type-safe client-side routing); TanStack Query (server-state caching, generated from FastAPI's OpenAPI schema via openapi-ts); Storybook (component dev); ESLint + Prettier (lint + format). Testing library TBD at implementation kickoff (Vitest + React Testing Library is the obvious default but not pinned here).
  - **FE-BE contract pipeline.** FastAPI generates an OpenAPI schema; openapi-ts consumes it to generate typed TanStack Query hooks. The schema is the contract; types stay in sync automatically.
  - **Command pipeline hosting.** FastAPI routes are the transport layer; a thin `Command` base class + dispatcher (carried to implementation phase) hosts the pipeline from `logic.md`. Routes call into commands; routes are not commands. This pins the structural separation now so implementation doesn't conflate them.
  - **Deployment shape pinned.** Monolith FastAPI container deployed to a managed PaaS (vendor TBD); static SPA built by Vite and deployed to the same platform's CDN; managed RDBMS-class DB on the same platform. Specific vendor (Fly.io / Render / Railway / similar) deferred to implementation kickoff.
  - **Dev DB workflow.** Both machines default to Neon free-tier Postgres (each machine = its own branch off `main`). SQLite preserved as offline-only fallback via the env-config loader (empty `DATABASE_URL` → local gitignored SQLite file). CI runs integration tests against Postgres (Neon ephemeral branch per PR is the cleanest option; docker-compose Postgres in the runner is the fallback).
  - **Engine-portability discipline.** App code uses SQLAlchemy core types and portable SQL idioms by default. Engine-specific features (Postgres JSONB ops, full-text search, advisory locks, etc.) sit behind a documented adapter boundary — never strewn through repository code. This keeps the SQLite fallback buildable and keeps the door open if Step 8b's persistence pick wants a non-Postgres engine (unlikely, but not foreclosed here).
  - **`backend/` and `frontend/` directories.** Per ADR-0001, the existing scaffolding is stale and will be cleared (or repurposed) at the start of the implementation phase. The stack pinned here is unconstrained by what's currently in those directories.
  - **Step 8b inherits one constraint:** the persistence engine must be a SQLAlchemy-supported RDBMS-class engine with a managed offering on the chosen PaaS, *and* must support concurrency primitives strong enough for the ADR-0010 cross-entity-invariant-revalidation requirement. Postgres is overwhelmingly likely; this ADR does not foreclose alternatives but does foreclose any engine that breaks the dev-config/SQLite-fallback model or the ADR-0010 isolation requirement.
  - **Step 8a complete.** Remaining in Conceptualization: **Step 8b** (persistence + history-impl shape + `planning/architecture.md`) → **Step 9** (data model sketch + roadmap + phase-transition ADR + pre-transition ADR consolidation pass for ADRs with 2+ amendments).

- **Amendments to other ADRs:** None. ADR-0001's stale-scaffolding stance is honored (consequence above); the framework, logic, history-patterns, MVP-scope, and domain ADRs are all unchanged by this stack pick.

- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Specific PaaS vendor pick.** Implementation-phase kickoff; revisit Fly.io / Render / Railway against criteria that emerge then (region/data-residency story, secrets management ergonomics, log aggregation, cost-at-actual-usage).
  - **`Command` base class + dispatcher design.** Implementation phase; pins the structural split between routes-as-transport and commands-as-unit-of-change. Pipeline order from `logic.md` (auth → lifecycle → apply → invariants → commit) is the spec.
  - **Frontend test runner pick.** Implementation-phase kickoff (Vitest + React Testing Library is the default; not pinned here).
  - **Stale-scaffolding cleanup.** Implementation-phase opening session: clear or repurpose `backend/` and `frontend/` directories per ADR-0001.
  - **Persistence engine + history-impl shape + `architecture.md`.** Step 8b (next session).

---

## ADR-0052 — Data layer: PostgreSQL + per-entity append-only history tables; system audit-log table for audit-log entities

- **Date:** 2026-05-16
- **Decision:** The data layer for `sca-tracker` lands at two coupled sub-decisions, bundled because engine capabilities constrain history-impl viability (JSONB, advisory locks, `SERIALIZABLE` isolation). **(D1) Persistence engine:** **PostgreSQL 15+**, accessed via SQLAlchemy 2.0 + Alembic per ADR-0051. Managed offering selected at PaaS-vendor pick (Neon free-tier is the pinned dev default per ADR-0051; production PaaS choice deferred to implementation kickoff). **(D2) History implementation shape:** **Per-entity append-only history tables** for the 9 history-carrying entities (3 comprehensive + 6 lifecycle), written in the same SQLAlchemy session/transaction as the entity mutation; a **shared system `command_audit_log` table** with polymorphic `(entity_type, entity_id)` reference for the 7 audit-log entities; no history infrastructure for the 5 no-history entities. Capture is enforced by the `Command` base class + dispatcher (carry-forward from ADR-0051) — for history-carrying entities the history-row write is structurally inseparable from the entity mutation; there is no handler-level escape hatch.
- **Status:** accepted
