- **Context:** Step 8b of the Conceptualization phase, the second half of Step 8 after the 2026-05-15 partition. Step 8a (ADR-0051) pinned the runtime stack and passed two constraints forward: the persistence engine must be SQLAlchemy-supported, RDBMS-class, available as a managed offering on the chosen PaaS, support concurrency primitives strong enough for ADR-0010's cross-entity-invariant-revalidation requirement, and accommodate the Neon-dev / SQLite-offline env-config model. Inputs were `mvp.md`, `framework.md`, `logic.md`, `history-patterns.md` (the 4-pattern menu), `domain-model.md` § History patterns per entity (the 3/6/7/5 distribution across 21 entities), and the substrate ADRs — ADR-0006 (per-entity history decision), ADR-0008 (atomic state-mutation + history-record at command boundary), ADR-0010 (well-formedness invariant enforcement on the write path), ADR-0013 (4-pattern menu + reference-snapshotting rule + forward-only promotion), and ADR-0051 (the inherited stack envelope).

  Two sub-decisions framed the bundle:

  - **(D1) Persistence engine.** Candidates that survived the ADR-0051 envelope: (a) PostgreSQL 15+ (Neon dev pin already in place; best-in-class isolation primitives — `SERIALIZABLE`, advisory locks, row-level `FOR UPDATE`, `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` — for the ADR-0010 cross-entity-invariant-revalidation requirement; JSONB for history-snapshot columns; most mature SQLAlchemy + Alembic support of any engine; universal PaaS availability); (b) MySQL/MariaDB (weaker `SERIALIZABLE` semantics, connection-scoped `GET_LOCK` is the wrong primitive for transaction-scoped guards, JSON column ergonomics weaker than JSONB, would conflict with the Neon dev pin); (c) SQLite-everywhere with Litestream (categorically violates ADR-0010 isolation requirement — single-writer-by-design "satisfies" serializability by removing concurrency; already pushed back against in ADR-0051's dev-workflow deliberation); (d) Distributed Postgres flavors (CockroachDB, YugabyteDB — overkill at MVP scale, no scale pressure ever projected, pricier than Neon free-tier, Alembic compatibility good but not flawless). Settled **(a)** with high confidence — the envelope was tight enough after ADR-0051 that Postgres was effectively the only honest answer; the canvass exists to record that the others were ruled out on their merits.

  - **(D2) History implementation shape.** Candidates: (a) Per-entity append-only history tables (one `<entity>_history` table per history-carrying entity, written in the same SQLAlchemy txn); (b) Single polymorphic history table (one table, `(entity_type, entity_id)` polymorphic ref, JSONB blob per row); (c) Temporal tables / system-versioned tables (Postgres lacks native support; would be hand-rolled via triggers); (d) Event store as system of record for history-carrying entities. Settled **(a)** with high confidence. Per-entity tables fall out of every constraint: ADR-0008 atomicity is the same SQLAlchemy txn that mutates the entity; ADR-0006 per-entity ownership maps 1:1 to per-entity tables; ADR-0013 reference rules apply column-by-column in the JSONB snapshot/context columns; Postgres + JSONB + Alembic + SQLAlchemy declarative bases compose cleanly. Audit-log entities get a separate shared `command_audit_log` table (polymorphic ref, same shape as Note per ADR-0018) — faithful to the pattern's "command metadata only, no state" definition. No-history entities get no history infrastructure.

- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Single polymorphic history table for history-carrying entities.* Rejected — polymorphic FK problem at high write volume (no DB-level FK to the entity table, orphan rows possible); comprehensive + lifecycle patterns end up sharing column space with pattern-specific nullables; per-entity indexing degenerates to one large index on `(entity_type, entity_id, at)` or partial indexes per type (at which point per-entity tables are recreated in shared schema). The cross-entity-system-wide history query is rare; the per-entity history query is the hot path. Doesn't pay for itself.
  - *Temporal tables (hand-rolled via triggers).* Rejected on principle, not ergonomics — wrong dependency direction. ADR-0008 enforces capture at the **command pipeline boundary**, not at the row-mutation boundary. Triggers fire on whatever wrote the row (raw SQL, Alembic data migrations, manual DB-console edits all produce captures with no command context); triggers can't easily access caller identity or command name (those live at the application layer); for lifecycle capture, reconstructing "is this lifecycle-affecting?" from column diffs inverts the ADR-0009 application-level declaration.
  - *Event store as system of record for history-carrying entities.* Rejected — already foreclosed by ADR-0007 (events-as-primary rejected at the change-unit level — commands won) and ADR-0008 (events as the history mechanism rejected — per-entity opt-out becomes awkward when events are produced universally by construction). Re-opening would reverse two settled ADRs without new evidence.
  - *MySQL/MariaDB persistence engine.* Rejected — weaker `SERIALIZABLE` semantics (gap-locking differences make ADR-0010 cross-entity revalidation harder to reason about); `GET_LOCK` is connection-scoped, not transaction-scoped (wrong primitive); JSON ergonomics weaker than JSONB; would conflict with the Neon dev pin from ADR-0051. Real cost, zero benefit at this scale.
  - *SQLite-everywhere with Litestream replication.* Rejected — single-writer-by-design "satisfies" `SERIALIZABLE` by removing concurrency, not by handling it; ADR-0010 cross-entity invariant primitives are unavailable. Same ground ADR-0051 covered in the dev-workflow pushback.
  - *CockroachDB / YugabyteDB (distributed Postgres flavors).* Rejected — horizontal scalability is unneeded at MVP scale (single-region, office-internal, small user count); managed offerings pricier than Neon free-tier; not standard on the candidate PaaS shortlist; Alembic compatibility good but imperfect. Cost paid for benefit that doesn't exist.
  - *Split into two ADRs (ADR-0052 persistence, ADR-0053 history-impl).* Rejected — coupling is real (engine capabilities constrain history-impl viability — JSONB, advisory locks, `SERIALIZABLE`); persistence sub-decision is honestly short (Postgres falls out of the ADR-0051 envelope in ~1 paragraph); ADR-0009/0010/0012's three-way split was justified by different declaration surfaces (state machine / entity / command), which this pair doesn't share. Same structural reasoning as ADR-0051's three-way bundle.

- **Consequences:**
  - **Engine pinned.** PostgreSQL 15+ (16 acceptable if Neon defaults there). Managed offering per the eventual PaaS vendor pick; Neon free-tier remains the dev default per ADR-0051.
  - **History topology pinned.** 9 per-entity history tables (3 comprehensive: `document_history`, `wa_history`, `rfa_history`; 6 lifecycle: `project_history`, `sample_batch_history`, `deliverable_history`, `employee_role_history`, `wa_code_history`, `contractor_engagement_history`) + 1 shared `command_audit_log` table for the 7 audit-log entities (Employee, User, Time Entry, Contractor, DepFiling, Contract, WABundle). No history infrastructure for the 5 no-history entities (School, Note, UserRole, WACodeAssignment, WABundleSite).
  - **Common metadata on every history row** (comprehensive + lifecycle tables alike): `id` (UUID, PK); `entity_id` (DB-level FK to the target entity table); `command_id` (UUID — links rows produced by the same command instance, useful for grouping cascading-command output per `domain-model.md` § Design patterns #5); `command_name` (text); `caller_id` (FK to User); `at` (timestamptz). Default per-table index: `(entity_id, at DESC)`.
  - **Comprehensive-pattern columns.** Each comprehensive history table adds `snapshot` (JSONB) — full entity state at the moment of the command, including intrinsic + lifecycle + derived-if-cheap fields. Typed-UUID references only per ADR-0013 § Reference snapshotting; no denormalized copies of referenced entities.
  - **Lifecycle-pattern columns.** Each lifecycle history table adds `from_state` (text, nullable on entity-creation row), `to_state` (text), `transition_name` (text — the lifecycle transition declared by the command per ADR-0009), `state_context` (JSONB — sufficient context to interpret the transition; typed-UUID references only). Non-lifecycle commands on lifecycle-capture entities produce no history row (per ADR-0013's pattern-4 definition).
  - **Audit-log table.** `command_audit_log`: `id`, `entity_type` (text), `entity_id` (UUID — polymorphic ref, no DB-level FK; same shape as Note per ADR-0018), `command_name`, `caller_id`, `at`, `payload_summary` (JSONB — what was requested, not what changed; no state snapshots). Written by the command dispatcher. **Timing (in-txn vs. post-commit) deferred to implementation phase** — ADR-0013 permits async / best-effort; in-txn is allowed and stronger than the pattern promises.
  - **Capture enforcement.** The `Command` base class + dispatcher (carry-forward from ADR-0051) holds the history-write step. For history-carrying entities, the history row is written in the same SQLAlchemy session as the entity mutation — both commit or neither does (ADR-0008's atomicity guaranteed by transaction semantics, not by application discipline). No handler-level skip; the framework surface does not expose a skip-capture path. Comprehensive vs. lifecycle scope is read from the entity's declared pattern at command-resolution time.
  - **Reference snapshotting rule (restatement of ADR-0013).** Snapshot/state_context JSONB contains typed-UUID references only. Past state of a reference is recoverable via the referenced entity's own history chain when that entity carries history; otherwise (no-history / audit-log targets) past reference state is not recoverable. This is a selection-criteria input — entities frequently referenced by history-carrying entities may warrant heavier patterns than their own accountability needs alone would suggest.
  - **Schema evolution.** JSONB snapshot/context columns absorb most entity-schema changes; old rows hold the old shape, new rows hold the new shape, readers tolerate. Only metadata-column changes (common metadata) require Alembic migrations on history tables. Code that reconstructs past state is responsible for old-shape tolerance — a manual / audit-time concern at this domain's scale, not a hot path.
  - **Cross-entity invariant isolation (ADR-0010 inheritance).** Cross-entity invariant revalidation in the command pipeline uses Postgres `SERIALIZABLE` transactions by default. `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` is available as an opt-in primitive for invariants where serialization conflicts would be too frequent (e.g., the closure-readiness derivation cluster — `domain-model.md` § Design patterns #3). Exact per-invariant choice is implementation-phase; the ADR pins the available primitives, not the per-invariant assignments.
  - **Engine-portability discipline (restatement of ADR-0051).** JSONB ops, advisory locks, and `SERIALIZABLE` isolation are Postgres-specific. All three sit behind the documented adapter boundary per ADR-0051; the SQLite-offline-fallback path uses degraded equivalents (JSON text column, optimistic-locking in place of advisory locks, default isolation). The fallback path is buildable for offline development but **not production-equivalent** — explicit, acknowledged.
  - **History-pattern promotion (restatement of ADR-0013).** Forward-only promotion (no history → comprehensive, lifecycle → comprehensive) is a schema-level change: add the history table per the appropriate pattern's column shape (or, for lifecycle → comprehensive promotion, add a comprehensive table alongside the existing lifecycle one) and amend the entity's pattern declaration. History begins at promotion; pre-promotion changes are irrecoverable.
  - **Quarantine remains deferred** per ADR-0011. Quarantine is orthogonal to history infrastructure; if commissioned later as a per-entity pattern, it would be a separate side-state mechanism on the entity itself, not a history-table variant.
  - **Step 8b complete.** Remaining in Conceptualization: **Step 9** (data model sketch + roadmap + phase-transition ADR + pre-transition ADR consolidation pass for ADRs with 2+ amendments).

- **Amendments to other ADRs:** None. ADR-0006 (per-entity history decision), ADR-0008 (atomic capture at command boundary), ADR-0010 (write-path invariant enforcement; isolation primitives deferred to Step 8 — now pinned here), ADR-0013 (4-pattern menu + reference rules + promotion), and ADR-0051 (stack envelope) are all honored without modification. ADR-0010's deferred isolation-mechanism question (serializable transactions / optimistic locking / advisory locks) is answered by this ADR's primitives commitment (`SERIALIZABLE` default + advisory-lock opt-in) — recorded here rather than as an amendment to ADR-0010 since ADR-0010 explicitly deferred the choice to Step 8.

- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **PaaS vendor pick + managed-Postgres offering** (Neon / Supabase / RDS / Cloud SQL / PaaS-bundled). Implementation-phase kickoff per ADR-0051; this ADR doesn't constrain beyond "managed offering on the chosen PaaS".
  - **`Command` base class + dispatcher concrete design** (carry-forward from ADR-0051). Implementation phase. The history-write step lands inside the dispatcher; pipeline order from `logic.md` (auth → lifecycle → apply → invariants → history → commit) is the spec.
  - **Per-invariant isolation-primitive assignment** (`SERIALIZABLE` vs. `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` per invariant). Implementation phase; the available primitives are pinned here, the per-invariant choice is not.
  - **Audit-log write timing** (in-txn vs. post-commit). Implementation phase.
  - **`backend/` and `frontend/` stale-scaffolding cleanup.** Implementation-phase opening session per ADR-0001 + ADR-0051.

---

## ADR-0053 — Blocker-and-resolution model (consolidates ADR-0032)

- **Date:** 2026-05-17
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** Consolidates ADR-0032's surface to reflect the current blocker-and-resolution model. Blockers attach to entities via typed Notes (subtype `blocker`); resolutions attach via typed Notes (subtype `resolution`) referencing the blocker they resolve. System-derived blockers stay derived (a registry-driven predicate over entity state) until a coordinator engages, at which point a system-authored blocker Note materializes lazily. User-flagged blockers are coordinator-authored from creation. The registry holds **10 entries** (9 `has-default-resolution` + 1 `fix-only`) with per-entry schema `(target, command_shape, optional compound_names, optional chain)`. The closure gate simplifies to **"no registry blocker holds,"** with predicates evaluated over not-written-off entities. Resolution kinds: `structural_fix | default_resolution | dismissal` — the first written automatically on predicate-flip, the second by the default-resolution command family (a generic `default_resolve` + three named compounds; nuclear-option guard: never autonomously system-initiated, mandatory coordinator justification), the third reserved for free-form user-flagged blockers (no registry entry). Chain shapes are named once and referenced from registry entries; one chain (`te_batches_by_coverage`) is in use, invoked by 4 entries. Note subtypes are the full set `regular | blocker | resolution | audit_reason | write_off` (the last two added by ADR-0040 and ADR-0042 respectively, included here for self-contained reading). Status flip on ADR-0032 only; ADR-0042 (write-off substrate), ADR-0046 (per-entry classification + registry schema extension), ADR-0049 (registry trim) stay `accepted` — each carries substantive deliberation context beyond ADR-0032 amendments that this consolidation preserves rather than compacts away.
- **Context:** ADR-0032 (2026-05-12) introduced the blocker-as-Note pattern with a `dismissable | fix-only` classification binary and a closure-gate text that allowed "OR has a dismissal resolution Note" as the dismissable escape clause. That model was reshaped by subsequent ADRs: ADR-0042 (2026-05-14) reframed the binary to `has-default-resolution | fix-only`, introduced the `write_off` Note subtype and the default-resolution model, and simplified the closure gate to "no registry blocker holds" over not-written-off entities; ADR-0046 (2026-05-15) applied the reframe to every registry entry, extended the registry schema with per-entry default-resolution metadata, and defined the named `te_batches_by_coverage` chain shape; ADR-0049 (2026-05-15) trimmed blockers #1 and #2 (unfireable post-keep-FK cascade per ADR-0048) bringing the registry to 10 entries. Single-amender additions (0033's chain-dismissal first instance, 0034's #9 predicate restructure, 0037's #10, 0039's #11, 0044's #12) compounded the reading-friction. A reader of ADR-0032's text today sees the wrong model: the wrong classification binary, the wrong closure-gate formulation, the wrong Note subtype set, the wrong registry size, no awareness of the write-off substrate. This consolidation is the phase-boundary cleanup: rewrite ADR-0032's surface to current state so implementation-phase readers begin from a correct picture. ADR-0042 / ADR-0046 / ADR-0049 retain their bodies — they contain load-bearing deliberation (coherence test for default-resolutions; per-cluster classification reasoning; the keep-FK cascade justification) that future readers will want when judging *why* the model is shaped this way.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Compact ADR-0032 + ADR-0042 + ADR-0046 + ADR-0049 into a single super-ADR.* Rejected per session 25 deliberation — collapses the deliberation chain entirely, including the write-off coherence test, the per-cluster classification logic, and the keep-FK justification. The user's framing (planning/steps.md § Step 9) explicitly cites deliberation-context loss as the cost mid-phase consolidation pays; phase boundary doesn't make that context worth less. Future implementation-phase readers wanting to know why a blocker is classified the way it is, or why the cascade keeps the FK, or whether their proposed new blocker meets the coherence test, are exactly the audience the three substantive amender ADRs serve.
  - *Compact ADR-0032 + ADR-0042 only (consolidate the two ADRs that changed the model, leave the registry-application and trim ADRs standing).* Rejected — ADR-0042's write-off coherence test is itself load-bearing for any future blocker classification, and its design-pattern-#14 narrative would have to be carried into the consolidated ADR (re-introducing the compaction problem at smaller scale).
  - *Skip the consolidation entirely; rely on status flips + `amends` chains for navigation.* Rejected per the same session 25 deliberation — ADR-0032 is the one ADR where the chain of amendments leaves the original body genuinely misleading (binary, gate, subtype set, registry size all changed). The phase-transition is the right moment to fix the one ADR that crosses that bar.
  - *Apply the literal "2+ amendments" test from steps.md line 612 (would qualify 18 ADRs).* Rejected as overcalibrated — the literal count conflates mechanical schema-addition amendments (e.g., "EmployeeRole gains `contract_id`") with substantive reframes (ADR-0042 → ADR-0032). The real signal is "the original ADR's text misleads a present-day reader about the current model," and ADR-0032 is the only ADR that crosses it. Phase-transition ADR records this honest deviation from the literal framing.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Note subtypes (per ADR-0018 + amenders).** Note's `subtype` enum: `regular | blocker | resolution | audit_reason | write_off`. `regular` is editable by creator per ADR-0018. `blocker`, `resolution`, `audit_reason`, `write_off` are immutable regardless of authorship. `audit_reason` added by ADR-0040; `write_off` added by ADR-0042. `authorship_class: 'user' | 'system'` discriminator on all Notes; `created_by` nullable for system-authored Notes. Inter-Note `references` field carries `blocker_ref` (resolution Note → blocker Note), `paired_blocker_ref` (cross-project paired blocker Notes), `write_off` chain references (cascade write-offs reference the originating blocker Note), and the general "this Note structurally references that Note" semantic.
  - **Polymorphic target (per ADR-0018 + ADR-0040).** Notes target any entity OR any history record. The history-record target is exercised by `audit_reason` Notes attached to grant/revoke history rows; the broader pattern is available for future event-anchored commentary without re-amendment.
  - **Lazy materialization (unchanged from ADR-0032).** A system-derived blocker stays derived (computed via registry-driven predicate over entity state) until a coordinator engages with it. Engagement triggers: (i) writing a `regular` Note referencing the blocker via `comment_blocker`; (ii) writing a `resolution` Note via the default-resolution command family or via `dismiss_blocker` for free-form user-flagged blockers. On first engagement, the system atomically materializes a system-authored `blocker` Note with `surfaced_at` backfilled from underlying entity history, then performs the engagement. Subsequent engagements find the blocker Note already materialized and append to it.
  - **User-flagged blockers (unchanged from ADR-0032).** A coordinator creates a `blocker` Note directly on any entity with `authorship_class: 'user'`, `blocker_type: null` (no registry entry), `surfaced_at = created_at`. Resolution via `dismiss_blocker` writes a `resolution` Note with `resolution_kind: 'dismissal'`; the `dismissal` kind is reserved for this case (no registry entry, no default-resolution path, no structural condition to watch).
  - **Cross-project blocker materialization (unchanged from ADR-0032).** For blockers spanning two records on different projects (currently #8), engagement by one project's coordinator materializes the blocker Note on that side; engagement by the other side materializes a paired Note linked via `paired_blocker_ref`. Each project's coordinator maintains a separate investigation thread. Auto-`structural_fix` resolution Notes are written per materialized side independently when the predicate flips.
  - **Resolution semantics.**
    - *Structural fix (system-authored).* When the underlying predicate flips false (over not-written-off entities), the system writes a `resolution` Note for each materialized blocker Note of that type+target with `authorship_class: 'system'`, `resolution_kind: 'structural_fix'`. Derived (non-materialized) blockers simply stop surfacing — no resolution Note since there is no blocker Note to resolve.
    - *Default resolution (user-initiated, nuclear-option guarded).* The coordinator fires a default-resolution command (generic `default_resolve` or named compound — see below). The command writes one `write_off` Note per affected entity (with `reason` = the coordinator's mandatory justification, `references` the blocker Note); writes one `resolution` Note on the blocker with `resolution_kind: 'default_resolution'`; for entries with a declared `chain`, emits direct `write_off` Notes per chained entity inheriting the same justification. Per ADR-0042's nuclear-option guard: never autonomously system-initiated (chain-cascades inherit the primary's coordinator-supplied justification); mandatory justification stamped onto every `write_off` Note the invocation produces.
    - *Dismissal (user-flagged blockers only).* Coordinator-authored `resolution` Note with `resolution_kind: 'dismissal'`, written by `dismiss_blocker`. Reserved for free-form user-flagged blockers — registry blockers never dismiss; they either structurally-resolve or default-resolve.
  - **Closure gate.** **"No registry blocker holds,"** with each entry's predicate evaluated over not-written-off entities. Replaces ADR-0032's two-clause gate (the "OR has a dismissal Note" escape clause is removed — default-resolutions dissolve their blockers *structurally* by removing the conflicting entities from the predicate domain via `write_off`, so a default-resolved blocker stops holding rather than holding-but-being-acknowledged).
  - **Canonical registry — 10 entries** (post-ADR-0049 trim; gap-preserving numbering since #1 and #2 were retired). Per-entry schema: `(target, command_shape, optional compound_names, optional chain)`.

    | # | Blocker | Classification | Target | Command shape | Compound names | Chain |
    |---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
    | 3 | Sample Batch Lab Report ∈ {`missing`, `invalid`} at closure | has-default-resolution | Sample Batch | generic | — | — |
    | 4 | Sample Batch COC `missing` at closure | has-default-resolution | Sample Batch | generic | — | — |
    | 5 | Time Entry no `daily_log` at closure | has-default-resolution | Time Entry | generic | — | `te_batches_by_coverage` |
    | 6 | DepFiling required-doc `missing` at closure | has-default-resolution | DepFiling | generic | — | — |
    | 7 | Open `draft`/`in_review` RFA at closure (add/remove RFA, MVP) | has-default-resolution | RFA | named-compound | [`resolve_open_rfa`] | — |
    | 8 | Cross-project time overlap on Employee | has-default-resolution | (paired Time Entries) | named-compound | [`resolve_overlap`, `resolve_overlap_paired`] | `te_batches_by_coverage` |
    | 9 | Sample collection time not in employee net on-site time | has-default-resolution | Sample Batch | generic | — | — |
    | 10 | Project's non-terminal RFP not in `saved` state at closure | **fix-only** | — | — | — | — |
    | 11 | Time Entry `(employee, role_type, contract, date)` not covered by EmployeeRole | has-default-resolution | Time Entry | generic | — | `te_batches_by_coverage` |
    | 12 | Time Entry dated before head WA's `initialization_date` | has-default-resolution | Time Entry | generic | — | `te_batches_by_coverage` |

    Retired (gap-preserved): **#1** (Time Entry `wa_code = null`), **#2** (Sample Batch `wa_code = null`) — both unfireable post-ADR-0048's cascade-keep-FK reframe (`wa_code = null` is no longer a state the system can produce; the cascade emits `write_off` Notes on referencing entities while keeping the FK to the terminal-state code). New entries: append at #13+ when introduced.

  - **Chain shapes.** **`te_batches_by_coverage`** (defined ADR-0046): when a Time Entry default-resolves, emit direct `write_off` Notes on each Sample Batch whose `(employee, school, collection_time)` falls within the Time Entry's `on_site_range`. Each chained Note inherits the primary's `justification` as its `reason` and `references` the primary blocker Note. Invoked by entries #5, #8, #11, #12.
  - **Default-resolution command family (per ADR-0046).**
    - **`default_resolve(blocker, justification)`** — generic, covers the 7 entries with `command_shape = generic` (#3, #4, #5, #6, #9, #11, #12). Atomic: materialize blocker if derived-only → write `write_off` Note on the registry-declared `target` entity → emit chain Notes if declared → write `resolution` Note with `resolution_kind: default_resolution`. Authorization: `role >= coordinator` (ADR-0047).
    - **`resolve_overlap(blocker_note, justification)`** — single-side compound for #8. Invokes `split_entry` on the engaging side to isolate the overlap sliver → writes `write_off` on the sliver → writes `resolution` on the blocker. The paired blocker on the other side resolves via auto-`structural_fix` (the overlap predicate stops holding once the sliver is excluded).
    - **`resolve_overlap_paired(paired_blocker_note, justification)`** — joint compound for #8 when both sides are written off symmetrically. Distinct from `resolve_overlap` in audit semantics (explicit `default_resolution` on both sides vs. one side with auto-`structural_fix` on the other).
    - **`resolve_open_rfa(rfa, justification)`** — named compound for #7 (MVP add/remove-RFA case only). Withdraws the RFA → cascade-empties the draft → resolves the blocker.
    - **`revoke_write_off(write_off_note, ...)`** — explicit lift command (ADR-0042 carry-forward). Writes an immutable superseding Note; re-exposes the entity to blocker-derivation predicates. Authorization: `role >= coordinator` (ADR-0047). Command shape (parameters, guards, audit shape) is a Step 6d / residual carry-forward.
  - **Nuclear-option guard (per ADR-0042).** Default-resolution commands are guarded two ways. (a) **Never autonomously system-initiated** — always either coordinator-initiated or a declared chain-consequence of a coordinator-initiated resolution (which inherits the primary's justification rather than prompting). (b) **Mandatory justification** — one justification per invocation, stamped onto the `reason` of every `write_off` Note the invocation produces. Cascade write-offs from non-default-resolution commands (e.g., the keep-FK cascade from `dismiss_wa_code` per ADR-0048 / ADR-0049) are not separately guarded — they inherit their `reason` from the initiating command, which is why the write-off model admits non-blocker reasons.
  - **Notes carry no history.** ADR-0018's no-history stance is preserved for all Note subtypes. The `blocker` Note IS the surface-record; the `resolution` Note IS the resolution-record; the `write_off` Note IS the exclusion-record; the `audit_reason` Note IS the grant/revoke rationale-record. `regular` Notes carry `edited_at` for the creator-edit case; other subtypes are immutable.
  - **Design pattern references (no new patterns added here).**
    - **#11 (blocker-as-Note)** — established by ADR-0032; unchanged.
    - **#12 (chain-dismissal)** — established by ADR-0033, generalized by ADR-0046 (`te_batches_by_coverage` named instance); under the write-off model, chained entities receive direct `write_off` Notes inheriting the primary's `justification` rather than the older `wa_code`-nulling mechanic.
    - **#14 (write-off / default-resolution)** — established by ADR-0042; the substrate this consolidation rests on. Future readers wanting the coherence test for new blocker classifications consult ADR-0042 directly.
  - **Supersession of ADR-0032 — what does and doesn't change.** ADR-0032's body remains in `decisions.md` for deliberation-context continuity (the original blocker-as-Note rationale, the lazy-materialization motivation, the per-entity-`acknowledged`-flag rejection, the cross-project paired-Note design) but its Status flips to `superseded by ADR-0053`. Readers seeking the *current model* consult ADR-0053; readers seeking *why the model has this shape* consult ADR-0032 (substrate), ADR-0042 (write-off reframe), ADR-0046 (registry application), ADR-0049 (registry trim).
- **Amendments to other ADRs:** None. ADR-0032's Status flips to `superseded by ADR-0053` (status-only edit; body unchanged). ADR-0042, ADR-0046, ADR-0049 unchanged.
- **Carry-forwards.** No new carry-forwards. Pre-existing carry-forwards remain attached to their origin ADRs:
  - **`split_entry` command shape** — load-bearing for #8's compounds. Carry-forward unchanged from ADR-0028 / ADR-0042 / ADR-0046; no home step (candidate: Step 6d or a residual; will likely land in the implementation phase).
  - **`revoke_write_off` command shape** — parameters, guards, audit-shape of the superseding Note. Carry-forward unchanged from ADR-0042 / ADR-0046 / ADR-0049.
  - **Revoke-line-item command shape** (rescinding coordinator-authored RFA `remove` line items before approval) — carry-forward unchanged from ADR-0049.
  - **#7 reclassification when budget RFAs land** — post-MVP. Carry-forward unchanged from ADR-0046.
  - **ADR-0031 auto-draft regeneration suppression at closure-gate** — carry-forward unchanged from ADR-0046.
  - **#4 drop candidate** — Sample Batch COC missing at closure. Carry-forward unchanged from ADR-0046; `mvp.md` § Carve-outs / `post-mvp.md` tracking.

---

## ADR-0054 — Conceptualization phase complete; Implementation phase begins

- **Date:** 2026-05-17
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** Mark the Conceptualization phase complete; mark the Implementation phase current. Triggers the four `phases.md` writes per `_workflow.md`'s phase-roster protocol: (a) flip Phase 1 status `current → complete`; (b) flip Phase 2 status `not started → current` with concrete Goal + Steps pointer; (c) archive current `planning/steps.md` → `planning/steps.archive/conceptualization.md` (creating the archive directory); (d) create new `planning/steps.md` for the Implementation phase, mirroring the 9 milestones from `planning/roadmap.md` (M0 Foundations → M8 Cutover prep). Also adds a Phase 3 stub to `phases.md` per the just-in-time enumeration principle.
- **Context:** The Conceptualization phase opened 2026-04-28 (ADR-0001) and closes here at 2026-05-17, having produced 53 ADRs across 9 steps + 8 partitioned sub-steps + 25 sessions. The rolled-up artifacts that Implementation work consumes: `planning/framework.md` (Step 1 — entity / value / relationship; four-kind state taxonomy; UUID identity); `planning/logic.md` (Steps 2–4 — commands; mandatory capture; lifecycle + invariant + authorization pipeline); `planning/history-patterns.md` (Step 5 — 4-pattern menu; selection criteria; reference snapshotting; promotion); `planning/domain-model.md` (Step 6d — 21 entities; 14 design patterns; 10-entry blocker registry; four-role chain; carry-forward catalog); `planning/mvp.md` (Step 7 — 6 must-have features; carve-outs; command-shape carry-forwards; categorized "not now"); `planning/architecture.md` (Step 8b — component diagram; data flow; out-of-band concerns); `planning/data-model.md` (Step 9a — conceptual data model with per-entity attribute rosters + history-table topology, not DDL); `planning/roadmap.md` (Step 9b — 9 ordered implementation milestones with rough sizing + carry-forward landing index). The pre-transition ADR consolidation pass settled with **one** consolidation: **ADR-0053 (consolidates ADR-0032 — blocker-and-resolution model)**.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Skip the phase-transition ADR; flip `phases.md` silently.* Rejected — `_workflow.md`'s phase-roster protocol explicitly requires a dedicated phase-transition ADR as the trigger for the four writes. The ADR is the audit anchor for "this is the moment the phase changed and these are the artifacts the next phase consumes."
  - *Apply the literal "ADRs with 2+ amendments" consolidation test from `steps.md` line 612 (would qualify 18 ADRs and partition Step 9b into 9b + 9c + 9d + ...).* Rejected per session 25 deliberation — the literal count conflates mechanical schema-addition amendments (e.g., "EmployeeRole gains `contract_id`") with substantive reframes (e.g., ADR-0042 → ADR-0032). The real signal is "the original ADR's text misleads a present-day reader about the current model," and ADR-0032 is the only ADR that crosses it (its `dismissable | fix-only` binary, closure-gate text, Note subtype set, and registry size are all wrong relative to the current model after ADR-0042 / 0046 / 0049 + single-amender additions). Position B-narrowed accepted: consolidate ADR-0032 alone via ADR-0053; leave 17 other 2+-amender ADRs standing (their amender chains preserve correctly-readable models). The deviation from the literal framing is recorded here as the honest finding.
  - *Pre-enumerate Phase 3 with concrete Goal + Steps.* Rejected per `phases.md`'s just-in-time enumeration principle — phases are enumerated when the next phase ends. Phase 3 lands as a stub only (per the precedent set when Phase 2 was a stub during Conceptualization).
- **Consequences:**
  - **Four `phases.md` writes execute** per `_workflow.md`'s lightweight gate (announce + wait for yes; not full deliberation). Listed in the Decision.
  - **`planning/roadmap.md` is the canonical milestone-shape source for Phase 2.** New `steps.md` mirrors roadmap milestones; per-step briefs expand as sessions consume them (Case 2 sizing as each step lands).
  - **`planning/mvp.md` is the canonical MVP-scope reference.** Adding a feature beyond `mvp.md`'s 6 must-haves requires a superseding ADR.
  - **`planning/data-model.md` is the conceptual data model**, not DDL. DDL is M0 Foundations work (Phase 2's first step).
  - **First Phase 2 step is M0 Foundations.** New `steps.md`'s Step 1 brief opens M0; the carry-forward landing index in `roadmap.md` shows which carry-forwards land at which milestone.
  - **The ADR consolidation pass result is recorded here.** Position B-narrowed: ADR-0032 → ADR-0053 (status flip on ADR-0032 only). The 17 other 2+-amender ADRs stay as-is; future readers chase their amender chains to current state.
  - **Conceptualization phase ADRs (ADR-0001 through ADR-0054) are the deliberation record for Phase 2.** Implementation-phase work consults them when judging *why* a model has the shape it has; the rolled-up artifacts (framework.md, logic.md, history-patterns.md, domain-model.md, mvp.md, architecture.md, data-model.md, roadmap.md) carry the *current state* answers.
- **Amendments to other ADRs:** None. ADR-0001's stale-scaffolding stance is consumed by M0 Foundations (Phase 2 work, not a Conceptualization amendment). All other ADRs unchanged.
- **Carry-forwards:** None from this ADR. All carry-forwards (command-shape + implementation-phase + carve-outs) are tracked in `roadmap.md` § Carry-forward landing index against the milestones they land in.

---

## ADR-0055 — Defer production PaaS vendor pick until prod is called for; preserve portability via discipline notes

- **Date:** 2026-05-18
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** Defer the production PaaS vendor pick + managed-Postgres offering indefinitely. Originally framed as Step 1.2 / M0.2 work landing at implementation kickoff (per ADR-0051 + ADR-0052 carry-forwards). Reinterpret the trigger from *"implementation kickoff (M0 opens)"* to *"user explicitly prompts to circle back."* Until that trigger fires, the development posture per ADR-0051 (Neon free-tier dev branches per machine + local) is the working environment, with no production deploy target named. Five discipline notes (Consequences below) keep the eventual vendor swap cheap.
- **Context:** Step 1.2 of the Implementation phase opened as a vendor canvass and was reframed on user push-back. The honest framing: no production audience exists yet; the project may live as a portfolio / learning artifact and never need production hosting. Of the downstream work in M0 + M1–M7, none actually depends on the vendor pick — ADR-0052 already pinned PostgreSQL 15+ independently of vendor; the M0.5 adapter wraps *Postgres-specific* features (JSONB, advisory locks, `SERIALIZABLE`), not *vendor-specific* features; the dispatcher / history infrastructure / domain code are vendor-agnostic. The "dependency ordering" rationale that placed Step 1.2 inside M0 in the 2026-05-17 partition (`PaaS picks Postgres flavor → primitives bind to that flavor`) is not actually load-bearing — Postgres is Postgres across all realistic managed offerings. M8 (cutover prep) is the latest moment the pick becomes necessary; any earlier production-driven trigger (e.g., a real user emerges) brings it forward. The cost of deferral is ~1 hour of vendor canvass deferred from now to the trigger moment, against the benefit of not spending decision budget on a decision that may never matter.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Pick vendor now per original Step 1.2 framing.* Rejected — no production audience; if the project never reaches production, the decision is wasted; the canvass is short enough (~1 hour) to do at the actual trigger moment with no portability penalty as long as the discipline notes hold.
  - *Pick vendor lazily at each milestone (M3 / M5 / M8 as triggers).* Rejected — no milestone before M8 actually needs the pick; "pick lazily" creates a constant low-grade re-evaluation tax at every milestone opening. Single deferral with a named trigger is cleaner.
  - *Pick a no-cost "default" now (e.g., Neon-prod-tier paired with Render or Fly.io for app hosting) without commitment.* Rejected — still spends decision budget canvassing the app-side bundle; the discipline notes give the same portability protection without spending the budget.
  - *Skip the ADR; just remove Step 1.2 from `steps.md` silently.* Rejected — the deferral reinterprets two prior carry-forward triggers (ADR-0051's "implementation kickoff," ADR-0052's "PaaS vendor pick"). That's an amendment by supersession of substantive ADR scope and earns its own audit anchor.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Postgres-version floor pinned to 15+.** Dev (`docker-compose.yml` for CI, Neon branch for local) runs Postgres 15 or higher. Universal floor across the realistic vendor shortlist (Render Postgres, Fly.io Postgres, Railway Postgres, Neon prod tier, AWS RDS, GCP Cloud SQL, Azure Database for PostgreSQL). Documented in the M0.1 CI config and reaffirmed when M0 closes.
  - **No vendor-specific Postgres extensions without availability check.** Adopting `pgvector`, `citus`, `pg_partman`, or any non-core extension requires checking availability on the realistic vendor shortlist before adoption. MVP scope (`mvp.md`) requires no such extensions; this is forward-looking discipline.
  - **Default Postgres driver only.** Stay on vanilla `psycopg` (SQLAlchemy 2.0 default). Neon's serverless driver, RDS Proxy, and other vendor-coupled connection layers are opt-ins at vendor-pick time, not adopted in dev. Connection pooling stays at the SQLAlchemy pool level.
  - **CI stays on docker-compose Postgres in the runner.** M0.1 deferred vendor-coupled ephemeral-PR DB wiring (e.g., Neon branch-per-PR) and that posture stays through MVP build-out. Vendor-coupled CI wiring lands when the vendor is picked.
  - **Architecture.md vendor slot stays "deferred per ADR-0055"** rather than "TBD." Step 8b's File contract clause *"the PaaS vendor is pinned at implementation kickoff (vendor name + DB managed-offering name)"* is amended-by-supersession: the trigger reinterprets to "user prompts circle-back" (no later than M8 if the project ships to production).
- **Amendments to other ADRs:**
  - **ADR-0051's "Specific PaaS vendor pick" carry-forward.** Trigger reinterpreted from *"Implementation-phase kickoff"* to *"user prompts circle-back; no later than M8 cutover if project ships to production."* Other ADR-0051 commitments (the runtime stack, the dev DB workflow pinning Neon free-tier, the deployment shape committing to managed-PaaS-monolith) are unchanged.
  - **ADR-0052's "PaaS vendor pick + managed-Postgres offering" carry-forward.** Same trigger reinterpretation. The constraint "managed offering on the chosen PaaS" still binds the eventual pick; this ADR doesn't relax that.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **PaaS vendor pick + managed-Postgres offering + provisioning + deploy wiring.** Lands when user explicitly prompts circle-back, or at latest M8 cutover prep if project ships to production. Canvass shape and candidate slate per the deferred Step 1.2 framing in `steps.md` (filter-first: managed Postgres 15+, monolith container target, single region, monthly cost ceiling, ops-familiarity floor).
  - **CI ephemeral-PR DB wiring** against the chosen vendor. Same trigger.
  - **Connection-pooling decision** (vendor-pooler vs. SQLAlchemy pool only). Same trigger.
  - **Architecture.md vendor pin** (vendor name + DB managed-offering name in the component diagram). Same trigger.

---

## ADR-0056 — Per-invariant isolation primitive: two-prong opt-in criterion + first per-invariant assignments

- **Date:** 2026-05-18
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** Resolves the per-invariant isolation-primitive half of ADR-0052's deferred implementation-phase carry-forwards (the audit-log timing half resolves in ADR-0057). Three pieces. **(D1.a) Opt-in criterion.** PostgreSQL `SERIALIZABLE` is the default isolation primitive for cross-entity invariant revalidation in the dispatcher's invariant step. Reach for `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` when **both** prongs hold: **(a)** the invariant's read footprint is wide enough that SERIALIZABLE will produce frequent false-positive serialization failures under realistic load (e.g., a predicate scanning many entities of multiple types); AND **(b)** the invariant's logical scope can be expressed as a small set of named lock keys (e.g., per-project, per-employee). If prong (b) cannot be satisfied — no stable key — SERIALIZABLE is the only honest choice; advisory locks without a key are misuse. **(D1.b) Closure-readiness predicate cluster → `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` keyed per-project.** The cluster (design pattern #3 in `domain-model.md`) is evaluated on `close_project` and revalidated by every command that mutates a closure-readiness-relevant entity (Time Entries / Sample Batches / Documents / RFAs / DepFilings / RFP — any entity whose state participates in a blocker-registry predicate per `domain-model.md` § Blocker registry). Lock-key shape (e.g., `hashtext('closure-readiness:' || project_id)::bigint`) is illustrative; exact computation lives in M0.3 dispatcher code. **(D1.c) EmployeeRole disjoint-ranges-per-`(employee, role_type, contract)` (ADR-0045) → SERIALIZABLE (default).** Conflict surface scopes to the same tuple; office workflow does not contend at this scope. Per-invariant primitive choices for invariants landing in M1–M7 are made when those invariants land in code, applying D1.a's criterion; the framework + 2 worked examples here do not pre-commit them. Amends ADR-0052 § Cross-entity invariant isolation by resolving its per-invariant carry-forward.
- **Context:** Step 1.2 / M0.2 (Phase 2) opened to resolve ADR-0052's two deferred carry-forwards: per-invariant isolation primitive (this ADR) and audit-log write timing (ADR-0057). ADR-0052 pinned the **available** primitives (`SERIALIZABLE` default + `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` opt-in) and named the closure-readiness cluster as a candidate but explicitly deferred per-invariant choice to implementation phase. Three sub-questions remained: the criterion (D1.a); closure-readiness assignment (D1.b); EmployeeRole disjoint-ranges assignment (D1.c). Session 29 also resolved two meta-questions before substance: **Q1 — bundle vs. split ADR shape** (split chosen: ADR-0056 here covers isolation; ADR-0057 covers audit-log timing — the two decisions are independent dispatcher-internal mechanism choices with no constraint coupling, so ADR-0052's bundling rationale doesn't apply); **Q2 — assignment scope** (framework + 2 worked examples chosen, not full enumeration — per-invariant choices land with the invariants in code, when the implementer has actual conflict-frequency context).
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *(D1.a) Single-prong criterion (conflict frequency only).* Rejected — *"reach for advisory lock when expected serialization-failure rate would cause user-visible retry storms"* is vague at M0 (no implementation experience to calibrate "expected rate") and gives the M1+ implementer no structural test. The two-prong shape forces the key-shape question upfront: without a stable lock key the primitive is unusable, regardless of read-footprint intuition.
  - *(D1.b) SERIALIZABLE for closure-readiness.* Rejected — the predicate scan touches many entities (Time Entries, Sample Batches, Documents, RFAs, DepFilings, RFP). Under SERIALIZABLE, `close_project`'s read predicates would conflict against virtually every concurrent write on any project-scoped entity, producing frequent `serialization_failure` errors during business-hours coordinator activity. The wasted-work-before-commit-rejection failure mode (vs. advisory-lock's fast-fail-before-work) also favors the advisory lock.
  - *(D1.c) Advisory lock for EmployeeRole disjoint-ranges.* Rejected — prong (a) fails. The predicate scans only EmployeeRole rows matching `(employee_id, role_type, contract_id)`, a small set per check; conflict surface bounded to concurrent commands hitting the same tuple. SERIALIZABLE's retry rate is near zero in office workflow (one admin editing one employee's rate history at a time). Adding advisory-lock machinery here would buy nothing.
  - *(Q2 — full enumeration of invariants in this ADR).* Rejected per session 29 deliberation — pre-assigning primitives for invariants that don't yet exist in code inverts the "decision with context" principle. A pre-assignment that proves wrong under actual workload (e.g., a SERIALIZABLE pick that turns contention-heavy under M4 bulk-import) requires an ADR amendment; the criterion-application alternative requires only a code change. Framework + 2 worked examples demonstrates the criterion in action without overcommitting.
  - *(Q1 — bundle with audit-log timing as a single ADR).* Rejected per session 29 — D1 (isolation primitive) and D2 (audit-log timing) are independent dispatcher-internal mechanism choices. The ADR-0052 bundling rationale (engine capabilities constrain history-impl viability) does not apply: neither D1 nor D2 constrains the other. Split keeps amendment chains focused (a future flip of audit-log timing doesn't muddy the isolation-primitive surface, and vice versa).
  - *`pg_advisory_xact_lock` (blocking variant) instead of the `_try_` variant.* Rejected — ADR-0052 specified `_try_` deliberately. Fast-fail prevents indefinite blocking on a hung transaction elsewhere; gives the dispatcher a clean signal to convert into a domain-meaningful retry response; avoids the wasted-work failure mode where a transaction does work before discovering it should have waited.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Default primitive pinned.** Every cross-entity invariant declaration includes its isolation primitive; absent an explicit advisory-lock declaration, SERIALIZABLE is the default. Single-entity well-formedness invariants are revalidated within the command's main transaction isolation level (SERIALIZABLE per ADR-0052's default).
  - **Two-prong opt-in test documented.** When M1+ implementation lands a new cross-entity invariant, the implementer applies: (a) is the read footprint wide enough to make SERIALIZABLE false-positives frequent under realistic load? AND (b) can the invariant's scope be named as a small set of stable lock keys? Both must hold to opt in. No ADR amendment is required for per-invariant criterion-applications — recorded in code comments referencing this ADR.
  - **Closure-readiness lock semantics.** Every dispatcher invocation that mutates a closure-readiness-relevant entity tries `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock(closure_readiness_key(project_id))` in the invariant step; `close_project` tries the same lock. On lock-acquisition failure (`false`), the dispatcher returns a domain-level retry signal (e.g., "another operation on this project is in progress; please retry") *before doing any work*. Two projects' commands run in parallel; same-project closure-readiness-relevant commands serialize.
  - **EmployeeRole serialization semantics.** `create_employee_role` / `edit_employee_role` / `change_employee_role_rate` (per ADR-0045) revalidate the disjoint-ranges invariant under SERIALIZABLE. On `serialization_failure` (rare in practice), the dispatcher returns a retry signal; the caller (typically the admin UI) re-submits.
  - **Closure-readiness-relevant entity set is enumerated.** Time Entry, Sample Batch, Document, RFA, DepFiling, RFP. New entities introduced in M1–M7 whose state participates in any blocker-registry predicate inherit the closure-readiness lock requirement; update the enumerated set as the registry expands (carry-forward below).
  - **Engine-portability discipline (ADR-0051 + ADR-0052 restated).** Both primitives are Postgres-specific; they sit behind the documented adapter boundary landing in M0.4 / Step 1.4. The SQLite offline-fallback path uses degraded equivalents (no advisory lock — SQLite's serial-write model approximates; default isolation in place of SERIALIZABLE). Not production-equivalent; explicit in adapter docs.
  - **Portability check (per ADR-0055).** `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` and `SERIALIZABLE` are both core Postgres 15+ — universally available across the realistic vendor shortlist. No vendor flag.
  - **Reversibility cost is low.** A wrong per-invariant primitive call is fixed by amending the invariant's declaration + redeploying — no schema migration, no data backfill, no downtime. A wrong criterion (D1.a) is more expensive: every prior per-invariant assignment under the old criterion would be re-reviewed.
  - **Out of scope for this ADR.** Exact lock-key hash function and namespacing (collision risk with future advisory-lock uses), dispatcher invariant-step pseudocode, per-entity invariant declaration syntax — all land in M0.3 / Step 1.3.
- **Amendments to other ADRs:**
  - **ADR-0052 § Cross-entity invariant isolation.** The deferred carry-forward *"Exact per-invariant choice is implementation-phase; the ADR pins the available primitives, not the per-invariant assignments"* is partially resolved here: the criterion is pinned (D1.a); two worked-example assignments are pinned (D1.b, D1.c). Remaining per-invariant choices for invariants landing in M1–M7 are criterion-applications, not ADR-worthy. ADR-0052's primitive-availability commitment (`SERIALIZABLE` default + `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` opt-in) is unchanged.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Per-invariant primitive choice at M1+ landings.** When a new cross-entity invariant lands in M1–M7, the implementer applies D1.a's two-prong criterion and records the per-invariant choice in code (no ADR amendment required for criterion-application). If a chosen primitive proves wrong, flip the declaration + redeploy — no schema migration. Document the flip in the relevant PR.
  - **Lock-key computation and namespacing.** Hash function, key prefix discipline (closure-readiness keys must not collide with future advisory-lock uses). Lands in M0.3 / Step 1.3 (dispatcher implementation).
  - **Closure-readiness-relevant entity set evolution.** Update the enumerated set above as M1–M7 introduces entities whose state participates in blocker-registry predicates.

---

## ADR-0057 — Audit-log write timing: in-txn with the entity mutation

- **Date:** 2026-05-18
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** Resolves the audit-log-write-timing half of ADR-0052's deferred implementation-phase carry-forwards (the per-invariant isolation-primitive half resolves in ADR-0056). The `command_audit_log` row for the 7 audit-log entities (Employee, User, Time Entry, Contractor, DepFiling, Contract, WABundle, per ADR-0052) is written **in-txn** with the entity mutation — same SQLAlchemy session, same transaction boundary. Both commit or neither does. The dispatcher writes the audit row inside the same transaction it commits the mutation in; no outbox table, no async queue, no fire-and-forget machinery in M0.3. The audit row's existence is structurally coupled to the mutation's: *"audit row exists iff mutation did."* Amends ADR-0052 § Audit-log table by resolving its timing carry-forward.
- **Context:** Step 1.2 / M0.2 (Phase 2). ADR-0013 permits async / best-effort audit-log writes at the pattern level; ADR-0052 explicitly allowed in-txn as *"stronger than the pattern promises"* and deferred the timing call to implementation phase. Both options are defensible — the question is which default we want at M0 (strong invariant or async-permissive) given (a) no current perf signal forcing a trade-off, and (b) the project's accountability-first framing (cf. ADR-0008's stance on history capture being inescapable from the call site — *"capture must be inescapable from the call site, or the declaration is meaningless"*). Session 29 split the M0.2 ADR write (Q1 — see ADR-0056 § Alternatives) so this timing decision lands as a focused amendment-friendly anchor independent of isolation-primitive amendments.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Post-commit (fire-and-forget).* Commit the entity mutation, then write the audit row in a separate transaction without retry / dead-letter. Rejected — process crash between commit and audit-write produces a permanent audit gap with no recovery path. Audit log becomes best-effort with no machinery to make the "best-effort" claim true. The user-visible latency win is hypothetical (no perf signal forcing it); the accountability loss is structural.
  - *Post-commit via outbox.* Commit the entity mutation and an outbox row in the same txn; a separate sweeper drains the outbox into `command_audit_log` asynchronously. Preserves the "no lost rows" guarantee while removing audit-write contention from the user-visible response. Rejected at M0 — adds real machinery (outbox table, sweeper process, retry/backoff, monitoring) for a perf concern we have no signal we need. Re-addable later: outbox is an additive migration (existing audit rows stay valid; new writes flow through the outbox); cost recoverable when actually needed.
  - *In-txn with handler escape hatch.* Allow the dispatcher to skip the audit-log write for designated "lightweight" commands. Rejected — same structural failure ADR-0008 rejected for history capture. If audit is escapable from the call site, the declaration is meaningless. The 7 audit-log entities are the ones for which audit *is* the accountability primary; an escape hatch defeats the purpose.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Atomicity guarantee.** For the 7 audit-log entities, the `command_audit_log` row is written in the same SQLAlchemy session as the entity mutation. The dispatcher's audit-emit step runs before `commit()`; if either the mutation or the audit-write fails, the transaction rolls back as a whole. No partial state, no orphan audit rows, no missing audit rows.
  - **"Audit row exists iff mutation did" invariant.** Compliance / forensic / audit-UI readers can treat `command_audit_log` as authoritative: every committed mutation on an audit-log entity has a row; no committed mutation lacks one.
  - **Latency cost.** Each command on an audit-log entity pays the audit-write's latency on the user-visible response path (~few ms for a single-row insert under normal load). At MVP scale (office-internal, low concurrency, single-region), this is well below user-perceptible thresholds; not a hot path.
  - **No new machinery in M0.3.** The dispatcher writes the audit row inline; no outbox table, no sweeper, no retry/backoff loop, no dead-letter queue. The `command_audit_log` schema (per ADR-0052 § Audit-log table) is unchanged.
  - **Failure mode for the audit-write itself.** If a `command_audit_log` insert fails (DB connection drop, schema mismatch, disk pressure), the whole command fails; the user retries; the audit log stays consistent with committed state. This is the desired failure mode — better than silently losing the audit signal.
  - **Reversibility cost is low but asymmetric.** Switching in-txn → post-commit (or outbox) is a dispatcher code change + redeploy; no schema migration. Historical audit rows written under in-txn stay reliable across the switch. But audit rows that *would have been written* under in-txn but were lost under a later post-commit era cannot be recovered. The asymmetry favors starting in-txn: the recovery surface is preserved.
  - **Engine-portability discipline (ADR-0051 + ADR-0052 restated).** No Postgres-specific surface here — in-txn writes work identically across the realistic vendor shortlist. The SQLite offline-fallback path runs the same in-txn pattern (different isolation guarantees per ADR-0056, same atomicity).
  - **Portability check (per ADR-0055).** No vendor-specific machinery; no flag.
- **Amendments to other ADRs:**
  - **ADR-0052 § Audit-log table.** The deferred *"Timing (in-txn vs. post-commit) deferred to implementation phase — ADR-0013 permits async / best-effort; in-txn is allowed and stronger than the pattern promises"* is resolved here in favor of in-txn. ADR-0013's pattern-level permission for async / best-effort is unchanged; this ADR exercises ADR-0052's "stronger than the pattern promises" allowance for `command_audit_log` specifically.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Perf revisit trigger.** If M5+ perf testing reveals `command_audit_log` write contention on hot-path audit-log entities (Time Entry is the highest-volume candidate), revisit by amending this ADR. Likely shape: outbox pattern for the specific contended entity, not a global flip. Triggering signal: measurable user-visible latency degradation traced to audit-write contention. No work to do now.

---

## ADR-0059 — `Command` base class shape: plain class + nested Pydantic Payload + explicit registry

- **Date:** 2026-05-18
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** Every state-changing operation in `sca-tracker` is a `Command` subclass authored as a plain Python class (ABC) with pipeline metadata as class-level attributes (`target_entity`, `transition_name`, `authorization`, `invariants`, `cascade`, `destructive`, `cascade_allowed_destructive`), a nested `Payload` Pydantic model declaring the command's input schema, and a `handler(self, session, payload) -> entity` method implementing the apply step per ADR-0011's binary-outcome contract. Commands register into an explicit module-level dict via `register(MyCommand)` -- typically at module-import time alongside the class definition -- producing a name-keyed lookup; collision on name with a different class raises. The pattern is uniform across the four-kind taxonomy: a non-lifecycle command sets `transition_name = None`; a non-history-carrying entity's command has no invariants on it that produce history; cascade declarations enumerate sub-commands the handler invokes (cascade-invoke machinery lands in ADR-0060). Resolves ADR-0051's *"`Command` base class + dispatcher concrete design"* carry-forward (the dispatcher itself lands in ADR-0058).
- **Context:** Step 1.3a / M0.3 (Phase 2). ADR-0051 pinned the runtime stack (Python 3.12+ / FastAPI / Pydantic / SQLAlchemy 2.0) and carried the `Command` base class + dispatcher concrete design to the implementation phase, naming `logic.md`'s pipeline order (auth → lifecycle → apply → invariants → history → commit) as the spec. ADR-0052 added per-entity history tables + the `command_audit_log` shared table; ADR-0057 pinned in-txn audit-emit timing; ADR-0056 pinned per-invariant isolation primitives. With the data-layer surface settled, Step 1.3a needs to pick the shape M1+ developers author every command in -- a load-bearing ergonomics + safety call. Three forks were canvassed in Session 30's Round A: Pydantic-model-as-command; plain class + nested Pydantic Payload + explicit registry (this ADR); function + decorator.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Pydantic-model-as-command (command IS its payload schema).* Rejected -- mixes value-shaped concerns (payload validation) with behavior-shaped concerns (pipeline orchestration) on one class. Pydantic's own guidance is that models stay value-shaped; subclassing with abstract methods + non-field class attrs requires `ClassVar[...]` discipline on every metadata attr (forget one → silent schema corruption); inheritance for shared metadata across related commands fights Pydantic's field-inheritance behavior. Pydantic-validation rejection becomes a parallel rejection path to dispatcher rejection -- ADR-0011's "single rejection surface" framing weakens. The footgun compounds over project lifetime.
  - *Function + declarative decorator (`@command(target=..., transition=..., invariants=[...])`).* Rejected -- decorator metadata is harder to introspect than class attrs (no methods, no inheritance, no overrides); cascade orchestration (compound commands per design pattern #5) without class shape gets awkward (sub-command invocation needs a stable handle); decorator-driven registration leaks across tests unless explicit reset machinery is added; mirrors the FastAPI route style optimally only for the bread-and-butter case where the function body IS the command, which is exactly the case commands diverge from (auth + lifecycle + invariants + history are pipeline concerns, not handler concerns). FastAPI-style fit isn't worth the lost introspection / inheritance / cascade ergonomics.
  - *Implicit subclass discovery (walk all `Command.__subclasses__()` at startup).* Rejected -- magical; slow tests (subclass walk hits unrelated test fixtures); registration becomes coupled to import order; "what commands exist?" requires runtime introspection rather than greppable enumeration.
  - *Decorator-driven registration on top of class-based commands (`@register` on each Command class).* Considered as a hybrid -- A2.b's class shape + a registration decorator. Rejected for 1.3a -- adds import-time side effects (a decorator that mutates a module-level dict during import); explicit `register(MyCommand)` is one extra line below the class definition, fully greppable. Cost is small enough that the import-time-cleanliness win pays.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Authored shape (M1+).** Each command lives in a module under `app/domain/commands/` (or per-cluster equivalent) as `class FooCommand(Command): target_entity = Foo; transition_name = "x" | None; authorization = pred; invariants = [...]; cascade = [...]; class Payload(BaseModel): ...; def handler(self, session, payload) -> Foo: ...`. The Payload class typically lives one screen above the handler -- two declarations, both in one module.
  - **Registration site.** Each command module ends with `register(FooCommand)`. A bootstrap module (`app.domain.commands.__init__` or equivalent) imports every command module at app startup to drive registration; routes / tests look up commands by name via `get_command("FooCommand")` when name-based dispatch is needed (e.g., from an audit-log replay path), and by class reference for direct invocation.
  - **Pipeline integration.** The dispatcher (ADR-0058) reads `target_entity`, `transition_name`, `authorization`, `invariants`, `cascade` off the class; instantiates the command (passing the validated Payload); calls `handler(session, payload)` for the apply step; revalidates `invariants` after handler; constructs the appropriate `HistoryRecord` variant (capture-sink interface; see commit history) for the history step. No handler-level escape hatch for any pipeline step per ADR-0008 + ADR-0011.
  - **Caller object.** A `Caller` Protocol declares the minimum surface the authorization predicate consumes (an `id`). M1+ extends the Caller shape as auth predicates from ADR-0047 land -- role attrs, relationship lookups, etc. The Protocol-shape preserves duck-typing freedom; the dispatcher does not own a concrete `Caller` class.
  - **Invariant object.** Invariants declare `primitive` (`"serializable"` default; `"advisory_lock"` opt-in per ADR-0056) and `check(session, target) -> bool`; advisory-lock invariants override `lock_key(target) -> str` returning a namespaced lock key (`app.framework.locks.LockNamespace`). The dispatcher's invariant step acquires advisory locks before re-checking the invariant.
  - **Pydantic validation rejection sits BEFORE the dispatcher.** A malformed payload raises `pydantic.ValidationError` at `Payload(...)` construction, not in the dispatcher. The route layer (the natural call site) translates Pydantic validation errors to HTTP 422 directly; the dispatcher's `CommandRejected` family covers auth / lifecycle / invariant rejection per ADR-0011. Two rejection paths, separated by phase -- input validation outside the pipeline, semantic rejection inside.
  - **Cascade declaration surface (final form lands in ADR-0060).** Commands enumerate sub-commands they invoke via `cascade = [SubCommand1, SubCommand2]`. The cascade-invoke entry point + the registry-load-time destructive-cannot-cascade guard + the drift test land in ADR-0060; this ADR pins the declaration shape and the destructive flag.
  - **Discoverability.** "What commands exist?" → grep `register(` across `app/domain/commands/` (or `registered_commands()` at runtime). "Who can run command X?" → read `X.authorization` (a callable; long-form ADR-0047 predicates land at the call site for M1+). "What does command X mutate?" → `X.target_entity` and `X.handler` source. All structurally legible.
  - **Test ergonomics.** The dispatcher takes the session_factory and capture sink as constructor args (no module-level singletons); tests construct `Dispatcher(session_factory=test_factory, sink=InMemorySink())` per fixture. `_clear_registry_for_tests()` exists for tests that build isolated command sets; production never uses it.
  - **Migration cost of changing minds later.** Switching to A2.a (Pydantic-as-command) post-MVP would touch every command file (move payload fields onto the Command class; convert metadata to `ClassVar`); a half-day per cluster. Switching to A2.c (decorator) similarly requires a touch on every command. Cost is recoverable but real -- not free. The decision pins now in exchange for the assurance of an authoring shape that scales to the ~70-100 commands the MVP-plus-near-term-cluster will need.
- **Amendments to other ADRs:**
  - **ADR-0051 § Carry-forwards.** Resolves the *"`Command` base class + dispatcher design"* implementation-phase carry-forward (the dispatcher itself lands in ADR-0058 alongside this ADR). ADR-0051's runtime-stack envelope is unchanged.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Cascade-invoke machinery + safeguards.** Cascade-invoke entry point, registry-load-time destructive-cannot-cascade check, drift test scaffolding. Lands in ADR-0060 (this session).
  - **`Caller` concrete shape.** ADR-0047 predicates consume role / relationship attrs; M1+ extends the Caller surface (Pydantic model or session-derived dataclass; TBD at first auth-predicate landing).
  - **Command-discovery bootstrap.** An `app.domain.commands.__init__` (or equivalent) imports every command module at startup to drive registration. Concrete bootstrap lands when the first real command lands in M1.

---

## ADR-0060 — Cascade auth-inheritance mechanism: context flag + runtime guard + registry-load-time destructive check + AST drift inspector

- **Date:** 2026-05-18
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** Compound commands (per `domain-model.md` § Design patterns #5) cascade-invoke their sub-commands via a dispatcher entry point `cascade_invoke(parent_command, child_command_cls, child_payload, session)`. The entry point runs the child's pipeline **with the authorization step skipped** -- per ADR-0047's policy that cascade effects inherit auth from the originating user-facing command. Three structural safeguards constrain the mechanism: **(G1) Runtime guard.** `cascade_invoke` rejects with `CascadeViolation` if `child_command_cls` does not appear in `parent_command.cascade`. The wrong invocation is impossible at runtime, not just discouraged by review. **(G2) Registry-load-time check.** `validate_registry()` walks every registered command; for each parent whose `cascade = [...]` contains a child with `destructive = True`, the parent must declare `cascade_allowed_destructive = True`. Otherwise raises `DestructiveCascadeViolation` at app startup (before any request runs). **(G3) Static drift inspector.** `extract_handler_cascade_invocations()` AST-parses each handler and extracts the Command class names passed to `cascade_invoke(...)` calls; `cascade_drift_report()` compares declared vs. invoked per command. The safety-critical invariant -- "invoked but not declared" -- is empty by construction of G1 (G3 catches it earlier at test time without requiring the path to execute); the cleanliness signal -- "declared but not invoked" -- surfaces stale declarations. Pinned mechanism + guards resolve Round B's cascade question (Session 30, Step 1.3a) and supplement ADR-0047's policy with its implementation envelope.
- **Context:** ADR-0047 settled cascade *policy*: cascade effects inherit auth from the initiating user-facing command, and the audit story credits the human who fired the top-level command (per `command_audit_log.command_name = <user-facing command>`, with per-sub-command history rows sharing `command_id`). Mechanism was not pinned -- ADR-0047 explicitly enumerated user-facing commands only and deferred how the framework enforces inheritance to the implementation phase. Step 1.3a needs to pick mechanism + guards before the dispatcher's invariant-step retry loop (ADR-0058) wires the call surface. Three mechanism candidates and three guard variants were canvassed in Session 30's Round B (B1); the user's safety question ("how much risk am I accepting?") forced explicit articulation of the failure modes and the guards each candidate would need to be safe.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Mechanism: re-evaluate auth with an always-true-for-cascade predicate.* Rejected -- relocates the auth bypass without removing it; the always-true predicate IS the bypass; auditability story is identical to the skip-auth mechanism but the predicate-evaluation machinery runs uselessly on every cascade child. No structural advantage.
  - *Mechanism: token-based delegation (parent mints a signed token; sub-commands verify the token as proof of authorization).* Rejected -- adds machinery (token format, signing key management, expiry semantics, replay-protection) for a flexibility we have no evidence we need at MVP scale. The dominant failure mode (mis-declared cascade) is unchanged by tokens: a developer who can declare `cascade = [...]` can also mint tokens. The cryptographic complexity buys against threats outside the trust boundary; cascade safety is an inside-the-trust-boundary concern, so the threat model doesn't match.
  - *Guard: no registry-load-time check; rely on PR review.* Rejected -- the catastrophe mode (destructive sub-command added to a cascade list by autocomplete or copy-paste) requires three things to fail: (a) the bad declaration lands, (b) PR review misses it, (c) no test catches it. Without G2, the only barrier is review -- one failure point. G2 makes the failure require an explicit `cascade_allowed_destructive = True` override, which surfaces in PR diff as an obvious flag.
  - *Guard: per-child allowlist (`cascade_allowed_from = [ParentCommand1, ParentCommand2]` on each child).* Rejected for 1.3a, preserved as a deferred carry-forward. The allowlist gives the child the choice of who may invoke it (compared with G2's parent-side declaration); meaningfully tighter for post-MVP at large command surface (~200+) where any child might be added to any cascade. At MVP scale (~70-100 commands by M7), G1 + G2 + G3 cover the failure modes; the allowlist's extra ceremony pays back only when the cascade declaration surface grows past what PR review can audit reliably. Reconsider if cascade declaration surface gets ungovernable.
  - *Guard: runtime tracking only (instrument `cascade_invoke` to record actual invocations; tests compare to declared after the suite runs).* Rejected as the primary drift mechanism -- runtime tracking only catches drift the tests actually exercise; a never-tested cascade branch goes undetected. AST-based G3 catches drift without requiring execution, which is the right shape for a safety invariant. Runtime tracking remains useful as a complementary signal (and is trivially addable later by wrapping `cascade_invoke`); for 1.3a it is not the primary safeguard.
  - *Drop G3 entirely (rely on G1's runtime guard alone for drift detection).* Considered -- G1 makes the safety-critical case ("invoked but not declared") impossible at runtime, so G3 buys nothing structurally for safety. Kept anyway: G3 catches drift at *test* time without requiring the path to execute, which means a never-tested cascade branch with a bad declaration still surfaces in CI; cheap to maintain (~30 lines of AST walk); cleanliness signal ("declared but not invoked") is useful for keeping declarations honest as the cascade surface grows.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Handler authoring shape.** Compound-command handlers call `cascade_invoke(self, ChildCommand, child_payload, session)` (positional args). The child runs auth-bypassed; lifecycle / apply / invariants / history / commit-step-participation all run normally. Sub-commands do not commit -- the parent's commit covers them (transactional atomicity per ADR-0008 + ADR-0011).
  - **Audit story.** `command_audit_log.command_name` records the parent's name; per-sub-command history rows on history-carrying entities share the parent's `command_id` per ADR-0052's common-metadata pattern -- the cascade lineage is queryable forensically (`WHERE command_id = ?` returns the full set of rows the cascade produced).
  - **Failure-mode coverage.** Three independent failures must compound to land a destructive cascade in production: (a) developer declares `destructive = False` on a destructive command OR adds `cascade_allowed_destructive = True` to the parent, AND (b) PR review misses both, AND (c) the G3 drift test passes (which means the handler actually does fire it -- intentional override, not accident). Each failure visible in PR diff. Materially better than mechanism-#2 or mechanism-#3 without guards.
  - **`destructive` declaration.** Commands whose effect is destructive (irrecoverable mutation, mass deletion, etc.) set `destructive = True` on the Command class. Default False per ADR-0059. M1+ adds entries to this surface as destructive commands land (Note: most MVP commands are not destructive -- creation / mutation / lifecycle-state-flips are recoverable via history; the destructive set is bounded to entity deletes per the delete policy in `domain-model.md` and irreversible cascades).
  - **`cascade_allowed_destructive` override.** Parents that legitimately invoke a destructive sub-command (rare in MVP; `cancel_project`'s cascade is the most likely candidate per the project-cancel semantics in ADR-0037) set `cascade_allowed_destructive = True`. This is an explicit, reviewable knob -- every appearance in the codebase is a signal worth examining at review time.
  - **G1's runtime cost.** One `in` check per cascade-invoke (~ns). Negligible. Provides the hard safety guarantee.
  - **G2's startup cost.** One iteration over the registry + per-parent iteration over its cascade list at app boot. Linear, runs once. Provides the loud-failure-before-traffic guarantee.
  - **G3's test-time cost.** One AST parse per handler at test time. Linear in command count. The drift report is a dict; pytest fixtures can assert `invoked_not_declared == set()` for all commands (the safety check) and warn (not fail) on `declared_not_invoked` (the cleanliness signal). Limitation: dynamic dispatch -- `cascade_invoke(self, some_var, ...)` where `some_var` is a Command class chosen at runtime -- is invisible to AST extraction. Acceptable for MVP; revisit if dynamic-cascade patterns emerge.
  - **Cascade-invoke entry point location.** The function lives in `app.framework.dispatcher` because it consumes dispatcher internals (session, pipeline-step machinery). Handlers import it explicitly -- there is no method-on-Command-base sugaring (which would require dispatcher state on every Command instance, a poor coupling shape). Explicit imports keep "where does cascade orchestration come from?" greppable.
  - **Sub-command transaction participation.** Cascade children run inside the parent's transaction. They do not call `session.commit()` (the parent's commit covers them); they may rollback (raising any `CommandRejected` subclass propagates up, rolls back the whole transaction including the parent's mutation). This matches ADR-0011: rejection at any pipeline step in any participant produces no mutation and no history row anywhere in the cascade.
  - **Lock acquisition under cascade.** If a sub-command's invariant requires an advisory lock per ADR-0056 (e.g., a closure-readiness-touching cascade child), the lock acquisition happens in the sub-command's invariant step.
