The parent's transaction is the lock holder; transaction-scoped lock release at parent commit/rollback applies. No special cascade-aware lock machinery.
- **Amendments to other ADRs:**
  - **ADR-0047.** Provides the implementation mechanism for ADR-0047's cascade policy. ADR-0047's policy text (cascade inherits auth from originating user-facing command; the table enumerates user-facing commands only) is unchanged. This ADR adds: cascade enforcement happens via `cascade_invoke()` with G1 / G2 / G3 safeguards.
  - **ADR-0059.** Confirms the cascade / destructive / cascade_allowed_destructive class attrs declared on the Command base class are load-bearing -- G2 consumes them at registry validation. ADR-0059 already pinned the declaration shape.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Per-child cascade allowlist.** If post-MVP cascade declaration surface grows past what PR review can audit reliably (rough threshold: ~200+ commands or ~30+ cascade-parent commands), revisit by amending this ADR to add `cascade_allowed_from = [Parent1, Parent2]` on each child as a complementary guard. No work to do now.
  - **Runtime cascade-invocation tracking.** Trivially addable by wrapping `cascade_invoke` to record (parent_cls, child_cls) pairs in a thread-local set. Useful for production observability (audit which cascades fire under load) if a need surfaces. No work to do now.
  - **Dynamic-cascade patterns.** If M1+ commands legitimately need to choose a sub-command class at runtime (currently no anticipated case), the G3 AST inspector becomes blind; revisit by either widening the AST extraction (track dynamic dispatch sources) or supplementing with the runtime tracker above.

---

## ADR-0058 — Dispatcher contention-retry boundary: dispatcher-owned loop with small fixed budget

- **Date:** 2026-05-18
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** The command dispatcher owns the retry loop for both contention modes produced by the invariant step under ADR-0056: `pg_try_advisory_xact_lock` returning False (pre-work fast-fail signal, surfaced as the internal `AdvisoryLockUnavailable`) and Postgres `serialization_failure` (SQLSTATE 40001, post-work commit failure under SERIALIZABLE isolation, surfaced via SQLAlchemy's `OperationalError`). The loop wraps the full `_run_pipeline` invocation, retrying the whole pipeline (auth → lifecycle → apply → invariants → history → commit) on either signal, up to **MAX_ATTEMPTS = 3** total attempts with exponential-jittered backoff (base 20ms; ~100ms total budget). On exhaustion, the dispatcher surfaces a typed `TransientContention` exception carrying the attempt count and the last underlying cause; route layers translate to HTTP 409 / 503 and the user retries the request. Auth / lifecycle / invariant rejections (`CommandRejected` subclasses) are caller-visible domain errors and **propagate unwrapped** -- the retry loop does not catch them. Every retry logs a WARN-level line naming the command and attempt number so hidden retries cannot mask broken predicates. Per-transaction SERIALIZABLE isolation is set at the dispatcher level (`connection.execution_options(isolation_level="SERIALIZABLE")` once per attempt's session-open), not at the engine level -- reads / scripts / health checks going through the same engine inherit default isolation per ADR-0010's write-path-only scope.
- **Context:** Step 1.3a / M0.3 (Phase 2). ADR-0051 + ADR-0052 carry-forwarded the `Command` base class + dispatcher concrete design to the implementation phase. ADR-0056 pinned the invariant-step primitives (SERIALIZABLE default + advisory-lock opt-in with `_try_` variant for fast-fail signaling) but left retry handling open: *"the dispatcher returns a domain-level retry signal"* without specifying where retry policy lives. Three forks were canvassed in Session 30's Round A (A1): dispatcher built-in retry loop (this ADR); pure pass-through with the route layer wrapping; hybrid (inline-retry advisory-lock-fail, bubble serialization_failure). The user's framing -- "how is this decision reflected in the final project?" -- grounded the canvass: it is application-layer Python code in the dispatcher module, not Neon configuration and not SQLAlchemy engine config; the choice is "where does the retry loop live in the codebase," not "which tool's config knob to set." The user followed with concern about WET code if two dispatch surfaces emerged for serializable vs. non-serializable commands; the canvass clarified that all commands are write-path per ADR-0010 and run under SERIALIZABLE uniformly -- the per-command differentiation exists at the invariant-primitive level (advisory-lock opt-in per ADR-0056), not at the dispatch-function level.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Pure pass-through; route layer wraps.* Rejected -- dispatcher single-attempt and deterministic, every caller must remember to wrap with a retry decorator. Easy to forget on a new route / transport surface (CLI, future async job runner); retry policy either duplicates across decorators or hides in one shared decorator that everyone must remember to apply. The cleaner separation is theoretical: in practice both modes converge on "user resubmits after a brief domain error" once the budget is small (3 attempts, ~100ms total), so the cost of letting transport pick its own budget buys nothing concrete. The "different transports want different policies" argument is speculative at MVP scale -- no async job runner is on the roadmap.
  - *Hybrid: inline-retry advisory-lock-fail (pre-work, cheap), bubble serialization_failure (post-work, expensive).* Rejected -- theoretically clean (matches cost shape: cheap retries land where they cost nothing; expensive retries become explicit caller decisions) but with a 3-attempt / 100ms total budget the asymmetry adds cognitive cost for marginal benefit. Both modes converge on the same user-visible outcome. Cleaner-on-paper not cleaner-in-practice at this budget.
  - *Larger retry budget (5+ attempts, longer backoff).* Rejected -- hidden retries with a large budget mask broken predicates. A real bug (predicate consistently fails for non-contention reasons) appears flaky rather than failing loudly. Small budget + per-retry WARN log + loud failure-after-exhaustion is the right shape: real contention recovers in 1-2 retries; real bugs surface after 3 attempts with logs to triage from.
  - *Retry budget as a Pydantic-settings env var (`MAX_RETRIES=3`).* Considered as a future tunable. Rejected for 1.3a -- premature configurability; "production needs a different budget than dev" is unsubstantiated; if a real tuning need emerges, promoting the constant to settings is a 5-line change. Hardcoded constants in the dispatcher module are reviewable, greppable, and inspectable from any test.
  - *Engine-level SERIALIZABLE (`create_engine(..., isolation_level="SERIALIZABLE")`).* Rejected -- over-applies the strongest isolation to operations ADR-0010 explicitly scopes outside the write path (reads, health checks, ad-hoc scripts going through the same engine). Dispatcher-level placement matches the ADR-0056 rationale exactly: SERIALIZABLE on every command, default elsewhere. Cost: two lines in the dispatcher vs. zero for engine-level. Trivial.
  - *Session-factory-level SERIALIZABLE.* Considered -- middle ground (every standard session inherits SERIALIZABLE; scripts that build their own session skip it). Rejected -- still over-applies vs. dispatcher-level; the dispatcher is the only write path per ADR-0051 + ADR-0052 + ADR-0059, so anyone going through `SessionFactory()` for non-dispatch work doesn't need the SERIALIZABLE tax. Per-transaction placement is the precise scope.
  - *Two dispatch entry points: `dispatch()` (default isolation) vs. `dispatch_serializable()` (SERIALIZABLE).* Rejected per Session 30 Round A WET-code clarification -- there is no "non-serializable command" category; every command is write-path per ADR-0010 and runs under SERIALIZABLE uniformly. The per-command differentiation the WET concern was reaching for already exists at the invariant-primitive level (ADR-0056 advisory-lock opt-in declared on the invariant attached to the command), where it is declaratively legible by reading the command's `invariants = [...]` class attr. Two dispatch functions would create a false distinction.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Retry loop location.** `app/framework/dispatcher.py`, in `Dispatcher.dispatch()`. One module, ~20 lines for the loop body; greppable as "the retry loop." Constants (`MAX_ATTEMPTS = 3`, `BACKOFF_BASE_MS = 20`) live at module scope.
  - **TransientContention exception.** Subclass of bare `Exception` (NOT `CommandRejected` -- transient contention is not a domain-rejection; it is a temporary system condition). Carries `attempts` (int) and `last_cause` (BaseException). Routes catch it at the HTTP layer; the user-facing message is generic ("the system is busy; please retry"); the underlying cause is logged but not echoed.
  - **AdvisoryLockUnavailable exception.** Internal signal raised by the invariant step's lock acquisition (`try_advisory_xact_lock` returned False). Caught by the dispatcher's retry loop only; never surfaced to callers directly. If a non-dispatcher caller raises it, the test should catch the leak.
  - **CommandRejected family unaffected.** Auth / lifecycle / invariant rejections propagate from the pipeline straight past the retry loop. Per ADR-0011, these are caller-visible domain errors with reasons; retrying them is wrong (the rejection is deterministic given the inputs, not transient).
  - **SerializationFailure detection.** Wrapped by SQLAlchemy as `OperationalError`; the underlying psycopg exception carries `sqlstate == "40001"`. The dispatcher's `_is_serialization_failure` helper unwraps and checks; non-Postgres dialects (SQLite offline-fallback) cannot raise `40001` so the check returns False -- offline-fallback retries do nothing because there is no contention to retry. Honest behavior given the ADR-0052 + ADR-0056 statement that the SQLite path is degraded-but-buildable, not production-equivalent.
  - **WARN logging on every retry.** `logger.warning("advisory-lock contention on attempt %d/%d for %s; retrying", ...)` and the serialization_failure analog. Hidden retries cannot hide bugs -- a command that consistently retries surfaces in the log signal even when it eventually succeeds.
  - **Backoff shape.** Exponential with full jitter (`random.uniform(0, BACKOFF_BASE_MS * 2^(attempt-1))`). Total worst-case budget: 20ms + 40ms = 60ms wait between 3 attempts. Below user-perceptible thresholds at MVP scale.
  - **Per-transaction SERIALIZABLE.** Inside `_run_pipeline`, after opening the session and before the pipeline runs: `session.connection().execution_options(isolation_level="SERIALIZABLE")`. Dialect-aware (skipped on non-Postgres). Matches ADR-0056 D1.a default exactly.
  - **Cascade interaction.** Cascade children share the parent's session + transaction (per ADR-0060); they do NOT open their own session and do NOT re-set isolation level. The whole parent-plus-cascade atomic unit retries together if the parent's commit hits serialization_failure -- this is the desired ADR-0011 atomicity behavior for compound commands.
  - **Test ergonomics.** Tests can verify retry behavior by injecting a `session_factory` whose first N sessions raise `OperationalError(sqlstate=40001)` and the N+1th succeeds. The constants are module-level so tests can monkeypatch `MAX_ATTEMPTS` / `BACKOFF_BASE_MS` for fast determinism (1 attempt + 0ms backoff for a "no retry" path).
- **Amendments to other ADRs:**
  - **ADR-0051 § Carry-forwards.** Resolves the dispatcher half of the *"`Command` base class + dispatcher design"* carry-forward (the Command base half resolves in ADR-0059). ADR-0051's runtime-stack envelope is unchanged.
  - **ADR-0056 § Consequences (closure-readiness lock semantics).** ADR-0056 said *"the dispatcher returns a domain-level retry signal ... before doing any work."* This ADR fills the gap: the signal is `AdvisoryLockUnavailable` caught by the dispatcher's own retry loop; only after MAX_ATTEMPTS does the loop surface `TransientContention` to the caller. The "before doing any work" framing is preserved -- the retry happens because no work was done (the lock acquisition is the first step of the invariant block).
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Per-environment retry budget tuning.** If production perf signals show 3 attempts is too few (or too many) under realistic load, promote MAX_ATTEMPTS / BACKOFF_BASE_MS to Pydantic settings env vars. No work to do now; the change is ~5 lines.
  - **Per-command retry budget overrides.** Some commands may eventually deserve different budgets (e.g., bulk-import commands tolerating more retries than interactive commands). If that surfaces, add an optional `max_attempts` class attr to Command with module-level default fallback. No work to do now; speculative.
  - **Metrics surface.** When observability lands (post-MVP), retry attempts should emit a metric (`dispatcher_retry_count{command_name=...,mode=...}`) so contention hotspots are visible at aggregate level. The WARN logs are the 1.3a substitute.

---

## ADR-0061 — Auth substrate: DB-backed sessions, argon2id hashing, bootstrap CLI, CORS, login-as-non-Command-surface

- **Date:** 2026-05-19
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** M1.1 lands the authentication substrate as six coupled choices, bundled here because they are deliberated as a single "how do users prove identity" surface. **(1) Session mechanism.** DB-backed server-side sessions. Opaque random token (`secrets.token_urlsafe(32)` — 256 bits) stored as the `session` row's primary key; the token doubles as the cookie value. Cookie attrs: `HttpOnly`, `Secure` (settings-toggled off in tests + local plain-HTTP dev), `SameSite=Lax`, 12h `Max-Age`. Sliding TTL: every successful `current_user` dep call refreshes `last_seen_at` and pushes `expires_at` forward. Revoke = `DELETE` on the row. **(2) Password hashing.** `argon2-cffi`'s `PasswordHasher` with OWASP 2024 parameters pinned explicitly (`time_cost=2`, `memory_cost=19456 KiB`, `parallelism=1`, `hash_len=32`, `salt_len=16`). Pinned rather than library-default so hashes from any machine stay verifiable across `argon2-cffi` version bumps. **(3) Bootstrap.** `app/cli/bootstrap_admin.py` — stdlib `input()` + `getpass.getpass()`, prompts for username + password (confirmed twice), creates a User row + UserRole(superadmin) grant; idempotent on username collision (exits non-zero, no overwrite). Click adoption deferred per the `app/cli/` convention (third command earns Click). **(4) CORS.** `fastapi.middleware.cors.CORSMiddleware(allow_origins=[settings.frontend_origin], allow_credentials=True, allow_methods=["*"], allow_headers=["*"])`. `allow_credentials=True` is load-bearing — without it the browser drops the session cookie cross-origin even with the origin header set. **(5) CSRF tokens.** Deferred. `SameSite=Lax` cookies cover the practical CSRF surface at single-deployment MVP scale per OWASP CSRF cheat sheet's same-site-cookies path. Revisit if a cross-site embed or POST-from-third-party-origin scenario arises post-MVP. **(6) Login as non-Command surface.** Login does not run through the `Dispatcher` (which requires a `Caller`; login is the surface that produces one). Implemented as a FastAPI route directly at `POST /auth/login`. Logout (`POST /auth/logout`) and `/auth/me` (`GET /auth/me`) likewise — they are substrate, not domain state changes. **One documented exception** to the "every state-change is a Command" rule (ADR-0051 + ADR-0059); the carve-out is bounded to these three routes.
- **Context:** Step 2.1 / M1.1 (Phase 2). Authentication was flagged as `architecture.md` line 108's *"pinned at implementation kickoff"* out-of-band concern but never milestoned in `roadmap.md`; the M1 admin-dashboard skeleton forced the question. Session 34's Case 2 sizing pulled auth into M1.1 (caught via the [[check-out-of-band-concerns]] discipline). The 8 *what*-level decisions were chat-side canvassed at Session 34; this ADR records the 6 here, ADR-0062 records Caller concrete shape (decision 7), and ADR-0063 records the frontend route-guard pattern (decision 8). At session head, six *how*-level details were canvassed and pinned: session token shape (`secrets.token_urlsafe(32)`), argon2 parameter pinning (explicit OWASP 2024), `Caller` module location (new `app.framework.caller`), `app.framework.auth` partitioning (single module), TanStack Router file-based `_authenticated` group, pytest fixture shape (dependency-override). The "non-Command login" exception is documented here because every M1+ developer will look for the rule that says "every state change is a Command"; the exception is small (3 routes), bounded (auth substrate only), and load-bearing (the alternative — a chicken-and-egg "Caller-less" pseudo-Command path through the dispatcher — would muddy the core abstraction for one use case).
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *JWT (stateless) sessions instead of DB-backed.* Rejected — revocation requires a denylist (which is a DB-backed session lookup by another name) or accepting that revoke-on-`revoke_user_role` is impossible until token expiry. DB-backed gives O(1) revoke; the per-request DB lookup is cheap (token is the PK).
  - *bcrypt instead of argon2id.* Rejected — argon2id is the OWASP 2024 first recommendation, resists GPU/ASIC attacks via memory-hardness in a way bcrypt's pure-CPU cost factor does not. No deployment-target constraint pushed the other way.
  - *Library-default argon2 parameters (no explicit pinning).* Rejected — `argon2-cffi`'s defaults have changed across releases; relying on them means a future version bump could leave existing hashes unverifiable. Explicit pinning costs ~5 lines and removes the upgrade risk entirely.
  - *Click-based bootstrap CLI from the start.* Rejected per the `app/cli/` convention pinned in Session 34's pre-M1.1 cleanup commit — Click adoption waits until the third CLI command lands. Stdlib `input()` + `getpass` is ~30 lines for the single-command case.
  - *Multi-origin CORS allowlist.* Rejected — MVP is single-deployment; one `frontend_origin` setting is the minimum that works and the maximum that's needed. Loosening to a list is a one-line change if/when a second origin appears.
  - *CSRF tokens at MVP.* Rejected per Session 34 canvass — `SameSite=Lax` blocks the cross-site form-POST attack vector that double-submit-token defends against; the residual surface (subdomain confusion, target=_top navigations to authenticated GETs that mutate state) does not apply at the MVP threat surface. Revisit when a cross-site embed or third-party form-POST scenario arises.
  - *Login goes through the Command pipeline with a `SystemCaller` placeholder.* Rejected — introduces a system-caller primitive that ADR-0047 locked clarification 3 explicitly excluded; muddies the "every Command runs on behalf of a human" audit story. The non-Command exception is bounded (3 auth routes) and named; the alternative would leak system-caller plumbing across the dispatcher surface for one use case.
  - *Per-device logout from the start (revoke single session row, not all of user's).* Decision-level coincidence — the implementation already does this. Both `POST /auth/logout` and the cookie-clear flow target the cookie's token row, not all of `user.sessions`. The future multi-device-management UI surfaces this without re-architecting.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Wire format.** `POST /auth/login` body `{username: string, password: string}` → on success, `Set-Cookie: session=<token>; HttpOnly; Secure; SameSite=Lax; Max-Age=43200; Path=/` + response body `Caller{id, username, roles}`. On failure, `401` + body `{"detail": "invalid credentials"}` — identical shape for unknown-user vs bad-password, defensive against enumeration. `POST /auth/logout` reads the cookie, deletes the session row (idempotent if absent), clears the cookie, returns `204`. `GET /auth/me` returns the current `Caller` or `401`.
  - **`session` table.** `id: text` (the token, PK), `user_id: uuid` (FK→user.id, ON DELETE CASCADE), `created_at: timestamptz`, `expires_at: timestamptz`, `last_seen_at: timestamptz`. Indexes on `user_id` and `expires_at`. Migrated in `25ea83fcec61_auth_substrate`.
  - **`user` table.** `id: uuid` (PK), `username: text` (UNIQUE), `password_hash: text`, `employee_id: uuid?` (no FK at M1.1 — Employee table lands in M1.2 and that migration adds the FK + UNIQUE constraint), `soft_deleted_at: timestamptz?`. The `User → Employee` 0..1 link per ADR-0041 Gap 5 stays nullable to accommodate superadmin / auditor users with no employee row.
  - **`user_role` table.** Composite key `(user_id, role)` per ADR-0036, with `granted_at` and `granted_by` audit columns. Role-grant commands (`grant_user_role`, `revoke_user_role`) land in M1.3; M1.1 seeds rows directly via `bootstrap_admin`.
  - **`current_user` FastAPI dependency.** Reads the session cookie (alias `session`), looks up the row (rejecting if missing or `expires_at <= now()`), loads the user (rejecting if missing or soft-deleted), refreshes `last_seen_at` + `expires_at`, builds the `Caller` (id, username, roles read from `user_role`), commits, returns. Raises `HTTPException(401)` on any miss. Single seam at which "the HTTP request" becomes "the actor" for downstream command dispatch.
  - **Bootstrap CLI invocation.** `uv run python -m app.cli.bootstrap_admin`. Reads `DATABASE_URL` from `.env` (per [[project-neon-current-policy]] this is the live Neon DB; in CI / local-SQLite contexts it's the offline-fallback). Idempotent: existing username → exit(2) with friendly message + no mutation.
  - **Settings additions.** `frontend_origin: str = "http://localhost:5173"`, `session_cookie_name: str = "session"`, `session_ttl_hours: int = 12`, `cookie_secure: bool = True`. The `cookie_secure` default of `True` is correct for any deployed environment; tests force it `False` (TestClient runs on http://testserver and httpx refuses to round-trip a Secure cookie over plain HTTP); local plain-HTTP dev sets it via `.env`.
  - **SQLite tz-portability shim.** `app.framework.auth._ensure_utc(dt)` coerces naive datetimes (which SQLite produces on roundtrip from `DateTime(timezone=True)`) to UTC at the comparison boundary. Postgres preserves the tz so the shim is a no-op in production. Localized to `lookup_session`; consider promoting to a framework-level helper when a second consumer surfaces.
  - **CORS + cookie interaction.** `allow_credentials=True` + a concrete origin (not `*`) is the only combination that lets the browser send the cookie cross-origin. Listed for forensic value: the next-most-common bug shape at this seam is "I added `*` to allow_origins and now the cookie disappears" — `*` and `allow_credentials=True` are mutually exclusive per the CORS spec.
  - **Login surface is the ONE non-Command exception.** The carve-out is bounded to `/auth/login`, `/auth/logout`, `/auth/me`. Any future non-Command route surface requires an ADR justifying why the alternative (Command + cascade or Command + bootstrap-Caller pattern) doesn't apply. The Command pipeline remains the rule.
- **Amendments to other ADRs:**
  - **ADR-0051 § runtime stack.** Adds `argon2-cffi>=25.1.0` to the backend dependency set. No envelope change.
  - **ADR-0059 § "Caller concrete shape" carry-forward.** Resolved by ADR-0062 (this session). The Caller Protocol stub in `app.framework.command` is removed; `app.framework.caller.Caller` is the concrete shape.
  - **`architecture.md` § Out-of-band concerns.** "Auth" was flagged but never milestoned; this ADR + its session lands the answer. Strike "Auth" from out-of-band; file under "M1.1, ADR-0061" if a future scan needs the lineage.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Password reset.** Not in MVP per `mvp.md`. Admin uses `edit_user` (M1.2) to set a new password for a user who has forgotten theirs. A self-serve reset (email-driven) is post-MVP; needs email infrastructure (also out-of-band per `architecture.md`).
  - **Rate limiting / lockout on login.** Not in MVP. At single-deployment small-firm scale the attack surface is bounded; revisit if a deployment surfaces it.
  - **Remember-me / persistent sessions beyond 12h sliding TTL.** Not in MVP. The 12h sliding TTL is opinionated; if office workflow forces re-login mid-day too often, raise the constant (~1 line). A "remember me" checkbox that issues a 30-day cookie is a post-MVP product call.
  - **2FA / MFA / OAuth / SSO.** Not in MVP. Argon2id-on-DB-backed-sessions has the right shape to accept TOTP as a second factor later (add a column on `user` for the secret; gate `create_session` on TOTP verification).
  - **Immediate session invalidation on `revoke_user_role`.** Per `mvp.md` line 73, next-request authorization check is MVP behavior — when a role is revoked, the user keeps their current session but loses authorization at the next dispatched command. Immediate invalidation requires either deleting the session row at revoke time (easy) or pushing a revoke signal to active websockets (harder; no websockets yet). Land at the same time as the security-immediate-revoke surface from ADR-0040's carry-forward.
  - **CSRF tokens.** Not in MVP per decision 5. The double-submit-token shape is well-understood; revisit when a cross-site scenario surfaces.

---

## ADR-0062 — `Caller` concrete shape: Pydantic frozen model in `app.framework.caller` with `Role(StrEnum)` and `has_role_at_least` helper

- **Date:** 2026-05-19
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** The `Caller` consumed by the dispatcher (per ADR-0059's pipeline) and by ADR-0047's authorization predicates is a concrete Pydantic frozen model: `Caller(id: UUID, username: str, roles: frozenset[Role])`, where `Role` is a `StrEnum` enumerating ADR-0040's four roles (`superadmin`, `admin`, `coordinator`, `auditor`). Lives in a new module `app.framework.caller` next to `command.py` and `dispatcher.py`. The `Caller` Protocol stub previously in `app.framework.command` is removed; `command.py` re-imports the concrete `Caller` for the pipeline's typing. A module-level helper `has_role_at_least(caller, minimum)` encodes ADR-0040's linear-hierarchy chain (`auditor < coordinator < admin < superadmin`) — class-rule predicates ("role >= coordinator") call it; per-target-role predicates (`grant_user_role` per ADR-0047 non-uniform row) inline their own logic against `caller.roles`. Resolves ADR-0059's *"Caller concrete shape"* carry-forward.
- **Context:** ADR-0059 pinned the `Command` base class but deferred Caller's concrete shape: *"M1+ extends the Caller surface (Pydantic model or session-derived dataclass; TBD at first auth-predicate landing)."* M1.1 forces the question — `current_user` (ADR-0061) needs to return *something*, and the dispatcher's typing was carrying a Protocol-shaped placeholder. Three forks were considered at session head: (a) Pydantic model (this ADR); (b) frozen dataclass; (c) SQLAlchemy-mapped detached User. The Pydantic pick aligns with the rest of the request-layer (Payload models are Pydantic; the auth route's response model is `Caller` — round-tripping through Pydantic preserves type consistency). The module-location fork (`app.framework.caller` vs. inline in `app.framework.command`) was an explicit session-head canvass; new module won per the legibility argument — actor concept is distinct from command pipeline shape and earns its own seam.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Frozen dataclass.* Rejected — Pydantic is in the stack regardless (every Command's Payload is Pydantic); using dataclass here just to avoid one Pydantic import creates a heterogeneous "what shape is request data?" story. Pydantic also serializes cleanly to the `/auth/me` response without an adapter.
  - *SQLAlchemy-mapped detached User row passed directly.* Rejected — couples the dispatcher to a SQLAlchemy detached-instance contract (refreshing relationships hits the DB; checking `.roles` requires either a relationship traversal or an extra query). The Pydantic shape pre-loads roles at construction time so predicates evaluate without DB access — important for the dispatcher's auth step that runs before any handler query.
  - *Keep `Caller` as a Protocol; let each call site define its own concrete shape.* Rejected — the Protocol approach was M0's expedient ("any object with `.id` works"); M1+ predicates need `.roles` and any future predicates may need more attributes. A single concrete model centralizes the shape contract and eliminates the "which Caller-like object am I holding?" question that Protocols introduce.
  - *`Caller` inline in `app.framework.command` (no new module).* Rejected at session head — actor concept is semantically distinct from command pipeline shape; co-locating them invites future drift where command.py grows actor-related concerns it shouldn't own. The new-module cost is one import; the legibility win is structural.
  - *`Role` as plain `Enum` (not `StrEnum`).* Rejected — Pydantic + JSON serialization of `Enum` produces `"Role.ADMIN"` style strings unless overridden; `StrEnum` serializes as the value ("admin") natively. The wire shape and the DB-stored shape align without coercion code.
  - *`role: list[Role]` instead of `frozenset[Role]`.* Rejected — set semantics are correct (a user has roles, order doesn't matter, dedup is silent); frozen prevents accidental mutation post-construction. The wire form serializes to a JSON array; openapi-ts maps it to `Role[]` on the TypeScript side without issue.
  - *`has_role_at_least` as a method on `Caller`.* Rejected — method-on-data-object pulls authorization logic into the data shape; the helper-function form keeps `Caller` purely value-shaped and the chain semantics auditable in one place (the `_CHAIN_ORDER` tuple). Future non-chain predicates inline their own logic against `caller.roles` without inheriting a method that wouldn't apply.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Module shape.** `app/framework/caller.py` exports: `Role` (StrEnum with `SUPERADMIN/ADMIN/COORDINATOR/AUDITOR`), `Caller` (Pydantic frozen `BaseModel`), and `has_role_at_least(caller, minimum) -> bool`. The `_CHAIN_ORDER` tuple is module-private; future non-chain roles (per ADR-0040's "freeze" property) add a column to ADR-0047's predicate table without changing `_CHAIN_ORDER`.
  - **Dispatcher integration.** `app.framework.command.py` removes the `Caller` Protocol; imports `Caller` from `app.framework.caller`. `app.framework.dispatcher.py` likewise imports the concrete type. No call-site changes — the dispatcher only reads `.id` for history records today; M1.2+ predicates read `.roles` via the same `Caller` instance.
  - **Test ergonomics.** `tests/conftest.py` provides per-role fixtures (`as_superadmin`, `as_admin`, `as_coordinator`, `as_auditor`) that override `app.framework.auth.current_user` with a synthetic `Caller`. M1.2+ command/route tests use these to assert ADR-0047 predicates without round-tripping a real login. Previous smoke-test `FakeCaller` dataclass is removed; tests construct `Caller(id=..., username=..., roles=frozenset())` directly.
  - **`auth_predicate` signature.** Per ADR-0059's pinned shape: `(caller: Caller, command_cls: type[Command], payload: BaseModel, session: Session) -> bool`. With `Caller` concrete, M1.2+'s first ADR-0047 predicate authoring lands without a Protocol-to-concrete migration step.
  - **`audit_log_record.caller_id`.** Type stays `UUID` (per ADR-0052 common-metadata pattern). The `Caller` model surfaces `caller.id: UUID` directly; no adapter needed.
- **Amendments to other ADRs:**
  - **ADR-0059 § Carry-forwards.** *"Caller concrete shape"* — resolved.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Caller surface extensions for non-uniform predicates.** Some ADR-0047 predicates may need relationship lookups (e.g., "is this caller the creator of this note?" for `edit_note`'s creator-only rule). Two options: (a) extend `Caller` with relationship attributes (becomes heavyweight); (b) keep `Caller` minimal and let predicates query the DB via the session arg (the chosen direction in ADR-0059's predicate signature). Option (b) is the default; revisit only if a predicate's lookup is hot-pathed enough to push toward (a).

---

## ADR-0063 — Frontend auth-route guard: TanStack Router file-based `_authenticated` + `useCurrentUser` query + login `setQueryData` (not `invalidateQueries`)

- **Date:** 2026-05-19
- **Status:** accepted
- **Decision:** Frontend route protection uses TanStack Router's file-based `_authenticated.tsx` layout group at `frontend/src/routes/_authenticated.tsx` + `_authenticated/index.tsx` (and future children). The layout's `beforeLoad` reads the current-user TanStack Query via `context.queryClient.ensureQueryData(currentUserQueryOptions())`; on miss (null), throws `redirect({ to: '/login' })`. The router context carries the `QueryClient` (declared via `createRootRouteWithContext<{queryClient: QueryClient}>`); `main.tsx` passes it in at router construction. `useCurrentUser()` (a thin `useQuery` wrapper over `meAuthMeGet()`) is the canonical hook; its `queryFn` catches 401 and returns `null` rather than throwing, with `retry: false` (401 is the logged-out steady state, not a transient failure). **Critical: login mutation primes the cache via `queryClient.setQueryData(currentUserQueryKey, response.data)` before navigating; it does NOT use `invalidateQueries`.** Justified below.
- **Context:** M1.1 Step 2.1 plan listed this ADR as conditional on "non-obvious tradeoffs." Three non-obvious things surfaced in implementation and earn the write: (a) TanStack Router's `ensureQueryData` returns cached data even when stale (only fetches on missing data) — different from `useQuery` which respects `staleTime`; (b) `invalidateQueries` with default `refetchType: 'active'` only refetches queries with a mounted subscriber, which the `/login` page does not have for the user query; (c) the file-based `_authenticated` layout group with `beforeLoad` is the cleanest TanStack Router idiom for whole-subtree auth gating, but requires `createRootRouteWithContext` for typed access to the `QueryClient`. Item (b) bit during the browser flow verification — the original implementation used `invalidateQueries` in login's `onSuccess`, which marked the cache stale but did not refetch (no active subscriber); navigation then read the stale-null cached value and bounced back to `/login`. Switching to `setQueryData` with the Caller already in the login response eliminates the issue and saves a round-trip.
- **Alternatives considered:**
  - *Programmatic guards in each route's `loader` (no layout group).* Rejected — duplicates the `ensureQueryData` + redirect logic per route. The file-based layout group is the canonical TanStack Router idiom for "this subtree requires X"; matching the idiom keeps M1.2+ admin pages free of auth boilerplate.
  - *Server-side route protection (FastAPI returns 401 for unauthenticated requests to admin pages).* Not applicable — frontend is a SPA served by Vite; routing happens client-side. The 401 surface is per-API-call (which the backend already enforces via `current_user`); browser navigation does not consult the backend.
  - *401 response interceptor in the API client that redirects to `/login`.* Rejected — risks recursive 401 → `/auth/me` → 401 loops if not carefully gated; obscures the auth contract (redirect logic in two places); doesn't compose well with TanStack Query's caching (`useQuery`'s error state is the right surface for the hook's consumers). The `_authenticated.beforeLoad` is the single canonical redirect path; navigation interactions catch session expiry on the next route transition.
  - *`invalidateQueries` in login's `onSuccess` (the original implementation).* Rejected after browser flow verification surfaced the redirect-loop bug. The `setQueryData` path is strictly better: cache reflects truth immediately, no round-trip, no race between invalidation and navigation. Rule for future auth-state mutations: if the mutation response already contains the new state, prefer `setQueryData`; reserve `invalidateQueries` for cases where the response doesn't carry the new value.
  - *`refetchQueries` instead of `setQueryData`.* Considered as a compromise (forces a refetch but spends a round-trip). Rejected — `setQueryData` is cheaper and the source of truth is identical (login response IS the Caller). `refetchQueries` becomes the right tool when a mutation invalidates state that isn't returned (e.g., a future "edit profile" that changes adjacent data).
  - *Storing the Caller in `localStorage` or a Zustand store instead of TanStack Query.* Rejected — duplicates the source of truth (DOM state vs. server state) and requires manual sync invalidation on session expiry. TanStack Query is already the request-cache abstraction; `useCurrentUser` is a thin wrapper over it. Single store, single invalidation path.
- **Consequences:**
  - **Route topology.** `frontend/src/routes/login.tsx` (the one route outside the `_authenticated` group). `frontend/src/routes/_authenticated.tsx` (the layout). `frontend/src/routes/_authenticated/index.tsx` (the admin shell at `/`). M1.2+ admin pages land under `_authenticated/<page>.tsx`; no per-page auth wiring needed.
  - **`useCurrentUser` hook + queryOptions.** `frontend/src/hooks/useCurrentUser.ts` exports `currentUserQueryKey`, `currentUserQueryOptions()`, and `useCurrentUser()`. The `queryOptions` form is consumed by `_authenticated.beforeLoad`'s `ensureQueryData` (which needs `queryKey` + `queryFn` outside React); the hook form is consumed by components. Both share the same `queryFn` to keep caching consistent. `staleTime: 60_000` keeps the user payload fresh long enough for snappy navigation without serving stale role data after a role change (acceptable per `mvp.md` line 73's next-request authorization check).
  - **Login mutation pattern.** On success: `queryClient.setQueryData(currentUserQueryKey, data)`, then `navigate({ to: '/' })`. No `invalidateQueries`. Documented in the route's source-level comment because the rationale is non-obvious to a reader who hasn't hit the bug.
  - **Logout mutation pattern.** `onSettled`: `invalidateQueries(currentUserQueryKey)` (which DOES refetch — the admin shell subscribes to `useCurrentUser`, so `refetchType: 'active'` fires), then `navigate({ to: '/login' })`. The refetch sees a 401 from the now-revoked session and writes `null` into the cache; navigation lands at `/login`.
  - **Cookie configuration.** `app/api/configure.ts` calls `client.setConfig({ baseUrl, credentials: 'include' })` at app startup. `credentials: 'include'` is the fetch-API attribute that opts into sending cross-origin cookies — load-bearing for the cookie's round-trip given the backend lives at a different port (or, in production, a different subdomain).
  - **Root route context typing.** `__root.tsx` uses `createRootRouteWithContext<{ queryClient: QueryClient }>()` so `beforeLoad` reads `context.queryClient` with proper typing. M1.2+ layouts inherit the same context type — extending the context (e.g., adding telemetry handles) is a single-location amendment.
  - **No 401 API interceptor.** Documented above; future devs reaching for an interceptor should read this ADR first. The recursion risk + competing-source-of-truth risk are both real.
- **Carry-forwards:**
  - **Per-role admin sub-routing (M1.2+).** When the admin shell adds per-entity pages (Employee, School, Contractor, User, Contract), the nav links land in `_authenticated/index.tsx`'s header. Role-based hiding (auditors don't see edit links) reads `useCurrentUser()` and conditionally renders. If the admin shell needs a per-role layout (auditor read-only mode), nest layouts: `_authenticated/_admin.tsx` for the admin-or-higher subtree.
  - **Session-expiry UX during long sessions.** Mid-session expiry currently surfaces as a 401 on the next API call → component error → next navigation triggers `_authenticated.beforeLoad` → redirect to login. Acceptable for MVP. A post-MVP "session expired — please log in again" toast would intercept the 401 in a mutation `onError` and trigger logout + navigate.
  - **Pre-fetch user data on login route mount.** Not done in M1.1 — the `/login` route does not subscribe to `useCurrentUser`, so the user query is cold until the first `_authenticated` route is visited. If browser flow latency becomes user-perceptible, prefetch in `/login`'s loader (`queryClient.prefetchQuery(currentUserQueryOptions())`). Not worth the complexity at MVP scale.

---
